# Audit Report — DittoFS  (audit/develop-scan @ `2beda0f2`, 2026-06-03)

**Stack:** Go 1.25 · Cobra · chi · GORM · BadgerDB v4 · PostgreSQL (pgx v5) · SQLite · AWS SDK v2 S3 · gokrb5 · BLAKE3 · LZ4 · FastCDC · OpenTelemetry · Prometheus · controller-runtime
**Depth:** quick (3 lenses: bugs/security/slop) · **Findings:** 98 HIGH / 89 MED / 46 LOW (233 total) · adversarially verified

> Salvaged from run `wf_163abb3f-e15` (report-writer stalled before emitting). All findings survived adversarial verification. Quick-depth run — `structure`/`perf`/`bloat`/`comments`/`gaps` lenses NOT run.

## Findings


## HIGH

### [HIGH] Data race: DOC propagation writes OpenFile.DeletePending without lock · `bugs` · area: smb-create-open
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/close.go:396`
- **What:** In the DOC propagation block, `other.DeletePending = true`, `other.DeleteOnCloseParentKey`, and `other.HasDeleteOnCloseParentKey` are written directly to sibling `*OpenFile` structs inside a `sync.Map Range` callback without holding `other.mu`. Concurrent goroutines (e.g. a parallel `Create` calling `isFileDeletePending`) read `existing.DeletePending` at handler.go:1909 also without `mu`.
- **Why it matters:** Go's race detector will flag this as a data race. A concurrent `Create` on another goroutine can read a partially-written `DeletePending` (torn bool) or observe stale zero while the CLOSE goroutine is mid-write, causing a new open to succeed when it should return `STATUS_DELETE_PENDING`, or vice versa. The `mu` comment on `OpenFile` says it guards mutable fields but the DOC propagation block never acquires it.
- **Fix:** Acquire `other.mu.Lock()` before writing `other.DeletePending`, `other.DeleteOnCloseParentKey`, `other.HasDeleteOnCloseParentKey` and release after. Mirror the pattern already used for `SmbWriteTriggered` in the same file (line 565). Similarly protect reads in `isFileDeletePending`.
- **Verified:** close.go:396 writes other.DeletePending/other.DeleteOnCloseParentKey/other.HasDeleteOnCloseParentKey inside sync.Map Range callback with no other.mu.Lock(). handler.go:1909 reads existing.DeletePending in isFileDeletePending also without lock. Real data race.

### [HIGH] Data race: BaseFileDeletePending propagation writes without lock · `bugs` · area: smb-create-open
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/close.go:412`
- **What:** `other.BaseFileDeletePending`, `other.BaseFileDeleteParentHandle`, `other.BaseFileDeleteFileName`, `other.DeleteOnCloseParentKey`, and `other.HasDeleteOnCloseParentKey` are written to stream-handle `*OpenFile` structs inside `rangeStreamsOfBase` without `other.mu`. The same fields are read in `isFileOrBaseDeletePending` (handler.go:1949) also without a lock.
- **Why it matters:** Same race class as the previous finding. A concurrent `Create` opening a stream while the base file's CLOSE is propagating `BaseFileDeletePending` can observe torn state and miss the `STATUS_DELETE_PENDING` gate, opening a stream whose base is in the process of being deleted.
- **Fix:** Acquire `other.mu.Lock()` around the write block in `rangeStreamsOfBase` callback; similarly hold `existing.mu.RLock()` when reading `existing.BaseFileDeletePending` in `isFileOrBaseDeletePending`.
- **Verified:** close.go:412-416 writes other.BaseFileDeletePending/BaseFileDeleteParentHandle/BaseFileDeleteFileName/DeleteOnCloseParentKey/HasDeleteOnCloseParentKey inside rangeStreamsOfBase callback with no other.mu.Lock(). handler.go:1949 reads existing.BaseFileDeletePending without lock. Same race class as idx 0.

### [HIGH] Data race: Session identity fields mutated without lock during re-auth · `bugs` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/session_setup.go:1729`
- **What:** tryReauthUpdate writes sess.Username/Domain/User/IsGuest/IsNull (plain struct fields, no mutex) while concurrent goroutines dispatching pipelined requests on the same session read those fields via primeAuthContext/BuildAuthContext without any lock. Same race in reauthKerberosSession (kerberos_auth.go:195-200) for sess.User/Username/Domain/IsGuest/IsNull/ExpiresAt.
- **Why it matters:** Session struct comment says 'Identity fields (read-only after creation)' but re-auth violates the invariant. go -race detects this: the dispatch goroutine reads sess.User (auth_helper.go:223) concurrently with the SESSION_SETUP goroutine writing it. A torn read of the User pointer can cause a nil-deref or wrong-identity in permission checks on in-flight handles.
- **Fix:** Add a sync.RWMutex (identityMu) to Session. Write-lock it in tryReauthUpdate and reauthKerberosSession around the identity field assignments. Read-lock it in GetSession callers that read identity fields (primeAuthContext, BuildAuthContext, CaptureOpenerIdentity, IsExpired). Alternatively use atomic.Pointer[models.User] for the User field and atomic stores for the string/bool fields, but a single RWMutex covering all five fields is cleaner.
- **Verified:** session_setup.go:1729-1733 writes sess.Username/Domain/User/IsGuest/IsNull directly. Session.mu (line 161 in session.go) only guards credit mutations per comment. Identity fields comment says 'read-only after creation' but re-auth violates this. Concurrent dispatch reads these fields without any lock.

### [HIGH] Auth bypass: user with no NT hash gets authenticated non-guest session without credential check · `bugs` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/session_setup.go:1241`
- **What:** When UserStore.GetUser succeeds and user.Enabled is true but hasNTHash is false (line 1086), execution falls to the 'no NT hash' block at line 1218. CreateSessionWithUser is called (line 1241) and buildAuthenticatedResponse is returned with nil exportedSessionKey. No NTLMv2 challenge-response is ever validated. Any client that knows a valid username but presents any (including garbage) NtChallengeResponse is authenticated as that user.
- **Why it matters:** The NTLM TYPE_3 parse at line 1032 extracts the username. GetUser at line 1083 succeeds. hasNTHash (line 1086) is false so the ValidateNTLMv2Response block is skipped entirely. The session is created as ctx.IsGuest=false with the target user's identity. This is an explicit auth bypass, acknowledged in the comment ('any client knowing the username can authenticate'). Session signing is also absent (nil key), so subsequent signed requests silently pass without verification.
- **Fix:** Reject authentication when hasNTHash is false: return NewErrorResult(types.StatusLogonFailure) instead of creating a session. Operators must set NT hashes before users can authenticate. If a transitional grace period is needed, gate it behind an explicit insecure-auth config flag (default false) and log at Error, not Warn.
- **Verified:** session_setup.go:1218-1241: when hasNTHash=false, NTLMv2 validation block skipped entirely. CreateSessionWithUser called with nil exported session key (no signing). Comment at line 1220 explicitly acknowledges: 'any client knowing the username can authenticate'. Real auth bypass.

### [HIGH] flushWatcher races on re-arm: timer from old watcher prematurely flushes new watcher · `bugs` · area: smb-lease-oplock-notify
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/change_notify.go:1181`
- **What:** `bufferEventLocked` captures `fileID` by value in the `time.AfterFunc` closure; `flushWatcher` then looks up `r.byFileID[fileID]` to get the notify instance. When `Register` replaces an existing watcher (same FileID, line 589-590) and calls `r.unregisterLocked(old)` which calls `old.flushTimer.Stop()`, `Stop()` returns false if the timer already fired (goroutine blocked on `r.mu`). After lock is released, the stale timer goroutine wakes, finds the NEW watcher under `fileID`, drains its (possibly empty) buffer and calls `r.unregisterLocked` on it — permanently evicting the freshly-registered watcher before any real event is delivered.
- **Why it matters:** One-shot watcher is destroyed before the client receives any notification. The client never sees STATUS_PENDING turn into a notification response; from the client's perspective the CHANGE_NOTIFY silently vanishes. Reproducible in any scenario where a re-arm races with the 100µs flush timer firing (e.g. smbtorture smb2.notify.mask, cancel+re-register flows).
- **Fix:** Store the notify pointer itself in the timer closure instead of just fileID, then in `flushWatcher` compare `byFileID[fileID] == notifyPtr` before draining. Alternatively, use a per-watcher generation counter: increment on every `Register`, capture in the closure, and bail in the callback when the stored generation doesn't match.
- **Verified:** change_notify.go:1170 captures fileID by value in AfterFunc closure. Register (line 589) calls unregisterLocked(old) which calls old.flushTimer.Stop() — if timer already fired and goroutine is blocked on r.mu, Stop() returns false. After r.mu released, stale goroutine calls flushWatcher(fileID), finds NEW watcher under same fileID in r.byFileID, drains it and unregisters it.

### [HIGH] COPYCHUNK access check uses DesiredAccess (pre-DACL) instead of GrantedAccess · `bugs` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/ioctl_copychunk.go:250`
- **What:** `validateCopyChunkAccess` reads `src.DesiredAccess` and `dst.DesiredAccess` (the requested, pre-DACL mask) to gate COPYCHUNK source read and destination write access.
- **Why it matters:** Every other access gate in the codebase (read.go hasReadAccess, write.go hasWriteAccess, set_info.go, query_info.go, ioctl_sparse.go, ioctl_fsctl.go) explicitly consults `GrantedAccess` (post-DACL intersection at CREATE). The gap is documented in the codebase as bug class B (#619): a MAXIMUM_ALLOWED open whose DACL stripped FILE_READ_DATA still has it in DesiredAccess, so the check passes when it should deny. An unprivileged user can abuse COPYCHUNK to read or write a file their DACL forbids.
- **Fix:** In `validateCopyChunkAccess`, change `srcAccess := types.AccessMask(src.DesiredAccess)` → `srcAccess := types.AccessMask(src.GrantedAccess)` and `dstAccess := types.AccessMask(dst.DesiredAccess)` → `dstAccess := types.AccessMask(dst.GrantedAccess)`. Update the log format strings from `src.DesiredAccess`/`dst.DesiredAccess` to `src.GrantedAccess`/`dst.GrantedAccess` accordingly.
- **Verified:** ioctl_copychunk.go:250-251: validateCopyChunkAccess reads src.DesiredAccess and dst.DesiredAccess. All other access gates in the codebase use GrantedAccess. DesiredAccess is the pre-DACL requested mask; GrantedAccess is the post-DACL effective mask set at CREATE time.

### [HIGH] Compound NextCommand < HeaderSize causes panic in ParseCompoundCommand · `bugs` · area: smb-framing-dispatch-compound
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/compound.go:553`
- **What:** ParseCompoundCommand validates NextCommand is 8-byte aligned (line 541) but never checks NextCommand >= header.HeaderSize (64). A value like 8, 16, 24, 32, 40, 48, or 56 passes the alignment guard and reaches `body = data[header.HeaderSize:bodyEnd]` where bodyEnd = NextCommand < 64, producing `data[64:N]` with N < 64 — index out of range panic.
- **Why it matters:** Any unauthenticated client can send a compound request with NextCommand = 8 (non-zero, 8-byte aligned, passes every existing check). The panic propagates to handleRequestPanic recover(), killing only that connection goroutine. Repeated across new connections = per-connection DoS from unauthenticated peers.
- **Fix:** Add `if hdr.NextCommand > 0 && hdr.NextCommand < uint32(header.HeaderSize) { return nil, nil, nil, fmt.Errorf("compound NextCommand too small: %d", hdr.NextCommand) }` after the alignment check at line 541.
- **Verified:** compound.go:541-553: only checks 8-byte alignment (NextCommand%8!=0), no check for NextCommand>=HeaderSize(64). Values like 8,16..56 pass. Then bodyEnd=NextCommand<64, body=data[64:bodyEnd] where bodyEnd<64 — index out of range panic.

### [HIGH] Compound NextCommand < HeaderSize causes panic in splitCompoundBody · `bugs` · area: smb-framing-dispatch-compound
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/framing.go:306`
- **What:** splitCompoundBody processes the FIRST command of a compound (called from parseSMB2Message in the connection read loop). bodyEnd = min(int(hdr.NextCommand), len(message)). When NextCommand is e.g. 56 and message length >= 56, bodyEnd = 56 and `message[header.HeaderSize:bodyEnd]` = `message[64:56]` — index out of range panic. Same class as the ParseCompoundCommand bug; the framing path has no prior NextCommand < HeaderSize guard either.
- **Why it matters:** parseSMB2Message is invoked in the Serve read loop before any goroutine spawn. The panic propagates to the deferred handleConnectionClose recover(), terminating the connection goroutine. However, unlike the compound.go path, this fires on the FIRST compound command before any authentication handshake completes — any client connecting on port 12049 can trigger it.
- **Fix:** In splitCompoundBody, guard before slicing: `if hdr.NextCommand > 0 && int(hdr.NextCommand) < header.HeaderSize { body = nil; remaining = nil; return }` — or return an error sentinel and let parseSMB2Message surface it. Alternatively add the same check in parseSMB2Message before calling splitCompoundBody: if hdr.NextCommand > 0 && hdr.NextCommand < uint32(header.HeaderSize), return STATUS_INVALID_PARAMETER.
- **Verified:** framing.go:303-306: splitCompoundBody has bodyEnd=min(int(hdr.NextCommand),len(message)). With NextCommand=56 and len(message)>=56, bodyEnd=56, body=message[64:56] — panic. No NextCommand>=HeaderSize guard. Fires before any auth on the connection read loop.

### [HIGH] LockNew: orphaned lock-owner + lock-state on seqid error · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:1761`
- **What:** In LockNew, new lockOwner inserted into sm.lockOwners (line 1761) and new lockState inserted into openState.LockStates + sm.lockStateByOther (lines 1788-1789) BEFORE seqid validation at lines 1794-1817. On ErrBadSeqid return both objects stay in maps permanently.
- **Why it matters:** Orphaned lock-owner + lock-state persist until lease expiry. Subsequent LockNew from same (clientID, ownerData) finds ownerExists=true; subsequent CLOSE fails NFS4ERR_LOCKS_HELD on phantom lock, blocking file close. Client is wedged until lease expires.
- **Fix:** Move seqid validation (step 6) BEFORE state creation (steps 4-5). Only allocate lockOwner/lockState after confirming the seqid is a valid new request — mirror Linux nfsd nfsd4_lock which validates seqids before allocating state.
- **Verified:** manager.go LockNew: lockOwner inserted at line 1761, lockState inserted at lines 1788-1789, THEN seqid validation at lines 1794-1817. ErrBadSeqid return leaves both objects in sm.lockOwners and sm.lockStateByOther permanently until lease expiry.

### [HIGH] freeLockStateidLocked: unconditionally deletes lock-owner when freeing one stateid · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/stateid.go:392`
- **What:** freeLockStateidLocked deletes the lock-owner from sm.lockOwners (line 392) when freeing a single lock stateid, even when the owner has sibling lock states on other open files still live in sm.lockStateByOther.
- **Why it matters:** Sibling LockState objects in sm.lockStateByOther still hold a *LockOwner pointer. After the delete, the owner is absent from sm.lockOwners so ReleaseLockOwner becomes a no-op for that owner, and onLeaseExpired / EvictV40Client skip its cleanup path, leaking the sibling lock states and the underlying byte-range locks in the LockManager forever.
- **Fix:** Before deleting from sm.lockOwners, verify no other LockState in sm.lockStateByOther still references this owner. Only delete when reference count drops to zero — same approach ReleaseLockOwner already uses (scan lockStateByOther for matching LockOwner pointer).
- **Verified:** stateid.go:390-393 freeLockStateidLocked unconditionally deletes lock-owner from sm.lockOwners regardless of sibling lock states still in sm.lockStateByOther. After delete, onLeaseExpired/EvictV40Client skip cleanup for the owner, leaking sibling LockState objects and their byte-range locks.

### [HIGH] reapExpiredSessions: BackchannelSender goroutines leak on lease-expiry reap path · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:2645`
- **What:** reapExpiredSessions manually deletes expired-client sessions from sessionsByID/sessionsByClientID (lines 2645-2648) then calls purgeV41Client (line 2666). Neither path calls stopBackchannelSender. The BackchannelSender goroutine (started via StartBackchannelSender) is only stopped inside destroySessionLocked, which reapExpiredSessions never calls.
- **Why it matters:** One goroutine leaks per expired v4.1 client. The goroutine holds a reference to the session object (deleted from the map but not freed) and continues attempting backchannel sends indefinitely, burning goroutine stack and potentially accessing freed/replaced state.
- **Fix:** In the reaper's lease-expired branch, before deleting sessions call sm.stopBackchannelSender(session.SessionID) for each session, OR replace the manual delete loop with calls to sm.destroySessionLocked(session.SessionID, true, 'lease_expired') which already handles backchannel teardown cleanly.
- **Verified:** purgeV41Client (v41_client.go:298) destroys sessions via map delete but never calls stopBackchannelSender. The reapExpiredSessions path (manager.go:2644-2648) also deletes sessionsByID/sessionsByClientID directly, bypassing destroySessionLocked. stopBackchannelSender is only called from destroySessionLocked (line 2538). BackchannelSender goroutines (started via StartBackchannelSender) remain running indefinitely for every expired v4.1 client.

### [HIGH] CREATE default-case XDR stream desync — objname+fattr4 not consumed · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/create.go:103`
- **What:** The `default` branch of the `objType` switch returns `NFS4ERR_BADTYPE` immediately without consuming `objname` (component4 = XDR string) and `createattrs` (fattr4 = bitmap + opaque) from the reader. Any unknown/unexpected `createtype4` value (e.g. `NF4ATTRDIR`=8 or future types) leaves the reader positioned mid-stream.
- **Why it matters:** COMPOUND relies on strict sequential XDR decoding; once desynchronised every subsequent op in the same COMPOUND decodes garbage, producing cascading `NFS4ERR_BADXDR` errors or silent wrong-op dispatch. The `NF4REG` case (lines 91-101) correctly consumes `DecodeString + skipFattr4` before returning — the `default` case must do the same.
- **Fix:** Before returning in the `default` case, add `_, _ = xdr.DecodeString(reader)` (consume objname) then `skipFattr4(reader)` (consume createattrs), mirroring the `NF4REG` case.
- **Verified:** create.go default case (line 103-109) returns NFS4ERR_BADTYPE immediately. objname decode (line 112) and createattrs decode (line 131) come after the switch, so they are never reached. NF4REG explicitly consumes string+fattr4 before returning (lines 94-95); default consumes nothing, leaving the XDR reader mid-stream. Subsequent ops in the same COMPOUND decode garbage.

### [HIGH] OPEN CLAIM_NULL: file created before delegation-conflict check — orphan on NFS4ERR_DELAY · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/open.go:293`
- **What:** `handleOpenClaimNull` with `OPEN4_CREATE` calls `metaSvc.CreateFile` (line 293, sets `created=true`) and then checks `CheckDelegationConflict` (line 326). When a conflict exists, `NFS4ERR_DELAY` is returned (line 332). The newly-created file is committed in metadata but has no open state and no owner.
- **Why it matters:** On client retry: (a) with `GUARDED4` the file now exists → `NFS4ERR_EXIST` (incorrect; client never got `NFS4_OK`). (b) with `UNCHECKED4` the orphaned empty file is opened as existing — correct result but wrong causal sequence. The comment at line 322 says 'check BEFORE creating state' but the file create has already happened. RFC 7530 §16.16 requires atomic create-or-open; the delegation conflict must be tested before any metadata mutation.
- **Fix:** Move `CheckDelegationConflict` to before the `metaSvc.CreateFile` call (i.e., before the `if openType == types.OPEN4_NOCREATE` block or at minimum before the create branch at line 286). For `OPEN4_CREATE` with a non-existing file, check the delegation conflict against the parent directory entry first; if conflict, return `NFS4ERR_DELAY` without creating.
- **Verified:** open.go lines 293-306: metaSvc.CreateFile runs and sets created=true before CheckDelegationConflict (line 326). If conflict exists, NFS4ERR_DELAY is returned with the file already committed in metadata. With GUARDED4 the client's retry receives NFS4ERR_EXIST; file is an orphan with no open state or owner.

### [HIGH] OPEN CLAIM_DELEGATE_CUR missing v4.1 auto-confirm — open-owner stuck unconfirmed · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/open.go:666`
- **What:** `handleOpenClaimDelegateCur` does not strip `OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM` from `openResult.RFlags` nor call `StateManager.ConfirmOpenV41` when `ctx.SkipOwnerSeqid` is true (v4.1 session). `StateManager.OpenFile` sets `OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM` for any new open-owner (state/manager.go:1196).
- **Why it matters:** `CLAIM_NULL` (line 358-363) and `CLAIM_PREVIOUS` (line 452-455) both guard this with `if ctx.SkipOwnerSeqid && openResult.RFlags&types.OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM != 0`. `CLAIM_DELEGATE_CUR` omits it entirely. A v4.1 client receives `OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM` in the response, cannot send `OPEN_CONFIRM` (removed in v4.1), and the open-owner remains unconfirmed. All subsequent LOCK operations require a confirmed open-owner and will fail with `NFS4ERR_BAD_STATEID` or equivalent.
- **Fix:** Add the same guard used in `CLAIM_NULL` immediately after the `IsReplay` check (line 666): `if ctx.SkipOwnerSeqid && openResult.RFlags&types.OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM != 0 { openResult.RFlags &^= types.OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM; _ = h.StateManager.ConfirmOpenV41(&openResult.Stateid) }`
- **Verified:** handleOpenClaimDelegateCur (open.go:666-681) has no SkipOwnerSeqid/OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM guard. CLAIM_NULL (lines 358-362) and CLAIM_PREVIOUS (lines 452-454) both strip OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM and call ConfirmOpenV41 when ctx.SkipOwnerSeqid is set; CLAIM_DELEGATE_CUR omits this entirely. v4.1 clients receive OPEN4_RESULT_CONFIRM, cannot send OPEN_CONFIRM, and the open-owner stays unconfirmed, causing LOCK/CLOSE to fail.

### [HIGH] ReturnDelegation drops sm.mu mid-function — concurrent RevokeDelegation races on same delegation · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/delegation.go:306`
- **What:** ReturnDelegation holds sm.mu, calls StopRecallTimer, then for directory delegations drops sm.mu (line 306) to call flushDirNotifications, then reacquires (line 308). During the unlocked window the delegation still exists in delegByOther with RecallTimer stopped but not removed. A concurrent RevokeDelegation timer (already past Stop because Stop has a race window per time.Timer docs) can fire, set deleg.Revoked=true, call removeDelegFromFile, delete delegStateidMap entry, and call LockManager.RevokeDelegation. When ReturnDelegation reacquires (line 308) it then also calls delete(delegByOther) and LockManager.ReturnDelegation on the same lmDelegID — double-calling LockManager on the same delegation ID.
- **Why it matters:** The lock-drop TOCTOU window is reachable whenever the recall timer fires with a short timeout (5s) at the same moment DELEGRETURN arrives. LockManager called with both RevokeDelegation and ReturnDelegation on the same ID corrupts per-file lock accounting.
- **Fix:** After reacquiring sm.mu at line 308, check if deleg.Revoked is now true and return nil (delegation was concurrently revoked, client returning a revoked delegation is valid). Also consider removing the delegation from delegByOther before dropping the lock so RevokeDelegation's exists-check fails cleanly.
- **Verified:** ReturnDelegation (delegation.go:306-308) drops sm.mu for directory delegations to call flushDirNotifications. During that window, RevokeDelegation (manager.go:785) can fire, delete delegStateidMap entry, and call lockMgr.RevokeDelegation. When ReturnDelegation reacquires, it calls lockMgr.ReturnDelegation on the same lmDelegID. Whether this corrupts LockManager state depends on LockManager semantics, but the double-call is real. Window is only for directory delegations.

### [HIGH] CB_SEQUENCE seqID and RPC XID share single atomic counter — seqIDs skip every other value · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/backchannel.go:270`
- **What:** sendCallback calls bs.nextXID.Add(1) at line 270 to get seqID, then bs.nextXID.Add(1) again at line 284 to get xid. Both values come from the same atomic counter, so seqID advances 1,3,5,... (skipping even values) and xid advances 2,4,6,.... Per RFC 8881 §2.10.6.3 the server MUST increment the slot sequence by exactly 1 per new request; a client seeing slot 0 sequence jump from 1 to 3 MUST reply NFS4ERR_SEQ_MISORDERED.
- **Why it matters:** All v4.1 CB callbacks after the very first are rejected by well-behaved clients. sendCallbackWithRetry exhausts 3 retries, calls setBackchannelFault, and all further recalls use the 5-second revocation timer. Effectively all v4.1 delegations are revoked after 5s instead of honoring the lease period — cross-protocol consistency broken.
- **Fix:** Use two separate counters: keep bs.nextXID for RPC XIDs only. Add a separate per-slot seqID field (e.g. in SlotTable or as a dedicated atomic on BackchannelSender) incremented by 1 for each new CB_SEQUENCE send.
- **Verified:** backchannel.go lines 270 and 284 both call bs.nextXID.Add(1) on the same atomic counter. seqID increments 1,3,5,... and xid increments 2,4,6,... Per RFC 8881 §2.10.6.3, slot sequence must increment by exactly 1 per new request. Well-behaved clients reject the 1→3 jump with NFS4ERR_SEQ_MISORDERED, causing all callbacks to fail and delegations to be revoked after 5s.

### [HIGH] CheckDelegationConflict recalls only first conflicting delegation — remaining READ holders never recalled · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/delegation.go:475`
- **What:** The loop marks RecallSent and launches go sendRecall for the first conflicting delegation, then immediately returns true (line 477). If multiple clients each hold a READ delegation and an incoming OPEN requests WRITE access, only the first READ delegation is recalled. All other READ delegation holders are never sent CB_RECALL.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 7530 §10.4.5: when a WRITE open conflicts with existing READ delegations all READ delegation holders must be recalled. With multiple READ holders only one is recalled; others continue caching stale data. The WRITE opener sees NFS4ERR_DELAY repeatedly until each holder happens to be the first in the map iteration on successive OPEN retries, requiring O(n) client retries in the worst case and leaving the write-delegation exclusivity invariant violated until all accidental misses are covered.
- **Fix:** Remove the early return inside the if-block. Accumulate all conflicting delegations, mark all RecallSent/RecallTime, launch goroutines for all, then return true after the loop completes if any conflict was found.
- **Verified:** CheckDelegationConflict (delegation.go:463-478): on first conflicting delegation, sets RecallSent, launches sendRecall goroutine, then returns true immediately. Multiple READ holders are never all recalled. RFC 7530 §10.4.5 requires all READ delegation holders be recalled on WRITE conflict. Remaining holders must be hit by accident on successive OPEN retries.

### [HIGH] DESTROY skips call-header MIC verification — unauthenticated context teardown · `bugs` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/framework.go:412`
- **What:** handleDestroy receives only cred (no verifBody, no headerPreimage). It deletes the context immediately without verifying the call-header MIC. The dispatch at line 412 passes neither the verifier body nor the header preimage to handleDestroy.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 2203 Section 5.3.3.3 states DESTROY is formulated like a DATA request and MUST carry a valid sequence number and header checksum verifier. Any on-path observer who captures a context handle from the INIT reply (sent in plaintext) can craft a DESTROY packet and force-delete an active client's security context, causing a DoS: the victim's next DATA request returns CREDPROBLEM. With krb5 svc_none where request bodies are unencrypted, this also allows replay of context destruction.
- **Fix:** Pass verifBody and headerPreimage to handleDestroy from Process (same as handleData). Inside handleDestroy, call verifyHeaderMIC and gssCtx.SeqWindow.Accept before p.contexts.Delete, returning RPCSEC_GSS_CREDPROBLEM on failure.
- **Verified:** framework.go line 413: handleDestroy receives only cred, no verifBody or headerPreimage. No sequence number or header MIC validation is done before deleting the context. Any attacker who captures a context handle from INIT replies can forge a DESTROY packet and kill active sessions. RFC 2203 §5.3.3.3 requires DESTROY to carry a valid header checksum verifier.

### [HIGH] readXDROpaque uses reader.Read instead of io.ReadFull — silent short-read on truncated input · `bugs` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/integrity.go:155`
- **What:** readXDROpaque calls reader.Read(data) on a *bytes.Reader. bytes.Reader.Read returns (n, nil) with n < len(data) when fewer bytes remain than requested; the trailing data[n:] bytes stay zero-filled. The short read goes undetected.
- **Why it matters:** A crafted integrity/privacy-wrapped message with a falsely large opaque-length field causes databodyInteg or checksumBytes to be partially zeroed. For integrity, the MIC is verified over wrong data producing a misleading error. For privacy (same function called from privacy.go:69), a truncated ciphertext is passed to crypto.DecryptMessage; if the cipher does not enforce minimum length it may produce zero-filled plaintext where bodySeqNum == 0 matches credSeqNum == 0 on a fresh context, potentially bypassing the dual seq_num validation.
- **Fix:** Replace reader.Read(data) with io.ReadFull(reader, data). io.ReadFull returns io.ErrUnexpectedEOF on a short read, propagating a clear error.
- **Verified:** integrity.go line 155: reader.Read(data) on *bytes.Reader — returns (n<len(data), nil) when insufficient bytes remain, leaving data[n:] zero-filled with no error. Short-read goes undetected; databodyInteg or checksumBytes may be partially zeroed, causing MIC verification over wrong data or passing zero-filled ciphertext to crypto.DecryptMessage.

### [HIGH] Double-reply for unknown NFSv4 procedure: writeReply + sendReply both fire on same XID · `bugs` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/nfs/handlers.go:359`
- **What:** `handleNFSv4Procedure` default case calls `c.writeReply(call.XID, errorReply)` to send PROC_UNAVAIL, then returns `(nil, writeReply_err)`. When `writeReply` succeeds it returns nil, so caller `handleRPCCall` receives `(replyData=nil, err=nil)`, skips all error branches, and falls through to `c.sendReply(call.XID, nil)` (line 251), sending a second empty RPC success reply for the same XID.
- **Why it matters:** Two reply frames for the same XID on the same TCP connection violate RFC 5531 and corrupt the RPC record stream. The client's RPC layer will misparse subsequent replies, causing cascading failures on any NFSv4 session that triggers the unknown-procedure branch (procedure number > 1).
- **Fix:** Return before `sendReply` fires. Either (a) use `return c.handleUnsupportedVersion(...)` pattern and let the caller not reach `sendReply`, or (b) return a sentinel so `handleRPCCall` knows a reply was already sent. Simplest: change the default case to not call `writeReply` at all — just return an error or a pre-formed reply bytes, consistent with how other error paths work:
```go
default:
    errorReply, err := rpc.MakeErrorReply(call.XID, rpc.RPCProcUnavail)
    if err != nil {
        return nil, fmt.Errorf("make NFSv4 proc unavail reply: %w", err)
    }
    return errorReply, nil  // let handleRPCCall send via sendReply
```
Or, if the intent is to send immediately and skip `sendReply`, use `return` directly from `handleRPCCall` like the `handleUnsupportedVersion` calls do.
- **Verified:** handlers.go line 359: default case calls c.writeReply (sends PROC_UNAVAIL reply) then returns (nil, nil) when writeReply succeeds. In dispatch.go line 174, replyData=nil, err=nil. No nil guard exists; falls through to sendReply(xid, nil) at line 251, sending a second empty RPC success reply for the same XID. Two reply frames corrupt the RPC record stream.

### [HIGH] Flush propagates ErrChunkLostBeforeMirror as hard error — protocol handlers fail on retryable condition · `bugs` · area: block-engine-gc-syncer
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/syncer.go:339`
- **What:** mirrorOnce returns block.ErrChunkLostBeforeMirror when a pending hash has no local bytes (chunk lost before first mirror). Flush at line 339 propagates this as a non-nil error to callers (NFS COMMIT handler, SMB Flush handler). syncLocalBlocks (upload.go:32) and uploadBlock (upload.go:69) both explicitly catch and swallow ErrChunkLostBeforeMirror as a non-fatal retry condition. Flush does not.
- **Why it matters:** Flush godoc defines err!=nil as 'hard failure, do not retry until addressed'. Protocol handlers receiving this error return a protocol-level error to NFS/SMB clients (e.g. NFS COMMIT fails, client may abort writes). The correct contract for this condition is Finalized=false, err=nil (soft condition), letting the client re-issue COMMIT/Flush on its own schedule. The inconsistency causes spurious hard failures on a retry-next-tick condition that other callers already handle gracefully.
- **Fix:** In Flush after mirrorOnce: if errors.Is(err, block.ErrChunkLostBeforeMirror) { return &block.FlushResult{Finalized: false}, nil }. This mirrors the handling in syncLocalBlocks and uploadBlock and matches the Flush soft-condition contract (Finalized=false, err=nil).
- **Verified:** `mirrorOnce` returns `block.ErrChunkLostBeforeMirror` at syncer.go:448. `Flush` at line 339 propagates it as `return nil, err`. `CommitBlockStore` returns it verbatim. NFSv4 COMMIT handler at commit.go:124 returns `NFS4ERR_IO`. The periodic uploader (upload.go:32) and `uploadBlock` (upload.go:69) both swallow it as non-fatal — but `Flush`/`CommitBlockStore` do not. Godoc says `err!=nil` is a hard failure; this condition is retryable.

### [HIGH] groupCommit.Sync failure leaves lf.eofPos stale, corrupting logIndex on next write · `bugs` · area: block-local-fs-appendlog
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/local/fs/appendwrite.go:423`
- **What:** When lf.groupCommit.Sync(ctx) returns an error (ctx cancellation while piggybacked on in-flight fsync, or raw fsync error in bypass path), the function returns at line 424 without advancing lf.eofPos and without evicting the fd. writeRecord at line 372 already wrote the full record to lf.f, advancing the OS file position by n bytes. The next AppendWrite for the same payload calls writeRecord again — the OS continues appending at old_eof+n — but logPos := lf.eofPos (line 433) equals old_eof, pointing at the abandoned record's frame. lf.eofPos += uint64(n) (line 434) then lands at old_eof+n_new, not old_eof+n+n_new. Every subsequent logIndex entry is off by n bytes, so readRecordAt will pread the wrong position, causing CRC mismatches and silent data loss in rollup.
- **Why it matters:** lf.eofPos is the canonical log-position cursor used by the logIndex to record where each record lands. It must equal the actual OS file position at all times while the fd is live. Failing fsync without evicting the fd leaves eofPos behind the true file position. The writeRecord error path (lines 403-409) correctly evicts the fd, but the Sync error path at line 423 does not apply the same recovery posture despite the same invariant violation.
- **Fix:** On groupCommit.Sync failure, apply the same fd-eviction posture as the writeRecord error path: mu.Unlock(); tsh.mu.Lock(); delete(tsh.logFDs, payloadID); tsh.mu.Unlock(); _ = lf.f.Close(). Alternatively, capture n as the pre-advance value before calling Sync and advance lf.eofPos unconditionally after writeRecord succeeds (before Sync), since the bytes are already on disk regardless of fsync outcome. The second approach matches the invariant more directly: eofPos tracks physical file size, not durability.
- **Verified:** `writeRecord` at line 372 writes data to `lf.f`, advancing the OS file position by `n` bytes. If `lf.groupCommit.Sync` at line 423 fails, the function returns at line 424 WITHOUT advancing `lf.eofPos` and WITHOUT evicting the fd. The next AppendWrite writes at OS position `old_eof+n`, but `logPos := lf.eofPos` (line 433) = `old_eof`, so the logIndex entry points to the abandoned record frame, not the new record. The `writeRecord` error path (lines 403-409) correctly evicts the fd; the Sync error path does not.

### [HIGH] ResetLocalState skips subdirectory .log files, leaving stale append-log data after restore · `bugs` · area: block-local-fs-rollup-chunk
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/local/fs/drain_reset.go:272`
- **What:** Best-effort residual-log sweep in ResetLocalState uses os.ReadDir(logsDir) and explicitly skips directories (`if e.IsDir() { continue }`). PayloadIDs with a share prefix (e.g. `share1/myfile`) produce log files at `<logsDir>/share1/myfile.log`, nested inside a subdirectory. ReadDir returns that subdirectory as a DirEntry with IsDir()==true and it is skipped. The nested `.log` file is never unlinked.
- **Why it matters:** After a snapshot restore, RestoreSnapshot calls ResetLocalState to drop all append-log state so reads resolve purely through the restored CAS manifest. If any share-prefixed payload has a log file (the common case — recovery.go:236-240 explicitly documents share-prefixed payloadIDs stored in subdirectories), that file survives the reset. The next Recover() call uses filepath.WalkDir (recursive) and reinstalls the stale log file. ReadPayloadAt then replays the surviving post-snapshot append-log records on top of the restored CAS content ('last record wins'), silently returning post-snapshot mutated bytes instead of the restored content — exactly the data corruption ResetLocalState is designed to prevent.
- **Fix:** Replace the os.ReadDir flat sweep with filepath.WalkDir (or os.RemoveAll on the entire logsDir and recreate it). Minimal fix: `_ = filepath.WalkDir(logsDir, func(path string, d os.DirEntry, err error) error { if err != nil || d.IsDir() { return nil }; _ = os.Remove(path); return nil })`. Alternatively, `os.RemoveAll(logsDir)` followed by `os.MkdirAll(logsDir, 0755)` is simpler and atomic for the whole tree.
- **Verified:** `ResetLocalState` at drain_reset.go:272-283 uses `os.ReadDir(logsDir)` (non-recursive) and skips directories (`if e.IsDir() { continue }`). `logPath` at appendwrite.go:58-59 uses `filepath.Join(bc.baseDir, "logs", payloadID+".log")` — a payloadID with a slash (e.g. `share1/myfile`) produces `logs/share1/myfile.log` nested in a subdirectory. recovery.go:18-21 documents share-prefix payloadIDs as normal. The nested `.log` survives reset and is re-installed by the recursive `filepath.WalkDir` in Recover, replaying stale post-snapshot data.

### [HIGH] updateDescendantPaths silently discards tx.PutFile error · `bugs` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/file_modify.go:829`
- **What:** Error from tx.PutFile(ctx, child) is discarded with `_`. Any child whose path fails to persist returns no error; updateDescendantPaths returns nil and the whole Move transaction commits, leaving descendant File.Path values stale.
- **Why it matters:** A failed PutFile means the child's path in the store still holds the old prefix. On postgres (path-keyed) this silently corrupts the namespace: snapshot/restore, GetFileByPayloadID, and path-based lookups resolve to dead/wrong paths. The caller's comment at line 758–763 explicitly says 'Propagate the error: a partial descendant rewrite leaves stale child Paths that diverge from the parent' — but the inner PutFile error is not propagated, so the entire protection is a no-op.
- **Fix:** Return the error instead of discarding it: `if err := tx.PutFile(ctx, child); err != nil { return fmt.Errorf("update path for %s: %w", child.Path, err) }`
- **Verified:** file_modify.go:829 discards `tx.PutFile(ctx, child)` error with `_`. `updateDescendantPaths` returns `nil` even when child path update fails. The caller comment at line 758-763 says partial rewrite leaves stale paths, but the protection is a no-op. On postgres (path-keyed) this silently corrupts the namespace after Move.

### [HIGH] PrepareWrite owner-bypass skips DOS READONLY enforcement · `bugs` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/io.go:143`
- **What:** PrepareWrite unconditionally skips checkWritePermission when the caller is the file owner (isOwner == true). checkWritePermission → checkFilePermissions → calculatePermissions is the only code path that enforces modeDOSReadonly (0x100000). An SMB client sets FILE_ATTRIBUTE_READONLY; the file owner on NFS can then write despite that flag.
- **Why it matters:** calculatePermissions clears the write permBit when mode&0x100000 is set (line 334) and has a dedicated conformance test (TestCalculatePermissions_DOSReadonlyDeniesOwnerWriteCrossProtocol in auth_permissions_sid_test.go:43). The owner bypass at io.go:145 short-circuits before that test is ever reached, breaking the documented cross-protocol READONLY contract. Root bypass is elsewhere and separately correct; this is the non-root owner path.
- **Fix:** Remove the owner short-circuit in PrepareWrite. Always call checkWritePermission regardless of ownership — the write permission check already handles owner vs. non-owner mode bit evaluation inside calculatePermissions. The comment 'Owner can always write to their own files (even if mode is 0444)' is wrong for DOS READONLY files; POSIX open-time check semantics don't apply to the SMB-layer READONLY flag.
- **Verified:** `PrepareWrite` at io.go:143-150 skips `checkWritePermission` when `isOwner==true`. The DOS readonly enforcement (`attr.Mode&0x100000 != 0` clears write permBit) lives inside `calculatePermissions` at auth_permissions.go:334, which is only reachable via `checkFilePermissions` → `checkWritePermission`. Owner bypass short-circuits before that path. A file owner can write to a `FILE_ATTRIBUTE_READONLY` file, violating the cross-protocol readonly contract.

### [HIGH] AdjustACLForMode drops Protected/AutoInherited/NullDACL/Source on chmod · `bugs` · area: metadata-acl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/acl/mode.go:99`
- **What:** AdjustACLForMode returns `&ACL{ACEs: newACEs}` — a fresh struct with only the ACEs field set. The input ACL's `Protected` (SE_DACL_PROTECTED), `AutoInherited` (SE_DACL_AUTO_INHERITED), `NullDACL`, and `Source` fields are silently discarded.
- **Why it matters:** Protected=true means the DACL blocks further inheritance from ancestors. Dropping it on chmod means a file/dir that was shielded from ancestor propagation silently becomes inheritable again on the next `ComputeInheritedACL` pass — wrong. Dropping AutoInherited means `ComputeInheritedACL` no longer stamps `ACE4_INHERITED_ACE` on children, causing inheritance-flag drift visible to smbtorture. Called from `pkg/metadata/file_modify.go:284` on every SETATTR mode change.
- **Fix:** Copy ACL metadata fields from the input: `return &ACL{ACEs: newACEs, Source: a.Source, Protected: a.Protected, AutoInherited: a.AutoInherited, NullDACL: a.NullDACL}`
- **Verified:** `AdjustACLForMode` at mode.go:99 returns `&ACL{ACEs: newACEs}` — only the `ACEs` slice is set. Input ACL fields `Protected` (SE_DACL_PROTECTED), `AutoInherited`, `NullDACL`, and `Source` are all zero-valued in the returned struct. Dropping `Protected=true` means a DACL that blocks ancestor propagation silently loses that protection on the next chmod, allowing `ComputeInheritedACL` to overwrite explicitly shielded ACEs.

### [HIGH] PropagateACL drops existingACL.Protected — SE_DACL_PROTECTED silently cleared on re-propagation · `bugs` · area: metadata-acl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/acl/inherit.go:340`
- **What:** PropagateACL builds `result := &ACL{ACEs: combined}` without copying `existingACL.Protected` (SE_DACL_PROTECTED). The code's own comment (line 308) correctly states Protected is per-SD and never inherited, but that means it must be PRESERVED from the child's existing SD, not silently zeroed.
- **Why it matters:** A child directory with Protected=true (set by Windows ACL editor or explicit SetInfo) is supposed to block further ancestor propagation. After any parent-ACL change triggers recursive PropagateACL, the child's Protected flag is lost on the returned ACL. Subsequent propagation passes will overwrite the child's ACEs with parent-derived ACEs that the operator explicitly blocked. AutoInherited from existingACL is also discarded, though the parent's value overwrites it anyway — this is a lesser issue. The real harm is the Protected erasure.
- **Fix:** Preserve the existing child SD flags: after constructing `result`, add `result.Protected = existingACL.Protected` and `result.Source = existingACL.Source`. The AutoInherited override from parent is intentional per the spec but Protected must survive from the child.
- **Verified:** `PropagateACL` at inherit.go:340 builds `result := &ACL{ACEs: combined}` and only conditionally copies `parentACL.AutoInherited` (line 344-346). `existingACL.Protected` is never copied to `result`. A child with `Protected=true` (blocking ancestor propagation) has that flag erased on every parent-ACL-change-triggered propagation pass, causing subsequent passes to overwrite the child's explicitly protected ACEs with parent-derived ones.

### [HIGH] OpLockBreakScanner uses AcquiredAt (grant time) instead of BreakStarted for break timeout, immediately force-revoking long-held leases · `bugs` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/oplock_break.go:274`
- **What:** `scanExpiredLeaseBreaks` computes `breakDeadline = pl.AcquiredAt.Add(timeout)`. `AcquiredAt` is the lease *grant* time (set once in `ToPersistedLock` from `lock.AcquiredAt`, never updated). `BreakStarted` (the actual break-start timestamp) is explicitly not persisted (`store.go:434`). For any lease older than `DefaultOpLockBreakTimeout` (35s) at the time the break is initiated, `AcquiredAt + timeout` is already in the past, so every scan tick immediately force-revokes the lease.
- **Why it matters:** A long-lived RWH lease (e.g., 60 seconds old) that just had its break initiated will have `AcquiredAt` 60 seconds in the past. With the 35s default timeout, `breakDeadline = AcquiredAt + 35s` is already 25 seconds in the past. On the next 1-second scan tick, `now.After(breakDeadline)` is true and the lease is force-revoked before the client has any time to ACK. This violates MS-SMB2 §3.3.6.5 which requires the server to wait at least 35 seconds from break *initiation*, not from lease *grant*.
- **Fix:** Persist `BreakStarted` in `PersistedLock` (add a `BreakStarted time.Time` field, populate it in `ToPersistedLock` when `lock.Lease.Breaking`, restore in `FromPersistedLock`). Update `scanExpiredLeaseBreaks` to use `pl.BreakStarted` as the deadline base. The test at `oplock_break_test.go:151` already sets `AcquiredAt: breakStart` to paper over this gap — updating it to use the proper `BreakStarted` field will make both the scanner and the test correct.
- **Verified:** `scanExpiredLeaseBreaks` at oplock_break.go:274 computes `breakDeadline = pl.AcquiredAt.Add(timeout)`. `AcquiredAt` is the lock grant time (set at creation, manager.go:826/837), never updated when `Breaking=true` is set. Break initiation sets `lock.Lease.BreakStarted = time.Now()` (manager.go:2671) but `BreakStarted` is runtime-only and not persisted (store.go:434). Comment at line 273 claiming 'AcquiredAt is updated when break initiated' is incorrect. Any lease older than 35s has `AcquiredAt+35s` already past, so the scanner force-revokes it immediately.

### [HIGH] scanExpiredLeaseBreaks deletes lease from store but never updates in-memory Manager, leaving WaitForBreakCompletion permanently blocked · `bugs` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/oplock_break.go:289`
- **What:** `scanExpiredLeaseBreaks` calls `lockStore.DeleteLock(ctx, pl.ID)` to remove a timed-out breaking lease from the persistent store, then invokes `s.callback.OnLeaseBreakTimeout(leaseKey)`. The in-memory `Manager.unifiedLocks` map is NOT updated. The `Manager` (`s.lockManager`) has `forceCompleteBreaksExceptKey` which performs the in-memory teardown, but it is never called from this path. The `OpLockBreakCallback` interface's `OnLeaseBreakTimeout` only notifies — it does not clear in-memory state.
- **Why it matters:** `WaitForBreakCompletion` (manager.go:2263) polls `lm.unifiedLocks[handleKey]` for any `lock.Lease.Breaking` entries. After the scanner deletes from the store, the in-memory record still has `Breaking=true`. Callers waiting on `WaitForBreakCompletion` will never see the break resolve through the signal path; they must wait until their context deadline triggers `forceCompleteBreaks` themselves. `HasOtherBreakingLeases` and `AnyHolderHasLeaseBits` also return stale true. `signalBreakWaitLocked` is never called, so all parked CREATEs stall until their own context expires.
- **Fix:** After `lockStore.DeleteLock` succeeds, call `lm.forceCompleteBreaksExceptKey(handleKey, [16]byte{})` on `s.lockManager` if set, or expose a `RevokeLease(leaseKey)` method that clears both store and in-memory state atomically. Alternatively, reuse the `ReleaseLease` path which already signals waiters via `signalBreakWaitLocked`.
- **Verified:** `scanExpiredLeaseBreaks` calls `lockStore.DeleteLock(ctx, pl.ID)` (persistent store only) then `s.callback.OnLeaseBreakTimeout(leaseKey)`. `OnLeaseBreakTimeout` has no production implementation (only a test mock). `Manager.unifiedLocks` still has the entry with `Lease.Breaking=true`. `WaitForBreakCompletion` at manager.go:2267-2299 polls `lm.unifiedLocks[handleKey]` — finding `Breaking=true` — and waits on `breakWaitChans`, which is never signaled. Callers stall until their context deadline triggers `forceCompleteBreaks`.

### [HIGH] memory DeleteShare leaks objectIndex entries and usedBytes counter · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/memory/shares.go:151`
- **What:** Non-transactional DeleteShare iterates store.files and deletes from files/parents/children/linkCounts/deviceNumbers but never touches store.objectIndex or store.usedBytes. The transaction-path DeleteShare (transaction.go:653-671) correctly cleans both.
- **Why it matters:** Stale objectIndex entries survive after share deletion. Next PutFile with same ObjectID gets spurious ErrConflict (objectIndex key still maps to deleted file's key). usedBytes counter is permanently inflated by the deleted share's regular-file sizes — GetUsedBytes/FSSTAT reports wrong usage forever.
- **Fix:** In the loop at line 151-158, add: if fd.Attr != nil && !fd.Attr.ObjectID.IsZero() { if mapped, ok := store.objectIndex[fd.Attr.ObjectID]; ok && mapped == key { delete(store.objectIndex, fd.Attr.ObjectID) } }. Also subtract regular-file sizes: if fd.Attr.Type == metadata.FileTypeRegular && fd.Attr.Size > 0 { store.usedBytes.Add(-int64(fd.Attr.Size)) }. Or collapse both paths so store.DeleteShare calls store.WithTransaction(ctx, func(tx) { return tx.DeleteShare(ctx, shareName) }).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: memory/shares.go DeleteShare (lines 151-158) iterates store.files deleting files/parents/children/linkCounts/deviceNumbers but never touches store.objectIndex or store.usedBytes. transaction.go:653-671 correctly handles both (lines 660-663 delete objectIndex, line 657 adjusts pendingDelta). Stale objectIndex entries survive share deletion; usedBytes permanently inflated.

### [HIGH] badger badgerTransaction.DeleteLocksByClient/DeleteLocksByFile open independent transactions, breaking outer-tx atomicity and OCC retry safety · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/badger/locks.go:625`
- **What:** badgerTransaction.DeleteLocksByClient (line 625-633) and DeleteLocksByFile (line 635-641) delegate to tx.store.lockStore.DeleteLocksByClient/DeleteLocksByFile, which open new db.Update transactions independent of the caller's badger.Txn. Similarly, IncrementServerEpoch (line 651-657) and SetCleanShutdown (line 667-673) call store-level methods that open new db.Update transactions.
- **Why it matters:** If the outer WithTransaction encounters ErrConflict and retries its fn closure, lock deletions from the first attempt are already committed and cannot be rolled back — locks are permanently deleted even though the outer operation will be retried. IncrementServerEpoch called inside a retried tx increments the epoch multiple times (once per retry). SetCleanShutdown commits out-of-band regardless of whether the outer tx succeeds.
- **Fix:** Implement in-transaction versions: DeleteLocksByClient/DeleteLocksByFile on badgerTransaction must collect lock IDs via the existing index (iterating tx.txn, same as listLocksTx) and call s.deleteLockTx(tx.txn, lockID) for each — all within tx.txn. For IncrementServerEpoch: use s.getServerEpochTx(tx.txn) + txn.Set inside tx.txn. For SetCleanShutdown: write directly to tx.txn (txn.Set([]byte(keyCleanShutdown), val)).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: badger/locks.go lines 625-633 (DeleteLocksByClient) and 635-641 (DeleteLocksByFile) delegate to store.lockStore methods that open new db.Update transactions independent of caller's badger.Txn. Lines 651-657 (IncrementServerEpoch) and 667-673 (SetCleanShutdown) do same. When outer WithTransaction retries on ErrConflict, lock deletions from first attempt are already committed and irrevocable; epoch incremented once per retry.

### [HIGH] Retry loop in WithTransaction never fires — mapPgError strips *pgconn.PgError from error chain · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/transaction.go:97`
- **What:** WithTransaction retries on isRetryableError(err), which does errors.As(err, &pgErr) to find *pgconn.PgError. But every operation inside fn (PutFile, DeleteFile, GetChild, etc.) wraps the PG error through mapPgError, which returns a new *metadata.StoreError{Code: ErrIOError, Message: ...} with no Unwrap(). StoreError has no Unwrap method (pkg/metadata/errors/errors.go). So errors.As never finds the original *pgconn.PgError; isRetryableError always returns false; the retry on deadlock (40P01) and serialization failure (40001) never triggers.
- **Why it matters:** Every concurrent-write workload under Postgres READ COMMITTED can produce 40001/40P01 errors. The declared retry mechanism is the only defense against these transient errors, but it is unconditionally bypassed. Callers receive ErrIOError instead of a transparent retry, causing spurious failures under load.
- **Fix:** Either (a) have mapPgError preserve the original error with %w so StoreError implements Unwrap, or (b) check the PG error code BEFORE calling mapPgError in the retry path: extract pgcode from err immediately in fn's return path before wrapping, or (c) add an Unwrap() method to StoreError that returns the wrapped cause. Simplest: in mapPgError, return fmt.Errorf("...: %w", pgErr) so errors.As can still find the underlying PgError through the StoreError.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: postgres/errors.go mapPgErrorCode converts 40001 and 40P01 into new *metadata.StoreError with no Unwrap() (StoreError struct has no Unwrap method). isRetryableError (transaction.go:40-51) does errors.As(err, &pgErr) looking for *pgconn.PgError — fails on StoreError since there is no error chain. Retry on serialization/deadlock never fires; callers get ErrIOError instead.

### [HIGH] SettingsWatcher.Stop() deadlocks when Start() never called · `bugs` · area: controlplane-runtime-shares
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/settings_watcher.go:127`
- **What:** `Stop()` blocks forever on `<-w.stopped` when `Start()` was never called. `stopped` is an unbuffered channel closed only inside the goroutine spawned by `Start()`. Any caller that constructs a `SettingsWatcher` and calls `Stop()` without a preceding `Start()` — including tests, early-error shutdown paths, or any code path where `lifecycle.shutdown` fires before `lifecycle.serve` reached `settings.Start(ctx)` — will deadlock.
- **Why it matters:** `NewSettingsWatcher` allocates `stopped: make(chan struct{})` but no goroutine closes it unless `Start()` was called. `lifecycle.Service.shutdown()` calls `settings.Stop()` unconditionally; if the server exits before `serve()` reaches `settings.Start(ctx)`, the process hangs.
- **Fix:** Initialize `stopped` as an already-closed channel and re-create it inside `Start()` before launching the goroutine, or add a started flag: `if !atomic.CompareAndSwap(&w.started, 0, 1) { return }` in `Start()` and guard `<-w.stopped` in `Stop()` with the same flag. Simplest: in `Stop()`, add `select { case <-w.stopped: return; default: }` before blocking, only block if `Start()` was ever called.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: settings_watcher.go Stop() (lines 118-129) closes stopCh then blocks on <-w.stopped. stopped channel is only closed inside goroutine spawned by Start() (line 95). If Start() never called, stopped is never closed, Stop() deadlocks forever. NewSettingsWatcher allocates stopped as unbuffered make(chan struct{}) with no goroutine to close it unless Start() runs.

### [HIGH] EvictBlockStore holds s.mu.RLock() across unbounded per-file disk I/O · `bugs` · area: controlplane-runtime-shares
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/shares/service.go:1703`
- **What:** `EvictBlockStore` acquires `s.mu.RLock()` at line 1703 with `defer s.mu.RUnlock()` and then calls `bs.DestroyCache()`, `bs.ListFiles()`, and `bs.EvictLocal()` (which calls `local.DeleteAppendLog` — disk I/O) for every file in every share in the registry. All write-path callers (`AddShare`, `RemoveShare`, `UpdateShare`, `DisableShare`, `EnableShare`) need `s.mu.Lock()` and will starve for the entire duration of the eviction loop.
- **Why it matters:** On a share with thousands of files, `EvictLocal` per file involves append-log deletion on disk. Holding the service-level RLock throughout serializes all share lifecycle operations against an unbounded I/O loop, causing indefinite write-lock starvation. `AddShare` / `RemoveShare` operations issued concurrently with an evict call will block until the entire eviction completes.
- **Fix:** Snapshot the target `*engine.Store` pointers under `s.mu.RLock()` into a local slice, release the lock, then operate on the engine stores outside the lock. The engine stores are independently thread-safe (`bs.enter()` / `bs.closeMu`). Pattern already used correctly in `DrainAllBlockStores` (lines 1596-1602).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: shares/service.go EvictBlockStore (line 1703) acquires s.mu.RLock() with defer s.mu.RUnlock() then calls bs.DestroyCache(), bs.ListFiles(), and bs.EvictLocal() per file (line 1742) — disk I/O — for all shares. AddShare (line 470) and RemoveShare (line 966) need s.mu.Lock() and starve for entire eviction loop duration.

### [HIGH] Response.Encode silently truncates stub data without error · `bugs` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/dcerpc.go:348`
- **What:** When fragLen > MaxFragmentSize (65535), code clamps fragLen and allocates a smaller buf, but copy(buf[24:], r.StubData) silently truncates stub data. FragLength header field still claims MaxFragmentSize bytes are present. Caller gets no error — returns a syntactically-valid but content-corrupted response.
- **Why it matters:** Client receives a complete-looking RPC PDU but reads garbage/zero bytes for the truncated portion. For LookupSids responses with many SIDs this produces incorrect SID-to-name mappings or parse errors. Should either error out or fragment the response per DCE/RPC fragmentation.
- **Fix:** Return an error (and a fault PDU) when stub data exceeds MaxFragmentSize-24, or implement proper multi-fragment response splitting (FlagFirstFrag/FlagLastFrag). At minimum: if fragLen > MaxFragmentSize { return buildFault(callID, 0x1C000009) } before building the response.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: dcerpc.go Encode (line 342-373): when fragLen > MaxFragmentSize (65535), fragLen is clamped and buf allocated to fragLen, then copy(buf[24:], r.StubData) silently truncates stub data to fit. No error returned. FragLength header still claims MaxFragmentSize. Caller gets syntactically valid but content-corrupted PDU.

### [HIGH] Data race on leaseTimeSeconds global — non-atomic uint32 written per GETATTR, read concurrently during encoding · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/attrs/encode.go:87`
- **What:** leaseTimeSeconds (plain uint32 package global) is written in SetLeaseTime (line 87) on every GETATTR call (getattr.go:45) and read concurrently in encodeSingleAttr (lines 326, 554) during parallel GETATTR/READDIR encoding. The neighboring fsMax* globals explicitly use atomic.Uint64 to avoid the same race (line 97-101), but leaseTimeSeconds does not.
- **Why it matters:** Concurrent unsynchronized read+write of a non-atomic uint32 is a data race per Go memory model. go test -race will detect it. On real hardware the word is 4-byte aligned so tearing is unlikely, but the race is real and the inconsistency is clearly an oversight given the atomics used right above.
- **Fix:** Change leaseTimeSeconds to atomic.Uint32: var leaseTimeSeconds atomic.Uint32 and init to DefaultLeaseTime in init(). Use leaseTimeSeconds.Store(seconds) in SetLeaseTime and leaseTimeSeconds.Load() in the two read sites.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: attrs/encode.go line 82 declares leaseTimeSeconds as plain var uint32. SetLeaseTime (line 86-88) writes it non-atomically. Neighboring fsMaxFileSize/fsMaxReadSize/fsMaxWriteSize (lines 99-101) explicitly use atomic.Uint64 with comment 'to avoid data races'. leaseTimeSeconds is read concurrently during GETATTR encoding (line 325+). Clear oversight; data race under go -race.

### [HIGH] LINK: nil deref on updatedFile after GetFile error · `bugs` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/link.go:239`
- **What:** After CreateHardLink succeeds, GetFile is called to refresh attributes (line 233). If it returns an error the code logs and continues (line 236), but line 239 unconditionally dereferences `updatedFile.FileAttr` — `updatedFile` is nil, causing a nil pointer panic.
- **Why it matters:** The error branch says 'Continue with cached attributes' but there are no cached attributes: `updatedFile` was declared at line 233 with no prior value, so it is nil. Any transient GetFile failure (e.g. context cancelled right after CreateHardLink succeeds) crashes the server.
- **Fix:** Guard the dereference: if updatedFile == nil, fall back to the pre-link `fileAttr.FileAttr` captured before CreateHardLink. For example:
  var nfsFileAttr *types.NFSFileAttr
  if updatedFile != nil {
      nfsFileAttr = h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &updatedFile.FileAttr)
  } else {
      nfsFileAttr = h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &fileAttr.FileAttr)
  }
- **Verified:** Confirmed: nfs/v3/handlers/link.go line 233 declares updatedFile via GetFile; line 234-237 logs error but continues without setting updatedFile to anything. Line 239 unconditionally dereferences &updatedFile.FileAttr — nil pointer panic when GetFile returns error (context cancel, transient store error). Comment says 'continue with cached attributes' but no cached value exists.

### [HIGH] CREATE EXCLUSIVE: verifier=0 always treated as conflict instead of retry · `bugs` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/create.go:199`
- **What:** The EXCLUSIVE retry check is `existingFile.IdempotencyToken == req.Verf && req.Verf != 0`. When both are 0 the guard `req.Verf != 0` fails and the code falls through to 'different token — return NFS3ErrExist'. RFC 1813 does not forbid a zero verifier; some clients send 0 or the store may not have persisted the token (e.g. after restart). The client's valid retry is rejected as a conflict.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 1813 §3.3.8 says the server compares the stored verifier with the client's verifier; there is no exclusion for the zero value. Excluding zero means: (a) a client using verf=0 can never successfully retry a CREATE EXCLUSIVE, and (b) if IdempotencyToken was lost (store restart) every retry returns EXIST even though the file was created by that client.
- **Fix:** Remove the `req.Verf != 0` guard. The comparison `existingFile.IdempotencyToken == req.Verf` is sufficient. If you want to avoid accidental matches when the token was never stored, check `existingFile.IdempotencyToken != 0 || req.Verf != 0` as the guard for the conflict path instead of blocking the retry path.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at create.go:199. Guard `existingFile.IdempotencyToken == req.Verf && req.Verf != 0` explicitly excludes zero verifier. When req.Verf==0 (or both are 0), falls through to the 'different token' branch at line 228 and returns NFS3ErrExist. RFC 1813 has no exclusion for zero verifier.

### [HIGH] NLM FREE_ALL handler is a no-op — crashed-client locks never released via direct FREE_ALL · `bugs` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/free_all.go:77`
- **What:** FreeAll() decodes the request and logs it, then returns immediately without releasing any locks. The comment says 'actual lock release is triggered by the adapter's OnClientCrash callback', but OnClientCrash is only wired through the NSM notifier path (nsm.Notifier.handleClientCrash). A Linux client that reboots and sends NLM FREE_ALL directly to the NLM port — without having previously registered via NSM SM_MON, or when NSM notification races — will receive an empty void response while all its byte-range locks remain held on the server.
- **Why it matters:** Per RFC 1813 / X/Open NLMv4, FREE_ALL is the definitive crash-recovery RPC for the lock manager. rpc.lockd sends it to release all locks on reboot regardless of NSM state. If the handler does nothing, stale locks persist indefinitely, blocking other clients from acquiring those byte ranges until server restart.
- **Fix:** Wire the crash-cleanup directly in the handler: after decoding req.Name, call h.onClientCrash (add a callback field to Handler similar to how nsm.Notifier wires it) or accept an NLMLockService extension method ReleaseAllLocksForClient(clientID string). Minimally: h.blockingQueue.RemoveClientWaiters(req.Name) must be called, and the lock manager's ReleaseByOwnerPrefix("nlm:"+req.Name+":") must be invoked across all shares.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at free_all.go:77-93. Handler decodes request, logs it, returns void — zero lock release. Comment says OnClientCrash handles it, but OnClientCrash is only wired through nsm/notifier.go handleClientCrash (SM_NOTIFY path). Direct NLM FREE_ALL RPC does not trigger it. Stale locks persist indefinitely.

### [HIGH] NLM GRANTED callback hardcodes port 12049 — breaks blocking-lock wake-up for all real NFS clients · `bugs` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/lock.go:259`
- **What:** extractCallbackAddr() strips the client port and replaces it with 12049, the server's NFS port. The NLM_GRANTED callback must be sent to the port the NLM client is listening on, which is an ephemeral port registered with the client-side portmapper. No real NFS client listens for NLM callbacks on port 12049; they register an arbitrary port with their portmapper and pass it implicitly via the RPC source address.
- **Why it matters:** Every blocking NLM LOCK that pends will never be woken up: ProcessGrantedCallback dials port 12049 on the client host, which will either be refused or hit a different service. The lock is acquired server-side but the client never receives NLM_GRANTED, leaving the client blocked forever (or until timeout). This makes all blocking NLM locks effectively broken.
- **Fix:** The NLM callback port must be obtained by querying the client's portmapper: dial clientHost:111 (or client's portmap port), issue PMAP_GETPORT(prog=NLM, vers=4, prot=TCP), use the returned port. Store the resolved callback address in the Waiter at enqueue time. Alternatively, use the RPC source port if the NLM spec permits (it does not — the callback goes to the client's NLM listener, not the originating socket).
- **Verified:** Confirmed at lock.go:249-259. extractCallbackAddr() strips client port and hardcodes 12049. Used at line 170 to set CallbackAddr on the Waiter, then passed to ProcessGrantedCallback→SendGrantedCallback. NLM clients register an ephemeral port; none listen on 12049. All blocking NLM locks permanently stall.

### [HIGH] lz4EncoderHandle.Close() pools writer unconditionally on error — poisoned encoder recycled · `bugs` · area: block-remote-s3-encryption-compression
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/compression/codec.go:172`
- **What:** lz4WriterPool.Put(h.w) executes on line 172 regardless of whether h.w.Close() returned an error on line 171. Same pattern in zstdEncoderHandle.Close() at line 94. A failed Close() means the lz4/zstd encoder has not flushed its internal frame (lz4 end-mark not written, zstd stream not finalized); its internal state is indeterminate. The next caller pops this writer from the pool, calls Reset(newWriter), and compresses into it — producing a silently truncated or corrupt compressed frame.
- **Why it matters:** lz4.Writer.Close() can fail if the underlying bytes.Buffer write errors. When decorator.Put() also calls enc.Close() from the error path (decorator.go:62, error discarded with '_'), a write-error encoder is guaranteed to be pooled. On the next Put the pool returns this dirty writer; Reset() rebinds its output but does not reset internal LZ4 block/frame state. The corrupted compressed body may be smaller than the original by coincidence, pass the size check at decorator.go:72, get framed, and go to S3 — later Get decodes garbage plaintext. If the compression decorator sits below the encryption decorator the garbage ciphertext still authenticates (AEAD is over the compressed body), so the corruption is undetected until the decompressed plaintext is consumed by the caller.
- **Fix:** Guard the Put with the error: `if err == nil { lz4WriterPool.Put(h.w) }` (and same for zstdEncoderPool.Put at codec.go:94). On error, let the writer be GC'd rather than recycled. The encoder-write error path in decorator.go:62 should propagate the Close error or at minimum not rely on the pool being clean: `if closeErr := enc.Close(); closeErr != nil { /* don't pool */ }`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at codec.go:166-174. lz4EncoderHandle.Close(): err=h.w.Close() line 171, then lz4WriterPool.Put(h.w) line 172 executes unconditionally. Failed Close() leaves encoder with unflushed frame; pooled writer produces corrupt lz4 stream on next use. decorator.go line 62 also calls enc.Close() with discarded error on write-error path, guaranteeing a dirty lz4 encoder enters the pool.

### [HIGH] zstdEncoderHandle.Close() pools encoder unconditionally on error — same pool-poisoning as lz4 · `bugs` · area: block-remote-s3-encryption-compression
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/compression/codec.go:94`
- **What:** zstdEncoderPool.Put(h.enc) at line 94 executes whether or not h.enc.Close() (line 93) returned an error. A zstd encoder whose Close() failed has not written its final frame bytes; its next Reset()+use produces a stream that begins mid-frame from the perspective of a zstd decoder, causing ErrCompressedFrameCorrupt or silent wrong output on Get.
- **Why it matters:** zstd.Encoder.Close() flushes and writes the end-of-stream marker. If the underlying bytes.Buffer write fails (e.g., OOM), Close returns an error and the encoder's internal flush queue is non-empty. Put recycles this encoder; Reset() changes the output writer but zstd's internal state (unflushed blocks, checksums) carries over. Subsequent compression produces an undecodable frame. The framed body passes the compression/size check at decorator.go:72 and is written to S3 verbatim. All subsequent Get calls for that block fail at decompression.
- **Fix:** Same as lz4: `if err == nil { zstdEncoderPool.Put(h.enc) }`. On error discard; the pool's New() will create a fresh encoder on the next Get().
- **Verified:** Confirmed at codec.go:88-97. zstdEncoderHandle.Close(): err=h.enc.Close() line 93, then zstdEncoderPool.Put(h.enc) line 94 executes unconditionally. Same pool-poisoning as lz4: failed Close leaves zstd stream without end-of-frame marker; next caller gets broken encoder after Reset().

### [HIGH] testLock_CleanShutdownMarker: toggle-to-false never read back — backend silent-ignore bug passes · `bugs` · area: metadata-storetest-conformance
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/storetest/lock_persistence.go:127`
- **What:** SetCleanShutdown(false) called at line 127 but no GetCleanShutdown follows before immediately overwriting with SetCleanShutdown(true) at line 133
- **Why it matters:** The function comment and the named contract both declare 'Toggling back to false reads false again' as an asserted property. Without a read-back, a backend that ignores SetCleanShutdown(false) when the stored value is true passes this test. Such a backend would always enter grace-period on restart (90-second wedge) since the crash marker is never correctly cleared.
- **Fix:** After line 128, add: `got, err = store.GetCleanShutdown(ctx); if err != nil { t.Fatalf("GetCleanShutdown (after toggle false): %v", err) }; if got { t.Fatalf("after toggle SetCleanShutdown(false), GetCleanShutdown = true; unclean marker not stored") }`
- **Verified:** Confirmed at lock_persistence.go:127-133. SetCleanShutdown(false) at line 127 is called but there is no GetCleanShutdown read-back before SetCleanShutdown(true) at line 133 overwrites it. A backend that ignores Set(false) when value is true silently passes this test, allowing grace-period wedge on restart.

### [HIGH] reconcileINV02: per-hash dedup skips RefCount of same-hash duplicate FileBlock rows — INV02 checker under-counts · `bugs` · area: metadata-storetest-conformance
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/storetest/inv02_fuzz.go:513`
- **What:** seen map deduplicates enumerated hashes so GetByHash is called at most once per ContentHash; only that one row's RefCount contributes to totalRefCount
- **Why it matters:** The contract explicitly allows multiple FileBlock rows with the same ContentHash (testPut_TwoIDsSameHash pins this). Each such row has an independent RefCount. If two rows share a hash with RefCount=1 each, reconcileINV02 counts only RefCount=1 (one row) while totalRefs counts both file references. The INV02 invariant check therefore produces false violations and—critically—misses real leaks on same-hash duplicate rows, making the PropertyFuzz blind to a whole class of refcount bugs.
- **Fix:** Remove the seen-dedup loop. Instead enumerate all FileBlock IDs (via ListFileBlocks across all payloads or the legacy interface) and sum their RefCounts directly. Alternatively, after EnumerateFileBlocks, iterate all blocks via ListFileBlocks to sum per-ID RefCounts rather than per-hash.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at inv02_fuzz.go:511-525. reconcileINV02 uses a `seen` map keyed by ContentHash and only counts RefCount of one row per hash via GetByHash. testPut_TwoIDsSameHash (file_block_ops.go:680) pins that two rows with same hash and independent RefCount=1 each are valid. The INV02 checker counts 1 instead of 2, producing false violations and missing real refcount leaks on same-hash duplicate rows.

### [HIGH] SetUserSharePermission / SetGroupSharePermission silently drops new permissions · `bugs` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/permissions.go:37`
- **What:** Both SetUserSharePermission and SetGroupSharePermission call db.Save(perm) on structs with composite primary keys (UserID+ShareID and GroupID+ShareID). GORM Save decides INSERT vs UPDATE by checking whether the primary key is the zero value — but for a composite PK that is never zero, so Save always issues UPDATE. When the row does not yet exist, the UPDATE matches 0 rows; GORM returns nil error and the permission is silently discarded.
- **Why it matters:** Interface contract says 'creates or updates'. Any caller that relies on Save to insert a new permission for the first time (which is the normal first-call path) silently gets no row in the DB. Share access is then evaluated against the share default, not the explicit permission that was supposedly set.
- **Fix:** Replace Save with an explicit upsert. For PostgreSQL use clause.OnConflict; for SQLite do a manual select-then-insert-or-update inside a transaction. Example: use db.Clauses(clause.OnConflict{Columns:[]clause.Column{{Name:"user_id"},{Name:"share_id"}}, DoUpdates: clause.AssignmentColumns([]string{"permission","share_name"})}).Create(perm).
- **Verified:** Confirmed at permissions.go:37,102. Both SetUserSharePermission and SetGroupSharePermission use db.Save(perm). Models UserSharePermission (user.go:154-155) and GroupSharePermission (group.go:51-52) have composite primaryKey (UserID+ShareID and GroupID+ShareID) as non-zero strings. GORM v1.31.1 Save always issues UPDATE for non-zero PKs; first-time insert silently drops with nil error.

### [HIGH] DSN() does not quote Postgres credentials — spaces in host/password/dbname corrupt the DSN · `bugs` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/gorm.go:86`
- **What:** DSN() builds the libpq keyword=value string via fmt.Sprintf concatenation without quoting any field. A password, username, host, or dbname containing a space (e.g. password='foo bar') produces a malformed DSN: the parser sees 'bar' as an unknown keyword and returns a connection error. Special characters like single-quote or backslash in those fields also corrupt the string.
- **Why it matters:** libpq keyword=value format requires values containing spaces or special chars to be enclosed in single quotes with internal single-quotes escaped as \'.
