Raw Sprintf interpolation never does this. Users who configure a password with a space get an opaque 'invalid dsn' or 'unknown option' error with no indication of the real cause.
- **Fix:** Either use pgx's pgconn.Config / url.Values URL form (postgres://user:pass@host/db?sslmode=...) where net/url handles escaping, or write a quoteLibpqValue helper that wraps the value in single quotes and escapes internal ' and \.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at gorm.go:86-87. DSN() builds libpq keyword=value string via raw fmt.Sprintf with no quoting. Password/host/dbname/user containing spaces or single-quotes produce malformed DSN — libpq parser fails with opaque error. Fix: wrap each value in single quotes with internal single-quote escaping.

### [HIGH] ChangeOwnPassword: partial-update leaves user locked out on UpdateUser failure · `bugs` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/users.go:378`
- **What:** UpdatePassword (line 371) succeeds, then UpdateUser (line 378) is called to clear MustChangePassword. If UpdateUser fails, handler returns 500 and no new token is issued. Password is now changed but MustChangePassword flag remains true in DB. User's old token is stale; every subsequent protected request is blocked by RequirePasswordChange. No self-recovery path — admin must manually clear the flag.
- **Why it matters:** Non-atomic two-step write with no rollback or compensation. UpdatePassword and UpdateUser are separate DB calls. A transient DB error between them permanently locks the user out of the system, including the /users/me/password endpoint itself (which re-reads MustChangePassword from DB).
- **Fix:** Combine the password hash update and MustChangePassword=false clear into a single atomic store operation (e.g. UpdatePasswordAndClearMustChange), or wrap both in a transaction. If the store interface cannot be changed, at minimum re-attempt UpdateUser with a retry loop and log a critical alert on persistent failure.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at users.go:371-379. UpdatePassword succeeds at line 371 (password changed in DB), then UpdateUser at line 378 clears MustChangePassword. If UpdateUser fails, handler returns 500 with no rollback. Password is changed but MustChangePassword=true remains; old token is stale; user cannot login or reach the password-change endpoint again. No recovery path short of admin DB fix.

### [HIGH] DITTOFS_* env vars silently ignored when no config file exists · `bugs` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/config/config.go:413`
- **What:** Load() returns GetDefaultConfig() directly when no config file is found, bypassing Viper entirely. All DITTOFS_* env vars bound in setupViper (via AutomaticEnv + BindEnv loop) are never read.
- **Why it matters:** Container deployments that rely purely on env vars (no config file at default path) get hard-coded defaults regardless of any DITTOFS_DATABASE_TYPE, DITTOFS_CONTROLPLANE_SECRET, DITTOFS_KERBEROS_* etc. settings. DITTOFS_DATABASE_TYPE=postgres silently boots SQLite; DITTOFS_CONTROLPLANE_SECRET is ignored meaning JWT signing uses the default/empty secret.
- **Fix:** Remove the early-return shortcut. When no config file is found, still call v.Unmarshal into a Config (Viper will supply zeros for all missing keys), then ApplyDefaults + Validate, so env vars take effect. Or: unmarshal before returning defaults, and only fall back to GetDefaultConfig() if Unmarshal also fails.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. pkg/config/config.go:413 returns GetDefaultConfig() directly when configFileFound=false, skipping the v.Unmarshal call entirely. setupViper at line 404 bound all DITTOFS_* env vars via AutomaticEnv+BindEnv loop, but that Viper instance is never queried. All env-var overrides silently ignored for container-only deployments.

### [HIGH] provisionOperatorAccount: login with freshly-generated password when user already exists (409) · `bugs` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/auth_reconciler.go:250`
- **What:** When `CreateUser` returns HTTP 409 (user already exists), the code falls through to `apiClient.Login` at line 250 using `operatorPassword` — the freshly-generated random password for this reconcile. But the existing user was created with a different password stored in a previously-deleted credentials secret. The login will fail with 401, causing permanent auth failure requiring manual intervention.
- **Why it matters:** The credentials secret is absent (caller checked `IsNotFound` before entering `provisionOperatorAccount`), so the old password is irrecoverable. The new random password won't match the existing user's stored password, so `Login` returns 401. `isTransientError` returns false for 401, so the error propagates as a permanent failure with no requeue.
- **Fix:** On 409: either (a) call admin API to reset the existing operator user's password to `operatorPassword` before logging in, or (b) delete the existing user and recreate it, or (c) treat 409 as an unrecoverable signal and emit a warning event asking the operator to delete the user manually.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_reconciler.go:242-246: 409 path logs and falls through. Line 250 calls apiClient.Login with freshly-generated operatorPassword. If the user was previously created (with a different password) and the credentials secret was deleted, Login returns 401. isTransientError returns false for 401 so error propagates as permanent failure with no requeue — operator stuck.

### [HIGH] MFsymlink auto-conversion: client-controlled symlink target injected without path validation · `security` · area: smb-create-open
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/close.go:912`
- **What:** On CLOSE, checkAndConvertMFsymlink reads a 1067-byte file written by the SMB client, decodes the symlink target via mfsymlink.Decode, and calls metaSvc.CreateSymlink with that target verbatim. ValidateSymlinkTarget (pkg/metadata/validation.go:201) only rejects empty string. No restriction on target content — absolute paths, `../../..` escapes, or `/etc/shadow` are all accepted.
- **Why it matters:** An authenticated SMB client can write a specially crafted 1067-byte file (XSym\n magic + MD5 + any target string up to 1023 bytes), then CLOSE it. The server creates a real symlink with the attacker-controlled target in the virtual filesystem. NFS clients (or future SMB follow-symlink paths) can then dereference that symlink to reach paths outside the share root — classic path traversal via symlink. This bypasses the share-boundary protection that file handle opaqueness and path normalization provide for direct CREATEs.
- **Fix:** In convertToRealSymlink (close.go:873) or in ValidateSymlinkTarget (validation.go:201), reject or sanitize targets that are absolute paths pointing outside the share (e.g., starting with / and not under the share root) or that contain `../` sequences escaping the share tree. Alternatively, require the SMB session to hold FILE_WRITE_ATTRIBUTES + a per-share 'allow-symlink-creation' capability before auto-converting MFsymlinks. At minimum, add a configurable toggle (default: disabled) for MFsymlink auto-conversion so operators control the attack surface.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. close.go:912 calls metaSvc.CreateSymlink with mfsymlink.Decode output as target verbatim. CreateSymlink (file_create.go:26) calls ValidateSymlinkTarget which only rejects empty string (validation.go:201-208). No path traversal check. Authenticated SMB client can write crafted 1067-byte XSym file and trigger symlink creation to arbitrary target including /etc/shadow or ../../ escapes.

### [HIGH] NTLM auth bypass: user with no NT hash gets full authenticated session · `security` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/session_setup.go:1218`
- **What:** When `hasNTHash=false` (user exists + enabled, but `GetNTHash()` returns no hash) the code falls through to line 1241: `CreateSessionWithUser` is called with `IsGuest=false`, mapping the client-supplied username to a real authenticated identity. No credential is verified. Any client that knows a valid username can authenticate as that user by sending an NTLM AUTHENTICATE with any (or no) NtChallengeResponse.
- **Why it matters:** Missing auth — the credential-check block at line 1088 (`if hasNTHash && len(authMsg.NtChallengeResponse) > 0`) is guarded only when a hash exists. The fallthrough at line 1218 grants the full user identity with a comment explicitly calling this a security bypass. The resulting session has `IsGuest=false` and carries the user's UID/GID/SID for all subsequent ACL checks, bypassing all DACL enforcement.
- **Fix:** Return `StatusLogonFailure` when `!hasNTHash` (no hash configured = account not usable for NTLM). Remove the 'transitional' path entirely; the admin action `dittofs user passwd` should be required before any authentication is possible. At minimum: treat no-NT-hash identically to wrong-password and call `destroySessionOnReauthFailure` then return `StatusLogonFailure`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. session_setup.go:1218-1241: when hasNTHash=false, code skips credential validation and calls CreateSessionWithUser with IsGuest=false. Code comment at 1218 explicitly says 'SECURITY: User exists but no valid NT hash configured... Any client knowing the username can authenticate - this bypasses credential checks entirely.' Real auth bypass, not a configuration edge-case.

### [HIGH] Anonymous/null SMB session mapped to UID 0 (root) in AuthContext · `security` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/auth_helper.go:69`
- **What:** `BuildAuthContext` for `ctx.User==nil && !ctx.IsGuest` (anonymous/null session) sets UID=0, GID=0 on the `metadata.AuthContext`. Any metadata store implementation that grants elevated access to UID 0 (root-bypass in POSIX permission checks) will grant that access to an unauthenticated anonymous SMB connection.
- **Why it matters:** An anonymous NTLM logon (empty `Username` or `FlagAnonymous` set) creates a null session (`IsNull=true`, `IsGuest=false`, `User=nil`). `createAnonymousSession` does not set `ctx.IsGuest=true`, so `BuildAuthContext` takes the `else` branch at line 68 and synthesises UID=0. Downstream metadata stores performing a UID-0 root-bypass (documented in `auth_priming_test.go:7`) will treat this anonymous connection as root.
- **Fix:** Map null/anonymous sessions to a safe unprivileged UID (e.g. 65534 `nobody`) the same as guest, or reject anonymous access at `checkGuestPolicy` when the operator has not explicitly enabled it. At minimum change the `else` branch in `BuildAuthContext` to use UID=65534/GID=65534 instead of 0/0, removing the comment 'use root (for now)'.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_helper.go:62-74: when ctx.User==nil && !ctx.IsGuest (anonymous/null session), UID=0, GID=0 assigned. Comment says 'Anonymous/null session - use root (for now)'. Any anonymous NTLM logon gets UID 0 in AuthContext, bypassing POSIX permission checks in stores that special-case root.

### [HIGH] LEASE_BREAK_ACK missing session ownership check — any session can ack another session's lease break · `security` · area: smb-lease-oplock-notify
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/stub_handlers.go:808`
- **What:** handleLeaseBreakAck passes client-supplied LeaseKey directly to LeaseManager.AcknowledgeLeaseBreak with no check that ctx.SessionID matches the session recorded in LeaseManager.sessionMap for that key. Epoch is hardcoded 0, bypassing the epoch staleness guard in acknowledgeLeaseBreakImpl (leases.go:919: `if epoch != 0 && ...`).
- **Why it matters:** Any authenticated session can send OPLOCK_BREAK with a forged/guessed 16-byte LeaseKey to forcibly complete a different session's in-progress lease break, downgrading that session's cached lease (Write→None). Attacker on same server can suppress another client's write caching, causing data-integrity failures or DoS. The epoch=0 bypass also lets replayed stale acks pass unchecked.
- **Fix:** Before calling AcknowledgeLeaseBreak, verify ctx.SessionID matches the owner: call lm.GetSessionForLease(ack.LeaseKey) and compare to ctx.SessionID; return STATUS_ACCESS_DENIED on mismatch. Also pass the epoch from the wire message (wire format bytes 2-3 in the LeaseBreakAcknowledgment; currently DecodeLeaseBreakAcknowledgment skips them via r.Skip(6)) to AcknowledgeLeaseBreak instead of hardcoded 0, so stale acks are rejected.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. handleLeaseBreakAck at stub_handlers.go:808 calls h.LeaseManager.AcknowledgeLeaseBreak with hardcoded epoch=0 and no check that ctx.SessionID matches sessionMap[leaseKey]. LeaseManager.sessionMap records the owning sessionID per leaseKey (lease/manager.go:89,285) but AcknowledgeLeaseBreak (lease/manager.go:375) only resolves the shareName from leaseShare, never verifies session ownership. Epoch=0 bypasses the staleness guard at leases.go:919.

### [HIGH] COPYCHUNK access gate checks DesiredAccess instead of GrantedAccess · `security` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/ioctl_copychunk.go:250`
- **What:** validateCopyChunkAccess reads src.DesiredAccess and dst.DesiredAccess (lines 250-251) when checking FILE_READ_DATA/FILE_EXECUTE on source and FILE_WRITE_DATA/FILE_APPEND_DATA/FILE_READ_DATA on destination. DesiredAccess is the client-supplied mask before DACL evaluation — it can contain MAXIMUM_ALLOWED or GENERIC_ALL even when the DACL denies the specific bits. Every other access gate in the SMB handler layer (READ line 196, SET_SPARSE line 78, QUERY_INFO line 294, security.go) uses GrantedAccess (the post-DACL intersection stored at CREATE time).
- **Why it matters:** A client can open a file with MAXIMUM_ALLOWED or GENERIC_ALL DesiredAccess but receive a restricted GrantedAccess from the DACL (e.g., read-only). validateCopyChunkAccess will still pass the write check on the destination because MAXIMUM_ALLOWED is non-zero and includes FILE_WRITE_DATA after the bitwise AND. This bypasses DACL-controlled write restrictions for server-side copy, allowing unauthorized data writes to the destination file. Same bug class explicitly called out for CHANGE_NOTIFY (#616) and WRITE (#603) in codebase comments.
- **Fix:** Replace src.DesiredAccess with src.GrantedAccess and dst.DesiredAccess with dst.GrantedAccess in validateCopyChunkAccess (lines 250-251 and log lines 256/263/270). The function already has access to both fields via OpenFile. Example: `srcAccess := types.AccessMask(src.GrantedAccess)` / `dstAccess := types.AccessMask(dst.GrantedAccess)`. Also expand GENERIC_* bits before checking if GrantedAccess may contain unresolved generic bits (use the existing hasAccessRight helper or resolveAccessFlags).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. validateCopyChunkAccess at ioctl_copychunk.go:250-251 reads src.DesiredAccess and dst.DesiredAccess. All other access gates (read.go:196, security.go) use GrantedAccess (post-DACL). A MAXIMUM_ALLOWED open whose DACL grants only read-only access will still pass the write check on destination because DesiredAccess contains MAXIMUM_ALLOWED|FILE_WRITE_DATA bits pre-DACL.

### [HIGH] Related compound subcommand signatures never verified — auth bypass · `security` · area: smb-framing-dispatch-compound
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/compound.go:596`
- **What:** VerifyCompoundCommandSignature is called with the raw parsed hdr before SessionID inheritance. Related subcommands carry SessionID=0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF (sentinel). GetSession(0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF) returns ok=false at line 596-599, causing the function to return nil (skip). SessionID is only resolved to the real value at line 860-862, AFTER the signature check. Result: every related compound subcommand (WRITE, SET_INFO, READ, CLOSE, etc.) on a non-encrypted signing-required session has its signature silently accepted regardless of content.
- **Why it matters:** MS-SMB2 §3.3.5.2.7.2 requires each command in a compound to be individually signed and verified. The spec does not exempt related operations. An on-path attacker or a rogue SMB client on a non-encrypted, signing-required session can substitute arbitrary body bytes in any related compound subcommand and the server will execute the tampered request. Attacker controls: file contents (WRITE), attributes/ACLs (SET_INFO), rename targets (SET_INFO rename), delete-on-close flag — any operation reachable via a related compound. The NeedsSession gate in prepareDispatch ensures the session must exist, but does not re-verify the signature on the modified body.
- **Fix:** Resolve the session before calling VerifyCompoundCommandSignature, or pass the inherited session ID explicitly. In processRemaining, perform the SessionID inheritance block (lines 859-866) BEFORE the signature verification block (lines 803-810). Alternatively, in VerifyCompoundCommandSignature accept an optional override sessionID and use it when hdr.SessionID is the sentinel 0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF, falling back to s.lastSessionID passed by the caller.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. VerifyCompoundCommandSignature is called at compound.go:804 with pre-inheritance hdr. Related commands carry hdr.SessionID=0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF; GetSession(0xFFFF...) returns ok=false at line 596-598; function returns nil (skip). SessionID is only patched to the real value at lines 860-862, AFTER signature verification. Every related compound subcommand on a signing-required non-encrypted session has its signature silently accepted.

### [HIGH] Missing NFS4ERR_CLID_INUSE check — principal mismatch allows session/lease hijack · `security` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:319`
- **What:** SetClientID and all five case-handlers (createNewClient, reuseConfirmedClient, handleClientReboot, replaceUnconfirmed) store the principal but never compare it against the existing confirmed record's principal. RFC 7530 §9.1.1 Case 5: when a confirmed record exists with the same clientIDStr+verifier but a DIFFERENT RPCSEC_GSS / AUTH_SYS principal, the server MUST return NFS4ERR_CLID_INUSE. ErrClientIDInUse is defined in client.go:21 but is never returned anywhere.
- **Why it matters:** Any client that knows a victim's nfs_client_id4 string and verifier (both visible on the wire) can call SETCLIENTID from a different UID/principal and immediately obtain the same clientID+confirmVerifier. After SETCLIENTID_CONFIRM it replaces the victim's confirmed record, inheriting all open state, locks and delegations — a complete session takeover without authentication.
- **Fix:** In reuseConfirmedClient (Case 5) and reuseConfirmedClient (Case 2 fallback), after verifier match, compare principal against confirmed.Principal. When both are non-empty and differ, return ErrClientIDInUse. Example guard in reuseConfirmedClient before line ~419:

if princ != "" && confirmed.Principal != "" && princ != confirmed.Principal {
    return nil, ErrClientIDInUse
}

Same check needed in handleClientReboot (Case 3) to reject a different-principal client from stealing the reboot slot.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. SetClientID at manager.go:319-354 implements five cases. Case 5 (confirmed!=nil, verifier matches) goes to reuseConfirmedClient with no principal comparison against confirmed.Principal. ErrClientIDInUse defined in client.go:21 but never returned anywhere in the codebase. RFC 7530 §9.1.1 mandates NFS4ERR_CLID_INUSE when principal differs on same clientIDStr+verifier.

### [HIGH] SSRF via client-controlled callback address in SETCLIENTID / CB_NULL and CB_RECALL · `security` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/callback.go:124`
- **What:** dialCallback dials an arbitrary host:port derived from the client-supplied cbNetID+cbAddr fields of SETCLIENTID (setclientid.go:50-65, manager.go:612-631). No validation is performed on the resolved host — loopback (127.x), link-local (169.254.x), RFC-1918, or cloud-metadata addresses are all accepted. The CB_NULL probe fires asynchronously in a goroutine from ConfirmClientID at manager.go:614, and CB_RECALL fires on every delegation recall.
- **Why it matters:** Any authenticated (or unauthenticated, if AUTH_NONE is in use) NFS client can force the server to make outbound TCP connections to arbitrary addresses. In cloud environments this trivially reaches the instance metadata service (169.254.169.254) or internal services. Because the connection sends a valid RPC CALL frame and reads back a response, it can be used for port-scanning internal networks or exploiting metadata-credential endpoints.
- **Fix:** In dialCallback (or ParseUniversalAddr caller), validate the resolved host before dialing:
1. Resolve the host to an IP.
2. Reject loopback (127.0.0.0/8, ::1), link-local (169.254.0.0/16, fe80::/10), cloud-metadata (169.254.169.254), and RFC-1918 ranges unless the server is explicitly configured to allow them.
Alternatively, restrict acceptable netids to 'tcp'/'tcp6' and validate the uaddr octets are in the client-network range.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. dialCallback at callback.go:124 calls ParseUniversalAddr then net.Dialer.DialContext with no host validation. CB_NULL fires in goroutine from ConfirmClientID at manager.go:614. No check for loopback, RFC-1918, or cloud metadata addresses (169.254.169.254). Any authenticated NFS client controls the callback host:port.

### [HIGH] RPCSEC_GSS auth claimed without verified identity — COMPOUND proceeds as anonymous · `security` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/context.go:50`
- **What:** ExtractV4HandlerContext: when AuthFlavor==AuthRPCSECGSS but gss.IdentityFromContext returns nil (no authenticated Kerberos principal in context), logs a warning and returns a CompoundContext with nil UID/GID. The COMPOUND is not rejected.
- **Why it matters:** buildV4AuthContext treats nil UID/GID as anonymous (authMethod="anonymous") and passes it to ResolveSharePermission. A client can claim RPCSEC_GSS flavor without completing the GSS handshake — bypassing RequireKerberos enforcement that only checks flavor at mount time, not per-COMPOUND. Operations execute under anonymous/squash identity instead of being refused with NFS4ERR_WRONGSEC.
- **Fix:** Return NFS4ERR_WRONGSEC (or refuse to build the CompoundContext) when AuthFlavor==AuthRPCSECGSS but no GSS identity is present in the context. Add: if compCtx.AuthFlavor == rpc.AuthRPCSECGSS && gss.IdentityFromContext(ctx) == nil { return nil, NFS4ERR_WRONGSEC } before the COMPOUND dispatch, or reject in ProcessCompound before dispatching ops.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. ExtractV4HandlerContext at context.go:36-53: when AuthFlavor==AuthRPCSECGSS but gss.IdentityFromContext returns nil, logs warning and returns CompoundContext with nil UID/GID (lines 51-53). buildV4AuthContext at helpers.go:33-36 sets authMethod='anonymous' (AuthRPCSECGSS != AuthUnix). ResolveSharePermission at share_permission.go:55 short-circuits allow-with-defaults on nil uid. COMPOUND executes as anonymous without rejection.

### [HIGH] SSRF: client-controlled callback address dialed without host validation · `security` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/callback.go:133`
- **What:** dialCallback resolves callback.Addr via ParseUniversalAddr then passes the result directly to net.Dialer.DialContext with no check on the resolved host. callback.Addr comes from the SETCLIENTID (v4.0) or EXCHANGE_ID (v4.1) request body, fully controlled by the NFS client.
- **Why it matters:** Any authenticated (or unauthenticated, if AUTH_NULL is accepted) NFS client can set its callback address to 169.254.169.254 (cloud IMDS), ::1 (loopback), or any RFC-1918/internal address. The server will TCP-connect to that host and write the CB_NULL probe and later CB_RECALL payloads, enabling port scanning and SSRF against internal services from the server's network identity.
- **Fix:** After ParseUniversalAddr succeeds, resolve the host to net.IP and reject loopback (ip.IsLoopback()), link-local (169.254.0.0/16 and fe80::/10), and optionally RFC-1918 ranges unless an allow-list is configured. Example guard in dialCallback before net.JoinHostPort: parse IP, call ip.IsLoopback() || isLinkLocal(ip) and return error if true.
- **Verified:** Confirmed (same root as idx 4). dialCallback at callback.go:133 passes client-supplied address directly to net.Dialer.DialContext with no host restriction. Both CB_NULL (SendCBNull) and CB_RECALL (SendCBRecall) use this path. Confirmed no validation in ParseUniversalAddr — it only parses format, not address ranges.

### [HIGH] RPCSEC_GSS DESTROY unauthenticated — any observer can evict any context · `security` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/framework.go:851`
- **What:** handleDestroy() deletes the named GSS context with zero authentication. It looks up the handle and calls p.contexts.Delete(cred.Handle) without verifying the call-header MIC or any other credential. The Process() dispatcher (line 413) routes gss_proc=DESTROY directly to handleDestroy, explicitly skipping MIC verification that is mandatory for DATA requests.
- **Why it matters:** An attacker who observes a 16-byte context handle in cleartext TCP traffic (or brute-forces the 2^128 space with repeated attempts on a long-lived server) can forge a DESTROY packet and evict any authenticated session, forcing re-authentication or causing a DoS. RFC 2203 Section 5.3.3.2 requires the verifier MIC to be checked on all non-INIT control messages. Linux sunrpc (svcauth_gss.c) verifies the MIC on DESTROY. Not verifying it breaks the security contract of RPCSEC_GSS.
- **Fix:** Before calling p.contexts.Delete, look up the context and call verifyHeaderMIC(gssCtx.SessionKey, headerPreimage, verifBody). If verification fails, return RPCSEC_GSS_CREDPROBLEM without deleting the context. Pass headerPreimage and verifBody into handleDestroy the same way handleData receives them, and route them through Process().
- **Verified:** Confirmed. handleDestroy at framework.go:851 calls p.contexts.Delete(cred.Handle) with zero authentication. Process() at line 412-413 routes RPCGSSDestroy directly to handleDestroy, bypassing MIC verification performed for DATA requests. RFC 2203 §5.3.3.2 requires verifier MIC on all non-INIT messages. Any observer of a 16-byte handle can evict any GSS context.

### [HIGH] AUTH_NULL / failed AUTH_UNIX parse grants full write access on any non-read-only share · `security` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/auth/share_permission.go:55`
- **What:** ResolveSharePermission returns allow-with-defaults (ReadOnly=false) when uid==nil. A client that sends AUTH_NULL, or whose AUTH_UNIX credential fails to parse (e.g. malformed body), produces handlerCtx.UID=nil in ExtractHandlerContext. That nil UID reaches BuildAuthContextWithMapping → ResolveSharePermission, which short-circuits at line 55 and grants unrestricted read-write access on any share that is not explicitly marked ReadOnly. The NeedsAuth flag in the dispatch table (dispatch_nfs.go lines 29–124) is set on WRITE, SETATTR, CREATE, MKDIR, SYMLINK, REMOVE, RMDIR, RENAME, LINK, COMMIT but is never read in dispatchNFSv3Procedure (dispatch.go line 248–262) or dispatchMount — it is dead metadata. No AUTH_NULL rejection gate exists anywhere between the TCP connection and the individual handler call.
- **Why it matters:** Any unauthenticated NFS client on the network can issue WRITE/CREATE/REMOVE/RENAME RPCs against any writable share. AUTH_UNIX credentials are client-controlled cleartext (no cryptographic binding), so an attacker can also deliberately send AUTH_NULL to avoid the UID lookup path and land on the nil-UID fast path that bypasses all per-user deny rules. Shares whose DefaultPermission is 'none' also rely on the uid!=nil path reaching line 82; with uid==nil the 'none' default is never evaluated.
- **Fix:** In ResolveSharePermission, when uid==nil and identityStore!=nil and share!=nil, treat the caller as a guest and apply the share's DefaultPermission (the same logic at lines 82-90) rather than blindly allowing. Separately, add an auth-flavor gate in dispatchNFSv3Procedure: if procedure.NeedsAuth && handlerCtx.AuthFlavor == rpc.AuthNull { return NFS3ErrAccess reply }. The NeedsAuth field should then be actively enforced or removed.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. ResolveSharePermission at share_permission.go:55: 'if identityStore == nil || share == nil || uid == nil { return result, nil }' returns allow-with-defaults when uid==nil. AUTH_NULL or malformed AUTH_UNIX produces nil UID in ExtractHandlerContext (dispatch_test.go:96 confirms). NeedsAuth flag is defined in dispatch table (dispatch.go:402) but never read or enforced in dispatchNFSv3Procedure (lines 248-262) — it's dead metadata. DefaultPermission='none' shares are also bypassed.

### [HIGH] reclaimLeaseImpl: missing caller-identity check — any client can steal another client's lease during grace · `security` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/reclaim.go:40`
- **What:** reclaimLeaseImpl has no clientID parameter and issues ListLocks with no ClientID filter (line 40). Match is purely on the 16-byte leaseKey (lines 48-56). Any authenticated client who can observe or guess a leaseKey can reclaim another client's lease during the grace window, acquiring that client's Read/Write/Handle caching rights. V4ClientRecoveryRecord.Principal (client_recovery_store.go:39) is documented as a 'lease-stealing guard at reclaim time' but is never consulted here.
- **Why it matters:** Missing authz: RFC 7530 §9.1.4 / RFC 8881 §8.4.2 require that reclaim be restricted to the original client identity (verified via boot verifier + principal). Without the ClientID gate, a malicious client that knows victim's leaseKey (observable on the wire or via GETATTR) reclaims the lease, gains Write caching rights, and then writes corrupt data under the original holder who no longer receives a break notification.
- **Fix:** Add clientID string param to reclaimLeaseImpl and pass it from every call site. Filter the ListLocks query: LockQuery{IsLease: &isLease, ClientID: clientID}. After matching leaseKey, assert pl.ClientID == clientID and return ErrLockNotFound on mismatch. For NFSv4.1 reclaim also retrieve the matching V4ClientRecoveryRecord and verify the incoming principal matches V4ClientRecoveryRecord.Principal before granting reclaim.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: reclaim.go:40 ListLocks uses LockQuery{IsLease:&isLease} with no ClientID filter. Lines 48-56 match purely on leaseKey bytes. No Principal/ClientID gate anywhere in reclaimLeaseImpl. Any client knowing leaseKey reclaims another client's lease.

### [HIGH] NSM MonName KV key injection: attacker-controlled MonName pollutes Badger prefix scan → unintended lock/registration deletion · `security` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/badger/clients.go:76`
- **What:** The NSM SM_MON handler (internal/adapter/nfs/nsm/handlers/mon.go:70) accepts `mon.MonID.MonName` directly from the network (unauthenticated XDR field) and stores it unescaped into the Badger secondary-index key at line 76: `nsm:monname:<MonName>:<clientID>`. `DeleteClientRegistrationsByMonName` (line 251) builds the prefix as `nsm:monname:<monName>:` and scans it; no length/character validation is applied to monName before either operation.
- **Why it matters:** A network NFS client can send SM_MON with a crafted `mon_name` containing `:` (e.g. `legithost:victimClientID`). The stored key becomes `nsm:monname:legithost:victimClientID:<attackerClientID>`. Later, `DeleteClientRegistrationsByMonName(ctx, "legithost")` scans prefix `nsm:monname:legithost:`, which matches both real `legithost` entries AND the attacker-planted entry, causing unintended deletion of `victimClientID`'s registration. This breaks NFS lock-recovery for that client (their SM_NOTIFY callbacks and file-lock state are silently wiped). The scan also incorrectly extracts `clientID` via `strings.TrimPrefix` leaving the attacker-injected suffix as the extracted ID (line 262), causing a subsequent `deleteClientRegistrationTx` on a non-existent or wrong client. NSM has no authentication — any NFS-reachable host can trigger this.
- **Fix:** Sanitize or encode `MonName` before embedding in Badger keys. Options: (a) hex-encode or URL-encode MonName in the key (`hex.EncodeToString([]byte(reg.MonName))`), keeping the decode symmetric in the extractor; (b) use a length-prefixed key format so the separator is not ambiguous; (c) reject MonName values containing `:` in the XDR decoder (RFC 1094 §A.2 restricts mon_name to hostname chars — no colon). The same discipline should be applied to `clientID` in the `nsm:client:` primary key and to `FileID`/`OwnerID`/`ClientID` in the lock secondary index keys (locks.go:84,90,96).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: badger/clients.go:76 key is prefixNSMByMonName+reg.MonName+":"+reg.ClientID. DeleteClientRegistrationsByMonName line 251 scans prefix prefixNSMByMonName+monName+":". MonName containing ":victimID" (e.g. "legithost:victimClientID") plants a key matched by the victim's prefix scan, causing unintended deletion of victimClientID's registration. No character validation on MonName before storage.

### [HIGH] DSN parameter injection via unquoted ConnectionString() · `security` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/config.go:122`
- **What:** ConnectionString() builds libpq key=value DSN via fmt.Sprintf with no quoting of Host, Port, Database, User, Password, or SSLMode values. pgx's libpq parser splits on whitespace and equals signs. A Password (or any other field) containing a space followed by a keyword (e.g. 'mypass sslmode=disable') injects a new DSN parameter that overrides the one already present in the string.
- **Why it matters:** Config values come from operator YAML or env vars (DITTOFS_* prefix via viper). A compromised config file, Kubernetes Secret, or env injection allows bypassing the intended sslmode (e.g. forcing sslmode=disable even when the operator wrote sslmode=verify-full), disabling TLS for the metadata store connection. This is a classic libpq DSN injection pattern; pgx's parseKeywordValueSettings confirms it splits on unquoted whitespace.
- **Fix:** Use URL-format DSN (postgres://user:pass@host:port/db?sslmode=...) which naturally percent-encodes special chars, or quote each value with single-quotes and escape internal single-quotes/backslashes per libpq rules. Simplest fix: replace fmt.Sprintf with url.URL construction: u := &url.URL{Scheme: "postgres", User: url.UserPassword(c.User, c.Password), Host: fmt.Sprintf("%s:%d", c.Host, c.Port), Path: c.Database}; q := u.Query(); q.Set("sslmode", c.SSLMode); ... u.RawQuery = q.Encode(); return u.String(). pgxpool.ParseConfig accepts URL format.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: ConnectionString() at config.go:121-132 is plain fmt.Sprintf with no quoting of any field. Password containing space+keyword (e.g. "pass sslmode=disable") injects extra DSN params parsed by libpq/pgx. Can override sslmode or other security-relevant params from operator config/env.

### [HIGH] Postgres metadata store TLS disabled by factory default · `security` · area: controlplane-runtime-shares
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/init.go:113`
- **What:** `CreateMetadataStoreFromConfig` sets `pgCfg.SSLMode = "disable"` when the operator config blob omits a `sslmode` key. `NewPostgresMetadataStore` calls `ApplyDefaults()` which only writes `"prefer"` when the field is empty — but `"disable"` is not empty, so the safe default never fires. All metadata traffic (auth credentials, file paths, ACLs, lock state) traverses the network in plaintext.
- **Why it matters:** Hardcoded insecure default overrides the struct's own safe default (`prefer`). An attacker on the same network segment can passively read or actively MITM all metadata store traffic, stealing credentials and ACL data or injecting rogue metadata.
- **Fix:** Remove the hardcoded `"disable"` fallback. Let the field stay empty so `ApplyDefaults()` sets `"prefer"`, or explicitly set `pgCfg.SSLMode = "prefer"` to match the struct contract. Document that operators who need no-TLS must explicitly set `sslmode: disable` in their config.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: init.go:113 hardcodes pgCfg.SSLMode="disable" when sslmode key absent. ApplyDefaults only sets "prefer" when SSLMode=="" (empty). "disable" is non-empty so safe default never fires. All metadata traffic goes plaintext by default.

### [HIGH] Netgroup hostname access control bypassed via attacker-controlled PTR records · `security` · area: controlplane-runtime-shares
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/netgroups.go:205`
- **What:** `matchHostname` authorizes NFS mount access by performing a reverse DNS lookup (`net.LookupAddr`) on the connecting client IP and comparing the returned PTR hostname against the netgroup pattern. PTR records are controlled by whoever manages the reverse-DNS zone for that IP block — in cloud or co-lo environments this is the tenant, not the operator.
- **Why it matters:** An attacker who controls their own PTR record (e.g. on any cloud provider where reverse DNS is self-service) can set it to `host.allowed-domain.example.com` and gain access to any share whose netgroup uses a `hostname`-type member or `*.example.com` wildcard. This is a classic reverse-DNS spoofing bypass for network access control.
- **Fix:** Either (a) remove hostname-type netgroup members entirely and document that only IP/CIDR entries are safe, or (b) after resolving the PTR hostname, perform a forward DNS lookup of that hostname and verify it resolves back to the connecting IP (forward-confirmed reverse DNS, FCrDNS) before accepting the match. Document that PTR-only matching is insecure.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: netgroups.go:204 matchHostname calls pkgDNSCache.lookupAddr (reverse PTR only), then string-matches against the pattern. No forward-confirmed reverse DNS. Cloud tenant controlling PTR can set it to an allowed-domain hostname and gain mount access.

### [HIGH] Unauthenticated IPC$ access via SessionID=0 bypass · `security` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/response.go:344`
- **What:** prepareDispatch skips ALL session validation when reqHeader.SessionID==0 (condition: cmd.NeedsSession && reqHeader.SessionID != 0). handleIPCShare then calls GetSession(0) which always returns the pre-allocated anonymous session (ID 0, created unconditionally in NewManager). The !found guard never fires, so any client that sends TREE_CONNECT with SessionID=0 — before completing SESSION_SETUP — is granted an IPC$ tree connection and can subsequently open and use lsarpc (SID-to-name resolution) and srvsvc (full share enumeration) pipes without authenticating.
- **Why it matters:** The anonymous session at ID 0 is pre-created in session/manager.go:47 and is never deleted. It satisfies the GetSession lookup in handleIPCShare. The intent of the SessionID!=0 guard is to handle pre-auth credit tracking, but it has the side effect of making every NeedsSession=true command (TREE_CONNECT, CREATE, READ, WRITE, …) reachable without a valid authenticated session when the client sets SessionID=0. An attacker can leak share names and resolve SIDs for any UID/GID without credentials.
- **Fix:** In handleIPCShare (tree_connect.go ~line 276), after GetSession succeeds, add: if sess.IsNull || sess.IsGuest { return NewErrorResult(types.StatusAccessDenied), nil } to reject unauthenticated/null sessions from IPC$. Alternatively, add a dedicated SessionID==0 early-reject in prepareDispatch for all commands except NEGOTIATE, SESSION_SETUP, and ECHO which legitimately arrive with no session.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: response.go:344 gate is "if cmd.NeedsSession && reqHeader.SessionID != 0" — skips auth check entirely when SessionID=0. handleIPCShare at tree_connect.go:276 calls GetSession(ctx.SessionID) where ctx.SessionID=0. manager.go:47-48 unconditionally creates and stores anonymous session at ID 0 in NewManagerWithStrategy. GetSession(0) returns found=true, non-nil session. IPC$ tree connect granted. Client can then open lsarpc/srvsvc pipes without authenticating.

### [HIGH] DESTROY_SESSION missing caller-ownership authz — any client can destroy any session · `security` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/v41/handlers/destroy_session.go:28`
- **What:** HandleDestroySession decodes args.SessionID from the wire and calls StateManager.DestroySession(args.SessionID) with zero check that the requesting client owns that session. DESTROY_SESSION is session-exempt (no SEQUENCE required), so any NFS client with network access can send a DESTROY_SESSION targeting another client's SessionId4.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 8881 §18.37.3 states: 'If the session is owned by a client that is not the same as the client that sent the request, the server MUST return NFS4ERR_NOT_SAME.' Missing authz lets a hostile client tear down any active session once it learns or brute-forces the 16-byte session ID (e.g., via CB_SEQUENCE logging, pcap, or enumeration). Denial-of-service against all connected NFSv4.1 clients is trivially achievable from any unauthenticated NFS connection.
- **Fix:** Before calling StateManager.DestroySession, verify the requesting client owns the target session. For SEQUENCE-bearing compounds, extract ClientID from the SEQUENCE slot; for session-exempt DESTROY_SESSION sent standalone, require the DESTROY_SESSION args include the owning ClientID (RFC 8881 §18.37.1: dsa_sessionid is the only arg) and cross-check it against the session record. In StateManager.destroySessionLocked, accept an optional callerClientID and return NFS4ERR_NOT_SAME when session.ClientID != callerClientID. Pass ctx.ClientState.ClientID (set during EXCHANGE_ID / CREATE_SESSION on that connection) as the caller identity.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: destroy_session.go:28 calls d.StateManager.DestroySession(args.SessionID) with zero ownership check. No comparison of requesting client identity against session owner. Any NFS client with network access can tear down any session by known/guessed SessionId4.

### [HIGH] READ handler bypasses file permission check — any client with a valid handle reads arbitrary file content · `security` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/read.go:101`
- **What:** Handler.Read never calls GetCachedAuthContext, BuildAuthContextWithMapping, or any permission check. It resolves the block store, calls getFileOrError (plain ctx, no auth), then reads content via common.ReadFromBlockStore — all without consulting the caller's UID/GID or file mode/ACL. The service exposes PrepareRead(*AuthContext, FileHandle) which enforces read permission; it is never called from this handler.
- **Why it matters:** Any NFS client that has obtained a file handle (e.g. via LOOKUP on a world-executable directory) can READ the file's bytes regardless of owner, mode bits (e.g. 0600), ACLs, or ShareReadOnly flag. This completely voids DAC enforcement for reads. An attacker NFS-mounting a share as UID=1001 can read root-owned 0600 files if they know or can guess the file handle.
- **Fix:** Call metaSvc.PrepareRead(authCtx, fileHandle) after building authCtx via h.GetCachedAuthContext(ctx), and propagate NFS3ErrAcces on permission denial. Pattern from WRITE: build authCtx first, then call the permission-checking service method before accessing block store.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: read.go never calls PrepareRead (which does checkReadPermission at io.go:540) or any auth/permission check. getFileOrError is a plain GetFile with no auth context. After file-type check, goes directly to ReadFromBlockStore. DAC enforcement completely absent for NFSv3 reads.

### [HIGH] NSM SM_MON stores client-supplied callback hostname used for outbound TCP dial (SSRF) · `security` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nsm/handlers/mon.go:65`
- **What:** mon.MonID.MyID.MyName (a fully client-controlled string from the SM_MON wire request) is stored verbatim as lock.NSMCallback.Hostname at line 65. That value is later passed to callback/client.go:Client.Send as the addr parameter and dialed as TCP at callback/client.go:98 (`dialer.DialContext(callbackCtx, "tcp", addr)`). No validation, no allowlist, no RFC-1918 block. The same path applies to the server-restart notify loop in nsm/callback/notify.go:44-57.
- **Why it matters:** SSRF: any NFS client that can reach the NSM port can register my_name=<internal-IP:port> and cause the server to open a TCP connection to arbitrary targets on the internal network whenever an SM_NOTIFY is dispatched. With prog/vers/proc also client-controlled, the server will send a crafted RPC payload to the target.
- **Fix:** Validate MyName against the client's own source IP on registration (i.e. require MyName resolves to / equals ctx.ClientAddr's IP), or restrict to IP-only form and reject hostnames that are not the registering client's address. At minimum, block RFC-1918 / loopback / link-local destinations before dialing in Client.Send.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: mon.go:65 stores mon.MonID.MyID.MyName (fully client-controlled wire field) verbatim into lock.NSMCallback{Hostname:...}. callback/notify.go:44 passes reg.CallbackInfo.Hostname as addr to client.Send. client.go:98 dials dialer.DialContext(callbackCtx, "tcp", addr) with no RFC-1918 block, no allowlist, no validation. prog/vers/proc also client-controlled. Classic SSRF from any NFS-reachable host.

### [HIGH] SSRF + plaintext S3 traffic via unvalidated http:// endpoint · `security` · area: block-remote-s3-encryption-compression
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/remote/s3/store.go:183`
- **What:** normalizeEndpoint passes through any URL with a recognized scheme unchanged, including http://. An admin who supplies endpoint=http://169.254.169.254/... or any internal http:// URL causes the AWS SDK to issue unauthenticated HTTP requests to that host — SSRF. Block data also travels in plaintext regardless of whether the encryption decorator is stacked above.
- **Why it matters:** Line 189-192: when strings.Index(endpoint,'://') > 0 and isValidScheme passes, function returns endpoint verbatim. No scheme whitelist exists. The field flows from user-controlled REST API config (internal/controlplane/api/handlers/block_stores.go Create/Update handlers) directly to s3.NewFromConfig at service.go:2030 and blockstoreprobe/probe.go:196 with no further validation. AWS SDK v2 honors a BaseEndpoint with an http:// scheme and will issue HTTP GET/PUT to it.
- **Fix:** In normalizeEndpoint, reject non-https schemes: after the isValidScheme check, add `if !strings.EqualFold(scheme, "https") { return "", fmt.Errorf("s3 endpoint scheme %q not allowed; use https") }`. Return an error from normalizeEndpoint (change signature to (string, error)) and propagate through NewFromConfig. For Localstack/MinIO dev use, allow http:// only when an explicit AllowInsecure bool is set in Config and the build tag is not production.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. normalizeEndpoint at store.go:189-192: isValidScheme('http') returns true (RFC 3986 valid), so http:// endpoint passes unchanged to s3.Options.BaseEndpoint at store.go:165. AWS SDK v2 honors http:// BaseEndpoint and issues plaintext HTTP. No scheme whitelist exists. endpoint flows from user-controlled REST config via blockstoreprobe/probe.go:196. Fix: whitelist 'https' only, or document that http:// is only for local dev and add a config-level warning.

### [HIGH] SSRF + internal-network probe via metadata store Create endpoint · `security` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/metadata_stores.go:86`
- **What:** POST /api/v1/store/metadata calls `runtime.CreateMetadataStoreFromConfig` with fully admin-controlled `type` and `config` (host, port, sslmode) before persisting. For type=postgres the server opens a TCP connection to the caller-supplied host:port; for type=badger it calls `pathutil.ExpandPath` + `badger.NewBadgerMetadataStoreWithDefaults` on a caller-supplied filesystem path. The raw `err.Error()` from these calls is returned in the 400 response body (line 90).
- **Why it matters:** Admin can point the server at any internal address (cloud metadata endpoint 169.254.169.254, internal DB, k8s API) and observe TCP reachability + connection error text (cert details, banner, timeout vs refused) in the response. Combines SSRF with internal network enumeration and internal error detail disclosure. The `badger` path allows confirming or reading partial data from arbitrary on-disk paths the server process can access.
- **Fix:** Separate validation (structural only — type allow-list, required fields present, path absolute) from instantiation. Do NOT open network connections or file handles during config validation in the Create handler. Move the actual `CreateMetadataStoreFromConfig` call to a post-persist async probe, or at minimum strip err.Error() from the 400 response body and log internally only. For postgres, validate that host is not a link-local / loopback / RFC-1918 address if the deployment policy forbids it.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. metadata_stores.go:86-90: CreateMetadataStoreFromConfig opens TCP to caller-supplied type+config (postgres host:port, badger path) before persisting; err.Error() returned verbatim in 400 body at line 90. Admin can probe internal addresses (169.254.169.254, internal DB) and read TCP reachability + error text (cert details, banner, timeout vs refused). badger path allows confirming on-disk paths. Fix: sanitize error before returning; add host allowlist or network policy.

### [HIGH] No request body size limit — OOM/DoS on all JSON endpoints · `security` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/helpers.go:187`
- **What:** `decodeJSONBody` passes `r.Body` directly to `json.NewDecoder(...).Decode(v)` with no `http.MaxBytesReader` guard. Every POST/PUT/PATCH handler (login, create user, create share, create block store, create metadata store, update settings, etc.) is affected. The server's `ReadTimeout` (default 10 s, config.go:197) limits wall-clock time but not bytes read; a slow-sender can stream gigabytes within that window.
- **Why it matters:** Unauthenticated endpoints (POST /api/v1/auth/login, POST /api/v1/auth/refresh) are reachable without a token. A client sending a multi-GB JSON body to /login causes the Go JSON decoder to buffer arbitrarily large input, exhausting server memory. Authenticated endpoints are also affected for any compromised or malicious admin.
- **Fix:** Wrap `r.Body` with `http.MaxBytesReader(w, r.Body, maxBodyBytes)` at the top of `decodeJSONBody` (or in a router-level middleware). A conservative limit like 1 MiB covers all legitimate control-plane payloads; snapshot/restore bodies are already small structs.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. helpers.go:187: json.NewDecoder(r.Body).Decode(v) with no http.MaxBytesReader guard. Grep for MaxBytesReader/MaxBytesHandler across entire codebase returns zero results. ReadTimeout=10s limits wall-clock not bytes. Unauthenticated POST /api/v1/auth/login can stream multi-GB JSON body within 10s window on slow sender. Fix: wrap r.Body with http.MaxBytesReader(w, r.Body, maxBodyBytes) in decodeJSONBody.

### [HIGH] NLM lock owner identity taken entirely from unauthenticated wire fields · `security` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/lock.go:91`
- **What:** buildOwnerID assembles the lock OwnerID from wire fields CallerName, Svid, and OH (owner handle). handleNLMProcedure in pkg/adapter/nfs/handlers.go:198-253 only parses AUTH_UNIX credentials into ctx.UID — it never validates that the wire CallerName matches the authenticated credential, and with AUTH_NULL ctx.UID is nil. The ownerID goes directly into LockFileNLM / UnlockFileNLM.
- **Why it matters:** Any client can send NLM_LOCK with CallerName set to a victim hostname to acquire locks attributed to that host, or send NLM_UNLOCK / NLM_CANCEL with the victim's CallerName and known OH to release/cancel the victim's locks. AUTH_UNIX CallerName is also trivially spoofable because it is not verified. This allows lock poisoning and lock denial-of-service for any NFS client.
- **Fix:** Bind the NLM OwnerID to the authenticated transport address (TCP source IP) rather than the wire CallerName. For AUTH_UNIX, cross-check that the wire CallerName is consistent with the credential UID or source IP. Reject NLM requests arriving with AUTH_NULL from untrusted source ranges, or enforce host-based access lists at mount time.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. lock.go:91: buildOwnerID uses wire-supplied CallerName, Svid, OH with no binding to authenticated credential. handlers.go:198-222: AUTH_NULL sets ctx.UID=nil; AUTH_UNIX CallerName is trivially spoofable (not verified against source IP). Any client can send NLM_LOCK/UNLOCK/CANCEL with forged CallerName to acquire or release victim locks. Fix: bind ownerID to source IP:port + file handle at lock acquisition; reject CallerName-only identity when credential is AUTH_NULL.

### [HIGH] SSRF via attacker-controlled server-url in operator credentials Secret · `security` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/adapter_reconciler.go:59`
- **What:** getAuthenticatedClient reads `server-url` from the operator credentials Secret and passes it verbatim as the HTTP base URL. The operator holds `secrets: ...patch;delete` on its namespace (RBAC marker line 102 in dittoserver_controller.go). Any principal with that permission (or who can escalate to it) can overwrite the Secret's `server-url` to an arbitrary address — internal cluster services, cloud metadata endpoint (169.254.169.254), or external. The operator will then send a Bearer token-authenticated DELETE /api/v1/users request to the attacker-controlled URL, leaking the operator service-account JWT.
- **Why it matters:** server-url is stored in a mutable K8s Secret; operator RBAC grants itself Secret write. No scheme, host, or port validation before use in http.NewRequestWithContext. Attacker controls destination; Bearer token is forwarded unconditionally (dittofs_client.go line 124).
- **Fix:** Derive the target URL exclusively from the live CR spec via ds.GetAPIServiceURL() instead of trusting the stored server-url. Remove server-url from the credentials Secret entirely; recompute it on each request from the immutable CR spec, which is admission-webhook-validated and namespace-scoped.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. adapter_reconciler.go:59-72: serverURL read from credSecret.Data['server-url'] verbatim; newAPIClient performs no URL scheme/host validation. dittofs_client.go:115: c.baseURL+path passed to http.NewRequestWithContext, Bearer token added at line 124. Operator RBAC at dittoserver_controller.go:102 grants secrets:patch;delete on namespace — attacker with that permission can overwrite server-url to internal cluster address or metadata endpoint. Fix: validate serverURL scheme (https only) and check it matches expected service hostname before use.

### [HIGH] Admin bootstrap password logged to structured logger (credential in logs) · `security` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfs/commands/start.go:115`
- **What:** `logger.Info("Admin user created", "username", "admin", "password", adminPassword)` emits the plaintext admin password as a structured log field at INFO level. If `logging.output` is a file (or a log-drain/SIEM), the credential is persisted there.
- **Why it matters:** First-run credential must never appear in logs — only in the operator's terminal (stdout). Logging it at INFO means any log rotation, remote syslog, or log-aggregation pipeline captures the bootstrap password. An attacker with log read access gets full admin credentials.
- **Fix:** Remove the `password` key-value pair from the `logger.Info` call. Keep only `fmt.Printf` to stdout (already present on line 116). The comment "It will not be shown again" is already correct for the stdout path — just don't contradict it by writing it to the log.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. start.go:115: logger.Info('Admin user created', 'username', 'admin', 'password', adminPassword) emits plaintext bootstrap password as structured log field at INFO level. Line 116 also prints to stdout (correct). Log-drain/SIEM/file output captures credential. Fix: remove password from logger.Info call; keep only fmt.Printf to stdout.

### [HIGH] UnlockAllForSession(sessionID=0) is a no-op for disconnected handles in ProcessAppInstanceId · `slop` · area: smb-create-open
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/durable_context.go:1033`
- **What:** ProcessAppInstanceId calls metaSvc.UnlockAllForSession(ctx, h.MetadataHandle, 0) with sessionID=0 when displacing persisted durable handles. doUnlockAllForSession filters by existing[i].SessionID == sessionID; real SMB session IDs are non-zero, so the call removes nothing. Byte-range locks from the displaced disconnected session are never released.
- **Why it matters:** The displaced persisted handle's locks were recorded under the original (non-zero) session ID. Passing 0 matches no lock entries. After the AppInstanceId failover, stale byte-range locks from the old session remain in the lock manager for that metadata handle. A subsequent lock or write from the new claimant can block on phantom locks, breaking the Hyper-V failover contract (MS-SMB2 §3.3.5.9.13). Classic AI-slop: plausible placeholder value (0 = 'no session') that is actually a no-op.
- **Fix:** Replace with UnlockAllForOpen keyed on the persisted handle's OriginalFileID: metaSvc.UnlockAllForOpen(ctx, h.MetadataHandle, fmt.Sprintf("%x", h.OriginalFileID)). PersistedDurableHandle already carries OriginalFileID (added by buildPersistedDurableHandle). Fall back to h.FileID when OriginalFileID is zero (pre-field legacy rows).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: durable_context.go:1033 calls UnlockAllForSession(ctx, h.MetadataHandle, 0). manager.go doUnlockAllForSession filters by existing[i].SessionID==sessionID; sessionID=0 never matches. More critically: SMB byte-range locks use OpenID-based cleanup (UnlockAllForOpen), not session-based (per lock/manager.go:1310-1318 comment). Displaced durable handle locks are never released. fix: call UnlockAllForOpen with the handle's OpenID instead.

### [HIGH] SMBAuthenticator validates Type-3 against any pending challenge, not session-specific one · `slop` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/auth/authenticator.go:256`
- **What:** `validateAgainstPendingAuths` iterates ALL pending NTLM challenges with `a.pendingAuths.Range` and accepts any matching challenge. There is no session-ID parameter — the Type-3 from connection A can match the challenge issued to connection B.
- **Why it matters:** NTLM challenge-response must be bound to the specific challenge issued in the same session/connection. Accepting any in-flight challenge breaks the session-binding invariant and allows cross-session replay: if attacker can issue a concurrent NTLM handshake they control the challenge and can authenticate as any user whose Type-3 they relay to this server.
- **Fix:** Thread the session ID (or the specific serverChallenge) from the pending-auth store through to `handleNTLMAuthenticate`, look up the specific `pendingNTLMAuth` by that key, and validate against only that entry — same pattern as the real path in `handlers/session_setup.go` which uses `GetPendingAuth(ctx.SessionID, ctx.ConnID)`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: validateAgainstPendingAuths (line 256) iterates ALL entries in a.pendingAuths with no session/connection parameter. pendingAuths keyed by internal counter; any in-flight challenge can match any Type-3 from any connection. No session binding enforced. Enables NTLM relay cross-connection within the same server instance.

### [HIGH] COPYCHUNK access check uses DesiredAccess (pre-DACL) instead of GrantedAccess (post-DACL) · `slop` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/ioctl_copychunk.go:250`
- **What:** validateCopyChunkAccess reads src.DesiredAccess and dst.DesiredAccess to gate FILE_READ_DATA/FILE_EXECUTE on source and FILE_WRITE_DATA/FILE_APPEND_DATA/FILE_READ_DATA on destination. Every other access check in the SMB handler layer (READ, WRITE, SET_INFO, QUERY_INFO, SET_SPARSE, SET_ZERO_DATA, QUERY_ALLOCATED_RANGES) uses GrantedAccess (post-DACL intersection computed at CREATE).
- **Why it matters:** DesiredAccess is what the client asked for; GrantedAccess is what the DACL actually granted. A MAXIMUM_ALLOWED or GENERIC_ALL open whose DACL strips FILE_READ_DATA still has those bits in DesiredAccess, so the check always passes even when the effective rights are absent. This is the same vulnerability class fixed by #616 (ChangeNotify), explicitly documented in multiple handler comments as 'Gate consults Open.GrantedAccess (post-DACL intersection at CREATE), not the pre-DACL DesiredAccess'.
- **Fix:** Change lines 250–251 from `src.DesiredAccess` / `dst.DesiredAccess` to `src.GrantedAccess` / `dst.GrantedAccess`, and update the fmt.Sprintf log lines on 256, 263, 270 to match. Match the pattern used in handleSetSparse (line 78), handleQueryAllocatedRanges (line 161), and handleSetZeroData (line 392).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: ioctl_copychunk.go:250-251 uses src.DesiredAccess and dst.DesiredAccess. Every other handler uses GrantedAccess (post-DACL). auth_priming_test.go explicitly documents this as bug class B. DesiredAccess=MAXIMUM_ALLOWED bypasses DACL stripping.

### [HIGH] reapExpiredSessions leaks BackchannelSender goroutines on lease expiry · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:2644`
- **What:** Lines 2644–2648 delete expired-client sessions from sessionsByID/sessionsByClientID directly, then call purgeV41Client (line 2665) which also deletes map entries directly. Neither path calls stopBackchannelSender. The BackchannelSender goroutine (started by StartBackchannelSender) only terminates on Stop() or context cancellation — neither happens here. Shutdown() at line 842 iterates sessionsByID to stop senders, but by then those sessions are already deleted.
- **Why it matters:** Goroutine without lifecycle/cancellation (Go best-practice violation). Every v4.1 client whose lease expires at runtime leaks its BackchannelSender goroutine. Under steady NFS workload (clients reconnecting across lease periods) this accumulates unboundedly. The goroutine holds a *BackchannelSender (containing a channel + references to StateManager) preventing GC.
- **Fix:** In reapExpiredSessions, replace the direct session-delete loop (lines 2644–2648) with calls to sm.destroySessionLocked(session.SessionID, true, "lease_expired") for each session — this already calls stopBackchannelSender. Alternatively, in purgeV41Client, iterate sm.sessionsByClientID[record.ClientID] and call sm.stopBackchannelSender(session.SessionID) before deleting from the maps.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: reapExpiredSessions (manager.go:2645-2648) deletes session entries from sessionsByID/sessionsByClientID directly without calling stopBackchannelSender. purgeV41Client (v41_client.go:322-323) also deletes without stopping senders. DestroySession (line 2537-2538) correctly calls stopBackchannelSender first — reapExpiredSessions bypasses that path. Shutdown iterates sessionsByID which is already empty for reaped sessions, missing those goroutines.

### [HIGH] Map write under RLock in isRecentlyRecalled causes data race · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/delegation.go:695`
- **What:** `isRecentlyRecalled` calls `delete(sm.recentlyRecalled, fhKey)` (lazy TTL cleanup) while `ShouldGrantDelegation` holds only `sm.mu.RLock()`. Multiple concurrent goroutines can hold RLock simultaneously, so two concurrent `ShouldGrantDelegation` calls — or one `ShouldGrantDelegation` and any read-locked operation that incidentally calls `isRecentlyRecalled` — produce a concurrent map write, triggering a Go data race detector panic and undefined behaviour.
- **Why it matters:** Go maps are not goroutine-safe for mixed read/write access. `sync.RWMutex.RLock` allows multiple concurrent readers; a `delete` while any other reader holds RLock is a concurrent write. `go test -race` will catch this as a DATA RACE on `sm.recentlyRecalled`.
- **Fix:** Remove the lazy delete from `isRecentlyRecalled`. Either (a) call it only from paths that hold `sm.mu.Lock()` (e.g. `GrantDelegation`, `RevokeDelegation`, `CheckDelegationConflict`) and keep the lazy cleanup there, or (b) run a periodic cleanup goroutine. For the read-only check path, just return `true`/`false` without modifying the map: remove lines 695-696 (`delete(sm.recentlyRecalled, fhKey); return false`) and simply `return false` when TTL expired — let the write-lock paths prune stale entries.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: delegation.go:695 calls delete(sm.recentlyRecalled, fhKey) while ShouldGrantDelegation holds only sm.mu.RLock() (line 406-407). The docstring 'Caller must hold sm.mu (RLock or Lock)' is incorrect for a write operation. Concurrent RLock holders can race on the map write. Go data race detector will panic.

### [HIGH] CB_SEQUENCE seqid skips every other value — RFC 8881 §20.9 violation · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/backchannel.go:270`
- **What:** `sendCallback` calls `bs.nextXID.Add(1)` twice: once at line 270 for `seqID` (used in CB_SEQUENCE) and again at line 284 for `xid` (RPC XID). Both are drawn from the same `atomic.Uint32` counter, so every call increments it by 2. Slot-0 CB_SEQUENCE seqids are 1, 3, 5, 7… instead of 1, 2, 3, 4…. RFC 8881 §20.9 (CB_SEQUENCE4args) requires the server to use a value exactly one greater than the last value sent on that slot. Linux `nfsd` and macOS kernel clients enforce this; a non-incrementing-by-one seqid results in `NFS4ERR_SEQ_MISORDERED` and the callback is rejected.
- **Why it matters:** Two logically independent counters — CB_SEQUENCE per-slot seqid and RPC XID — share one `atomic.Uint32`. The double-Add per call is a design mistake: seqid must advance by 1 per slot use (RFC 8881 §2.10.6.3), while XID only needs uniqueness per outstanding call.
- **Fix:** Use two separate counters: a dedicated `cbSeqID atomic.Uint32` for CB_SEQUENCE seqids and keep `nextXID` for RPC XIDs only. Change line 270 to `seqID := bs.cbSeqID.Add(1)` and add `cbSeqID atomic.Uint32` to the `BackchannelSender` struct. This gives monotonically-increasing-by-1 seqids while XIDs remain independently unique.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: backchannel.go:270 seqID=bs.nextXID.Add(1) then line 284 xid=bs.nextXID.Add(1) — same atomic counter incremented twice per sendCallback call. seqids sent are 1,3,5,7... instead of 1,2,3,4... RFC 8881 §20.9 requires exactly +1 per slot use. Linux/macOS NFS clients will reject with NFS4ERR_SEQ_MISORDERED.

### [HIGH] ResetLocalState residual sweep non-recursive — misses subdirectory logs · `slop` · area: block-local-fs-rollup-chunk
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/local/fs/drain_reset.go:272`
- **What:** `os.ReadDir(logsDir)` is a single-level scan; the loop at line 274 explicitly skips directories. PayloadIDs like `share1/file.txt` produce logs at `<logsDir>/share1/file.txt.log` — inside a subdirectory. After the live-fd teardown loop (which handles every fd in `sh.logFDs`), the residual sweep is only meant to catch orphaned logs that had no live fd. Those orphaned logs in subdirectories are silently missed.
- **Why it matters:** Doc comment says "removes the on-disk `.log` files under `<baseDir>/logs/`". `recoverAppendLogs` and `cleanupCompactTemps` both use `filepath.WalkDir` for the same reason (comment in `compaction.go:415` explicitly calls out the two-level layout). The test (`TestResetLocalState_DropsStaleLog`) only uses flat payload IDs and never exercises the subdirectory case. On a store with share-prefixed payloads, after `ResetLocalState` an orphaned `logs/<share>/<file>.log` survives on disk. The next boot's `recoverAppendLogs` re-installs it as a live fd, and `replayLogIntoDest` overlays stale post-snapshot bytes on top of the restored CAS content — exactly the C2 silent corruption the function is supposed to prevent.
- **Fix:** Replace `os.ReadDir` + manual loop with `filepath.WalkDir(logsDir, ...)` skipping directories and removing every `.log` file, matching the pattern used by `cleanupCompactTemps` and `recoverAppendLogs`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: logPath() (appendwrite.go:59) uses flat `{baseDir}/logs/{payloadID}.log` where payloadID contains `/` (recovery.go:237-240 comment confirms `<logsDir>/<share>/<file>.log` nested layout). ResetLocalState residual sweep (drain_reset.go:272-282) uses os.ReadDir (single-level) and explicitly skips dirs at line 274. Orphaned nested logs survive. recoverAppendLogs uses filepath.WalkDir for the same reason (recovery.go:229).

### [HIGH] updateDescendantPaths silently discards PutFile error on every descendant write · `slop` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/file_modify.go:829`
- **What:** tx.PutFile error blank-assigned with `_ = tx.PutFile(ctx, child)` inside the path-rewrite loop. Every descendant whose Path update fails is silently skipped.
- **Why it matters:** The caller comment at line 759-761 explicitly states 'Propagate the error: a partial descendant rewrite leaves stale child Paths that diverge from the parent, corrupting the Path-keyed postgres namespace. Roll the rename back instead.' The implementation contradicts the stated invariant. On postgres backend, a rename of any directory with children that hits a transient write error leaves child File.Path values pointing to the old location while the directory entry points to the new one — corrupting the postgres path-keyed namespace permanently. No panic, no error, transaction commits in a broken state.
- **Fix:** Return the error instead of discarding it: `if err := tx.PutFile(ctx, child); err != nil { return fmt.Errorf("update path for %q: %w", child.Path, err) }`
- **Verified:** Confirmed: updateDescendantPaths line 829 is `_ = tx.PutFile(ctx, child)`. Caller comment at file_modify.go:759-761 explicitly states 'Propagate the error: a partial descendant rewrite leaves stale child Paths that diverge from the parent, corrupting the Path-keyed postgres namespace. Roll the rename back instead.' Implementation contradicts stated invariant.

### [HIGH] SetFileAttributes: AtimeNow/MtimeNow boolean flags never applied — UTIME_NOW is a silent no-op · `slop` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/file_modify.go:219`
- **What:** SetAttrs.AtimeNow and SetAttrs.MtimeNow are consumed only in the permission-check branch (onlySettingTimesToNow, line 219-220) but are never used in the attribute-mutation block. The mutation block only handles attrs.Atime != nil (line 387) and attrs.Mtime != nil (line 392). NFS/SMB callers signalling UTIME_NOW pass AtimeNow=true with Atime=nil, so neither branch fires and the timestamp is never updated.
- **Why it matters:** POSIX utimensat(UTIME_NOW) and NFSv4 SETATTR time_access_set=SET_TO_SERVER_TIME / time_modify_set=SET_TO_SERVER_TIME require the server to stamp the current time. DittoFS accepts the SETATTR (permission check passes correctly via onlySettingTimesToNow), returns success, but leaves file.Atime and file.Mtime unchanged. NFS clients relying on server-side timestamp updates (e.g. after O_RDWR write without explicit mtime) see stale timestamps.
- **Fix:** After the existing attrs.Atime/attrs.Mtime blocks add:
  if attrs.AtimeNow { file.Atime = now; modified = true }
  if attrs.MtimeNow { file.Mtime = now; modified = true }
- **Verified:** Confirmed: AtimeNow/MtimeNow appear only at lines 220 and 224 (permission-check branch). Mutation block at lines 387-405 only handles `attrs.Atime != nil` and `attrs.Mtime != nil`. No code path sets file.Atime/file.Mtime to `now` when AtimeNow=true/MtimeNow=true with nil Atime/Mtime. UTIME_NOW is silent no-op.

### [HIGH] scanExpiredLeaseBreaks uses AcquiredAt (grant time) instead of break-start time for timeout computation · `slop` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/oplock_break.go:274`
- **What:** breakDeadline computed as pl.AcquiredAt.Add(timeout). Comment on line 273 claims 'AcquiredAt is updated when break initiated' — fabricated: no code path ever updates AcquiredAt on break initiation. applyBreakStageLocked writes BreakStarted=time.Now() (manager.go:2671) on the in-memory OpLock, but BreakStarted is explicitly 'runtime-only, not persisted' (store.go:434). AcquiredAt in PersistedLock maps to UnifiedLock.AcquiredAt, set at grant time and never changed.
- **Why it matters:** Any lease held longer than the break timeout (35s default) before a break is initiated has an AcquiredAt-derived deadline already in the past. The scanner will force-revoke such leases on the very next 1-second scan tick, treating a correctly-responding client as having timed out. Leases on long-lived open files are the common case.
- **Fix:** Add a BreakStartedAt field to PersistedLock (store.go), populate it in ToPersistedLock from lock.Lease.BreakStarted when Breaking=true, restore it in FromPersistedLock, and use pl.BreakStartedAt in the deadline calculation. Drop the false AcquiredAt-update comment.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: oplock_break.go:274 uses pl.AcquiredAt (persisted, set at grant time per store.go:69-70). BreakStarted=time.Now() set in manager.go:2671 but store.go:434 marks it 'runtime-only, not persisted'. Comment in oplock_break.go:273 'AcquiredAt is updated when break initiated' is false — no code path ever updates AcquiredAt on break.

### [HIGH] accessModesConflict logic contradicts doc: requires BOTH modes non-None, so existing deny-mode holders never block None-mode openers · `slop` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/types.go:354`
- **What:** accessModesConflict returns true only when both a != AccessModeNone && b != AccessModeNone. Doc says 'Any deny mode (DenyRead, DenyWrite, DenyAll) conflicts with any non-None mode on the other side' — the implementation contradicts this. existing=DenyWrite, new=None returns false (no conflict), meaning an open with share-deny-write does not block a subsequent None opener.
- **Why it matters:** Share-deny semantics in SMB: a holder with AccessModeDenyWrite should prevent new opens that want write access, regardless of the new opener's own deny flags. The AND condition means the check is effectively a no-op whenever any side opens with AccessModeNone, which is the default for most opens. ConflictsWith relies entirely on this for case 1 (access mode conflicts).
- **Fix:** The correct check is asymmetric: existing's deny mode constrains what the new opener can request. Replace with: 'return (a == AccessModeDenyRead || a == AccessModeDenyAll) && (b needs read) || (a == AccessModeDenyWrite || a == AccessModeDenyAll) && (b needs write)' — or at minimum 'return a != AccessModeNone || b != AccessModeNone' to match the doc description.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: accessModesConflict (types.go:353-354) returns `a != AccessModeNone && b != AccessModeNone` — requires BOTH non-None. Doc at lines 350-352 says 'Any deny mode (DenyRead, DenyWrite, DenyAll) conflicts with any non-None mode on the other side' — implementation contradicts doc. existing=DenyWrite, new=None returns false (no conflict).

### [HIGH] memory DeleteShare skips usedBytes update and objectIndex cleanup · `slop` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/memory/shares.go:134`
- **What:** Direct-store `DeleteShare` deletes all files for the share without adjusting `store.usedBytes` (atomic counter) and without removing their entries from `store.objectIndex`. The transactional counterpart at transaction.go:639 does both correctly via `tx.pendingDelta` and explicit `delete(tx.store.objectIndex, ...)` calls.
- **Why it matters:** After a share is deleted via the non-transactional path (called by storetest and any caller that invokes the `metadata.Store` surface directly), `usedBytes` is permanently over-reported by the deleted files' sizes, and stale ObjectID→handle entries remain in `objectIndex`. A later `FindByObjectID` for a recycled ObjectID can collide with the orphaned entry and return a false hit or a spurious ErrConflict from `PutFile`.
- **Fix:** Delegate to `WithTransaction`: `return store.WithTransaction(ctx, func(tx metadata.Transaction) error { return tx.DeleteShare(ctx, shareName) })`. The tx version already handles both `pendingDelta` and `objectIndex` cleanup correctly.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: memory/shares.go DeleteShare (lines 151-162) iterates and deletes files but never touches store.usedBytes or store.objectIndex. transaction.go correctly handles both (lines 169, 261, 311, 662). After DeleteShare, usedBytes permanently over-reported and stale objectIndex entries can cause false FindByObjectID hits.

### [HIGH] poolRow leaks connection when Scan never called · `slop` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/pool_helpers.go:174`
- **What:** poolRow.Scan is the ONLY path that calls conn.Release(). queryRow() manually acquires a dedicated pool connection via pool.Acquire(), wraps it in poolRow, then returns. If anything panics between queryRow() and .Scan() — or if a caller discards the returned pgx.Row without scanning — the acquired connection is never returned to the pool. No defer and no finalizer exist as a fallback.
- **Why it matters:** Connection pool exhaustion: each leaked connection permanently reduces pool capacity by one. Under sustained load (e.g. panics in a handler, or callers that short-circuit before scanning) the pool drains and subsequent operations block then time out. The native pgxpool Row returned by conn.QueryRow() internally tracks the connection and releases it on Scan, but the custom poolRow wrapper breaks that lifecycle.
- **Fix:** Add a sync.Once or a deferred release inside poolRow so the connection is always returned. Simplest: store a 'released' flag and call conn.Release() in both Scan and a Close method, or use a runtime.SetFinalizer as a last-resort backstop. Better still, drop the manual Acquire/release pattern and use pgxpool.Pool.QueryRow directly with a context that carries the acquire timeout — pgxpool manages the connection lifecycle internally: 'acquireCtx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, poolConnectionAcquireTimeout); defer cancel(); return s.pool.QueryRow(acquireCtx, sql, args...)'.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: poolRow.Scan (pool_helpers.go:174-178) is the only path calling conn.Release(). queryRow acquires connection via pool.Acquire (line 48) and wraps in poolRow (line 60) with no defer.
