If caller panics between queryRow() and .Scan(), or discards the pgx.Row without scanning, connection leaks permanently.

### [HIGH] Response.Encode silently truncates stub data > 65511 bytes · `slop` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/dcerpc.go:348`
- **What:** When fragLen > MaxFragmentSize (65535), code caps fragLen then allocates buf of that capped size, but copy(buf[24:], r.StubData) silently drops stub bytes beyond offset 65511. FragLength header claims 65535 but actual payload is truncated. No error returned, no fragmentation attempted.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong logic: the 'validate' comment implies safety but produces a malformed single-fragment response. LsarLookupSids with many/long domain names or a large NetrShareEnum response can exceed 65511 stub bytes. Client parses truncated NDR and sees corrupt/garbage data. This is slop — real DCE/RPC requires multi-fragment or a transport-level chunking path, not silent truncation.
- **Fix:** Return an error (or panic) if fragLen > MaxFragmentSize rather than silently capping. Alternatively implement multi-fragment responses. At minimum: if fragLen > MaxFragmentSize { return nil, fmt.Errorf("DCE/RPC response too large: %d bytes", fragLen) } and propagate the error up through HandleRequest/ProcessWrite.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: dcerpc.go:348-371 caps fragLen=65535, allocates buf[65535], then copy(buf[24:], r.StubData) silently drops bytes beyond offset 65511. FragLength header claims 65535 but payload is truncated. No error returned, no fragmentation attempted.

### [HIGH] defaultSIDMapper package-level var read/written without synchronization — data race · `slop` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/security.go:107`
- **What:** defaultSIDMapper is a package-level *sid.SIDMapper var. SetSIDMapper (line 112) writes it; BuildSecurityDescriptor, principalToSID, ParseSecurityDescriptorWithOptions (lines 156, 282, 437, 447, 556) read it during concurrent request handling. No mutex or atomic protects the pointer.
- **Why it matters:** Go memory model requires synchronization for concurrent read/write to the same variable. Any test with t.Parallel() or any server that calls SetSIDMapper after Serve() starts will trigger a data race detectable by -race. The comment 'Must be called before any connections are accepted' is not enforced. AI-slop: the SetSIDMapper nil-guard looks safety-conscious but the actual race is on the pointer assignment itself.
- **Fix:** Replace the bare var with a sync/atomic or sync.RWMutex-protected accessor. Simplest: use sync/atomic.Pointer[sid.SIDMapper]. Change var to var defaultSIDMapper atomic.Pointer[sid.SIDMapper] and init via defaultSIDMapper.Store(sid.NewSIDMapper(0,0,0)); update SetSIDMapper to call defaultSIDMapper.Store(m); update all reads to defaultSIDMapper.Load().
- **Verified:** Confirmed: defaultSIDMapper is plain var *sid.SIDMapper (security.go:107). SetSIDMapper writes it (line 114) with no lock. Read at lines 156, 282, 298, 437, 447, 556 during concurrent request handling with no mutex/atomic. Comment says 'Must be called before any connections' — not enforced; any test or late-init caller triggers data race.

### [HIGH] leaseTimeSeconds global mutable uint32 — data race with concurrent GETATTR handlers · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/attrs/encode.go:82`
- **What:** Plain `var leaseTimeSeconds uint32` written by SetLeaseTime() and read concurrently by every GETATTR encoding goroutine (lines 326, 554) with no synchronization. Immediately below it, the comment on line 97 explicitly says `fsMaxFileSize/Read/Write` use `atomic.Uint64` *to avoid data races with concurrent GETATTR encoding* — the same race class — but `leaseTimeSeconds` was inconsistently left as a bare global.
- **Why it matters:** Concurrent unsynchronized read+write on a plain Go variable is a data race; `go test -race` will flag it. Under concurrent GETATTR load, reads at lines 326/554 race with writes at line 87.
- **Fix:** Replace `var leaseTimeSeconds uint32` with `var leaseTimeSeconds atomic.Uint32`, update SetLeaseTime to `leaseTimeSeconds.Store(seconds)`, GetLeaseTime to `return leaseTimeSeconds.Load()`, and both read sites to `leaseTimeSeconds.Load()`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: leaseTimeSeconds is plain `var uint32` (encode.go:82). SetLeaseTime() writes it (line 87) without atomic. Read at lines 326 and 554 by concurrent GETATTR encoding goroutines. Lines 97-101 adjacent comment explicitly notes fsMaxFileSize/Read/Write use atomic.Uint64 'to avoid data races with concurrent GETATTR encoding' — leaseTimeSeconds was inconsistently omitted.

### [HIGH] Nil-deref after GetFile error-discard in LINK post-success attr fetch · `slop` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/link.go:239`
- **What:** After successful CreateHardLink, GetFile is called to fetch updated nlink attrs. On error the error is logged with a comment saying 'handle gracefully', but execution falls through unconditionally to `h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &updatedFile.FileAttr)` — dereferencing a nil pointer.
- **Why it matters:** Lines 233-237: `updatedFile, err := metaSvc.GetFile(...)` followed by `if err != nil { logError(...) // Continue }`. No return or guard. Line 239 then does `&updatedFile.FileAttr` which panics when `updatedFile == nil`. Any transient store error or context cancellation after a successful hard-link creation will crash the server process.
- **Fix:** Guard the dereference: `if updatedFile == nil { return &LinkResponse{...NFS3ErrIO...}, nil }`. Or use the pre-fetched fileAttr as fallback: replace line 239 with `var nfsFileAttr *types.NFSFileAttr; if updatedFile != nil { nfsFileAttr = h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &updatedFile.FileAttr) } else { nfsFileAttr = h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &fileAttr.FileAttr) }`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. link.go:233-239: `updatedFile, err := metaSvc.GetFile(...)` — on error logs and falls through with no return/guard. Line 239 `h.convertFileAttrToNFS(fileHandle, &updatedFile.FileAttr)` dereferences nil `updatedFile`. convertFileAttrToNFS takes `*metadata.FileAttr`; `&nilPtr.Field` panics. Any transient store error after successful CreateHardLink crashes server.

### [HIGH] Nil-deref pattern: error-discarding GetFile then unconditional FileAttr dereference in MKDIR (5 sites) · `slop` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/mkdir.go:177`
- **What:** Five sites in mkdir.go use `updatedParentFile, _ := metaSvc.GetFile(ctx.Context, parentHandle)` (ignoring error) immediately followed by `h.convertFileAttrToNFS(parentHandle, &updatedParentFile.FileAttr)`. If GetFile fails — e.g. during context cancellation (line 177 is literally inside a ctx.Context.Err() branch), store error, or handle not found — `updatedParentFile` is nil and `&updatedParentFile.FileAttr` panics.
- **Why it matters:** Lines 177-178, 192-193, 210-211, 268-269, 281-282 all follow the same pattern. The most egregious is line 177 which is inside the `ctx.Context.Err() != nil` branch — GetFile will routinely fail on a cancelled context. This is AI-slop copy-paste: the author intended best-effort WCC but implemented a certain nil-deref.
- **Fix:** Check nil before dereferencing: `if updatedParentFile != nil { wccAfter = h.convertFileAttrToNFS(parentHandle, &updatedParentFile.FileAttr) }`. Same fix needed at all 5 sites. Alternatively use `dirWccPair` which already handles nil safely.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. mkdir.go lines 177-178, 192-193, 210-211, 268-269, 281-282 all use `updatedParentFile, _ := metaSvc.GetFile(...)` then `&updatedParentFile.FileAttr`. nil-deref on GetFile failure. Most egregious is line 177 inside the `ctx.Context.Err() != nil` branch where GetFile on cancelled ctx will routinely return nil.

### [HIGH] Nil-deref pattern: error-discarding GetFile then unconditional FileAttr dereference in LINK WCC error paths (2 sites) · `slop` · area: nfs-v3-handlers

### [HIGH] provisionOperatorAccount logins with wrong (freshly-generated) password after 409 conflict · `slop` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/auth_reconciler.go:250`
- **What:** When CreateUser returns 409 (operator account already exists — e.g. credentials Secret was deleted but DittoFS retained the user), code at line 242 catches the conflict and falls through to Login at line 250 using operatorPassword, the freshly-generated random password from line 232. The existing operator account has a completely different password; this Login call returns 401. isTransientError returns false for 401, so reconcileAuth treats it as a permanent failure, sets Authenticated=False, and the operator is permanently stuck.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong control flow: comment says 'proceed to login' as if the new password applies to the pre-existing account. It does not. The only way a 409 can arrive with no credentials Secret is if the Secret was externally deleted while the DittoFS user persisted. Logging in with an unrelated new password cannot succeed.
- **Fix:** On 409 conflict, delete the existing operator user via the admin token (apiClient.DeleteUser) and then re-create with the freshly-generated password, or alternatively re-use admin-token to reset the password via a PUT/PATCH /api/v1/users/{username} endpoint if available. Simplest safe fix: treat 409 as a re-provision signal — delete + recreate — so the new operatorPassword is authoritative.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_reconciler.go:242-250: 409 conflict branch logs 'already exists, proceeding to login' then calls Login with freshly-generated `operatorPassword` (line 250). Existing account has a different password → Login returns 401 → reconcileAuth treats as permanent failure → operator stuck in Authenticated=False forever. Scenario: operator credentials Secret deleted but DittoFS user persisted. Fix: on 409 either re-read from existing credentials Secret or attempt password reset.

### [HIGH] LoginAsAdmin writes/reads developer's real ~/.config/dfsctl/config.json — no XDG isolation · `slop` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/helpers/cli.go:190`
- **What:** LoginAsAdmin runs `dfsctl login` which writes a JWT token into ~/.config/dfsctl/config.json (or $XDG_CONFIG_HOME/dfsctl/config.json). Then extractTokenFromLogin reads that file back. No XDG_CONFIG_HOME isolation is applied; the developer's real credentials file is overwritten on every test run. context_test.go shows the correct pattern (setupIsolatedCredentials calls t.Setenv("XDG_CONFIG_HOME", t.TempDir())), but LoginAsAdmin — used in 37 test files — never applies it.
- **Why it matters:** Every call to LoginAsAdmin corrupts the real developer credentials. In parallel test runs across 37 test files all talking to different short-lived test servers, entries accumulate indefinitely. More critically, if the developer is logged into a production dfsctl context and runs the e2e suite, their session is overwritten/corrupted.
- **Fix:** Add `t.Setenv("XDG_CONFIG_HOME", t.TempDir())` inside LoginAsAdmin before invoking RunRaw("login", ...). This isolates each test's credentials to a temp dir that is cleaned up automatically.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. LoginAsAdmin (cli.go:190) calls runner.RunRaw("login"...) which invokes real dfsctl binary. extractTokenFromLogin at line 236 reads XDG_CONFIG_HOME from env, falls back to ~/.config. LoginAsAdmin never calls t.Setenv("XDG_CONFIG_HOME", t.TempDir()). The isolation pattern exists only in context_test.go's setupIsolatedCredentials, not in LoginAsAdmin itself. 60 call sites unprotected.


## MED

### [MED] cleanupAndDelete has no synchronization — concurrent callers double-cleanup same handle · `bugs` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/durable_scavenger.go:136`
- **What:** expireHandles (background ticker goroutine) and HandleConflictingOpen/ForceExpireDurableHandle (SMB handler goroutines) can race to call cleanupAndDelete for the same PersistedDurableHandle simultaneously. No mutex or in-flight tracking on the scavenger struct guards this.
- **Why it matters:** Double-unlock of byte-range locks via UnlockAllForSession(sessionID=0) on a handle that a different session already holds. Double block-cache flush is benign but wasteful. Double RemoveFile on a delete-pending file can fail silently or hit a TOCTOU window. The lock double-release is the dangerous path — could release a lock belonging to a new opener that claimed the file after the first unlock.
- **Fix:** Add a sync.Map of in-flight handle IDs: before calling cleanupAndDelete, attempt to Store(h.ID, struct{}{}); if key already present, skip (another goroutine owns it). Delete after cleanup completes. Alternatively serialize all cleanup calls through a single channel.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: durable_scavenger.go cleanupAndDelete (line 136) has no mutex or in-flight tracking. Called from expireHandles ticker goroutine (line 124) and from HandleConflictingOpen (line 223) and ForceExpireDurableHandle (line 205) — both exported methods with no sync. Current callers are not yet wired to handler goroutines, so race is latent but the struct has no guard for concurrent calls on same handle.

### [MED] Nil-deref panic in reconcileContainerPorts: Containers[0] unguarded on re-fetch · `bugs` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/service_reconciler.go:513`
- **What:** `fresh.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[0].Ports = desiredPorts` with no guard on `len(fresh.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers)`. The first fetch at line 440 guards against the empty-containers case, but between that check and the second fetch at line 508 (done for optimistic locking) the StatefulSet could be replaced/recreated with 0 containers, causing an index-out-of-range panic.
- **Why it matters:** Race window between two separate Get calls. The container-count guard at line 450 is on `statefulSet` (first fetch), not on `fresh` (second fetch at line 508). Any reconcile that recreates the StatefulSet in that window produces a panic.
- **Fix:** After the re-fetch at line 508, add `if len(fresh.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers) == 0 { return fmt.Errorf("re-fetched StatefulSet has no containers") }` before line 513.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. service_reconciler.go:450 guards len(statefulSet.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers)==0 on first fetch. Line 513 indexes fresh.Spec.Template.Spec.Containers[0] on the second fetch (line 508) with no equivalent guard. Race window between the two Get calls is real; a reconcile-triggered StatefulSet replacement with 0 containers causes index-out-of-range panic.

### [MED] Lease rollback removes wrong entry when baseName includes ADS stream suffix · `bugs` · area: smb-create-open
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/create_post_break.go:964`
- **What:** When `ErrLeaseKeyInUse` fires after `createAction == types.FileCreated` for an ADS open, the rollback calls `metaSvc.RemoveFile(authCtx, parentHandle, baseName)` where `baseName` is the ADS-qualified name (e.g. `"file.txt:StreamName"`) — that is correct for the stream entry. However, if the base file was auto-created by the ADS creation path (create.go lines 1269-1292) it is NOT rolled back, leaving an orphaned empty base file in the metadata store.
- **Why it matters:** The auto-create of the base file happens unconditionally if the base did not already exist. On lease rejection the stream entry is removed but the base stays. A subsequent `FILE_CREATE` disposition on the same base name then fails with `ErrAlreadyExists` rather than creating cleanly. The base auto-creation block has no corresponding rollback in the lease-rejection path.
- **Fix:** In the `ErrLeaseKeyInUse` / `FileCreated` branch, after removing the stream entry, also check if the base file was just auto-created (i.e. `isADS && adsBaseFileName != ""`) and remove it if it was not already present before this CREATE (save a `baseCreatedByUs bool` flag in the ADS auto-create block).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. create.go:1268-1292 auto-creates base file (adsBaseFileName) before the lease request. Rollback at create_post_break.go:964 calls RemoveFile with baseName (the ADS-qualified name e.g. "file.txt:StreamName") — removes only the stream entry. adsBaseFileName is a local in create.go, not in createDraft; base file orphan is unreachable and unremovable by rollback path. Subsequent FILE_CREATE on base name hits ErrAlreadyExists.

### [MED] Malformed SecurityBuffer silently downgrades to guest session · `bugs` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/session_setup.go:93`
- **What:** parseSessionSetupRequest computes bufferStart = int(secBufferOffset) - 64, clamps to sessionSetupFixedSize if negative, then sets SecurityBuffer=nil (no error) when bufferStart+secBufferLength > len(body) (line 98-100). A client sending a plausible StructureSize=25 but secBufferOffset/secBufferLength combination that places the buffer past the end of body gets req.SecurityBuffer=nil. SessionSetup then hits the 'no recognized auth mechanism' branch at line 357 and calls createGuestSession.
- **Why it matters:** MS-SMB2 §3.3.5.5 mandates STATUS_INVALID_PARAMETER for a malformed SESSION_SETUP request. Silently granting guest access when GuestEnabled=true lets a client that cannot pass NTLM (e.g. one that lacks valid credentials) deliberately send a malformed buffer to force guest login. The guest check (checkGuestPolicy) only blocks when GuestEnabled=false or SigningConfig.Required is true.
- **Fix:** After computing bufferStart, validate it: if secBufferLength > 0 and bufferStart+int(secBufferLength) > len(body), return nil + fmt.Errorf(...) from parseSessionSetupRequest (so the caller returns StatusInvalidParameter) instead of silently setting SecurityBuffer=nil.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. parseSessionSetupRequest at lines 93-100: when bufferStart+secBufferLength > len(body), SecurityBuffer stays nil (no error returned). SessionSetup then falls through all auth branches (line 141: len(nil)==0, line 303: len(nil)<2, line 333: ntlmToken nil) to line 359: createGuestSession(ctx). MS-SMB2 §3.3.5.5 requires STATUS_INVALID_PARAMETER. When GuestEnabled=true, credential-less client can force guest login via deliberately malformed SecurityBufferOffset.

### [MED] NotifyRename double-charges armed ancestor watchers in cross-directory renames · `bugs` · area: smb-lease-oplock-notify
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/change_notify.go:1003`
- **What:** `NotifyRename` calls `chargeArmedBuffer` twice when `newParentPath != oldParentPath`: once with `(oldParentPath, {oldFileName, newFileName})` and once with `(newParentPath, {oldFileName, newFileName})`. An armed WatchTree handle whose `WatchPath` is an ancestor of **both** paths matches in both calls; its `BufferedBytes` is incremented by 4 × `encodedNotifyEntrySize` entries instead of the correct 2 (one OLD_NAME entry + one NEW_NAME entry). The over-count triggers premature `Overflowed=true` and fires `OnOverflow`, causing the next CHANGE_NOTIFY on that handle to return `STATUS_NOTIFY_ENUM_DIR` when the buffer has not actually overflowed.
- **Why it matters:** Recursive directory watchers watching a common ancestor of the rename source and destination prematurely report overflow and force the client to re-enumerate the directory. Under repeated cross-directory renames a watcher can get stuck in a permanent overflow loop. Required by smbtorture smb2.notify.tcon and any test exercising WatchTree across rename boundaries.
- **Fix:** For the second `chargeArmedBuffer` call (newParentPath), pass only the names not already charged in the first call. For a cross-directory rename, the correct charge per ancestor watcher is exactly two entries (relativeOldPath + relativeNewPath). One approach: compute the distinct relative paths for each armed ancestor handle once (across both parent paths) and charge only those, rather than calling `chargeArmedBuffer` twice with the full name list.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. Armed ancestor watcher (WatchTree=true, ancestor of both paths) is NOT in liveFileIDs skip map. chargeArmedBuffer called at line 1003 with oldParentPath charges 2×encodedSize; called again at line 1005 with newParentPath, same watcher matches again via pathIsAncestor, charged another 2×encodedSize = 4× total. But only 2 events were buffered (lines 996-999). BufferedBytes over-counted → premature Overflowed=true.

### [MED] WRITE handler never updates PositionInfo (CurrentByteOffset), violating MS-FSA §2.1.5.3 · `bugs` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/write.go:444`
- **What:** After a successful write, `openFile.PositionInfo` is not updated. The equivalent READ path calls `recordReadProgress(openFile, req.Offset, uint64(len(readResult.Data)))` at line 416 in read.go.
- **Why it matters:** MS-FSA §2.1.5.3 (Server Algorithm for Writing a File) requires CurrentByteOffset to be set to `ByteOffset + BytesWritten` on success. QUERY_INFO FilePositionInformation and FILE_ALL_INFORMATION.PositionInformation (offset 80) will return a stale value after any write. Conformance tests that issue a WRITE then query FilePositionInformation (analogous to smb2.read.position) will fail.
- **Fix:** After `CommitWrite` succeeds (after line 424), add: `openFile.PositionInfo = req.Offset + uint64(len(req.Data))`. The existing `h.StoreOpenFile(openFile)` call at line 446 will persist the updated value.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. write.go has no call to recordReadProgress or any equivalent PositionInfo update after CommitWrite at line 424. read.go has recordReadProgress at lines 416 and 507. WRITE never updates OpenFile.PositionInfo (handler.go:574). QueryInfo FilePositionInformation returns stale value after any write.

### [MED] TOCTOU race on mode bits in handleSetSparse and handleSetCompression · `bugs` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/ioctl_sparse.go:101`
- **What:** Both `handleSetSparse` (ioctl_sparse.go:101-118) and `handleSetCompression` (ioctl_fsctl.go:104-132) implement a read-modify-write on `file.Mode`: `GetFile` → compute `newMode` → `SetFileAttributes`. No per-file lock is held across this sequence.
- **Why it matters:** Two concurrent requests (e.g., SET_SPARSE from one handle and SET_COMPRESSION from another) can both observe the same `file.Mode` base, compute their respective `newMode` independently, then the second `SetFileAttributes` call overwrites the first's bit. `go test -race` will detect this. The `modeDOSSparse` (0x200000) and `modeDOSCompressed` (0x40000) bits are independent; whichever writer completes last silently drops the other's update. Unlike QUERY_DIRECTORY (which holds `openFile.Lock()`), these IOCTL handlers have no serialization.
- **Fix:** Move the mode bit manipulation into `SetFileAttributes` itself as a bitwise OR/AND-NOT patch (pass a `SetModeBit`/`ClearModeBit` field in `SetAttrs`), so the metadata store applies the change atomically under its own transaction. Alternatively, introduce a per-file-handle mutex around the GetFile→SetFileAttributes sequence for these two IOCTLs, matching the pattern used in SET_INFO BasicInformation (set_info.go:396–632).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. handleSetSparse (ioctl_sparse.go:101-118) and handleSetCompression (ioctl_fsctl.go:104-132) both do GetFile → compute newMode → SetFileAttributes with no per-file lock. Two concurrent requests observe same base Mode, compute independent newMode, second writer silently drops first's bit. modeDOSSparse (|= 0x200000) and modeDOSCompressed (|= 0x40000) can be lost. No serialization unlike QUERY_DIRECTORY which holds openFile.Lock().

### [MED] QueryInfo swallows all metadata/filesystem errors as STATUS_NOT_SUPPORTED · `bugs` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/query_info.go:405`
- **What:** After dispatching to `buildFileInfoFromStore`, `buildFilesystemInfo`, or `BuildSecurityDescriptor`, any returned error is unconditionally mapped to `types.StatusNotSupported` (line 406).
- **Why it matters:** `buildFilesystemInfo` returns errors from `metaSvc.GetFilesystemStatistics` (e.g., backend unavailable → should be StatusInternalError). `buildFileStreamInformation` can return errors from `common.ResolveForRead`. Mapping real I/O errors to STATUS_NOT_SUPPORTED confuses clients: Windows will retry with a different info class rather than surfacing the real failure, making store errors invisible. Only `types.ErrNotSupported` from an unsupported info class should produce STATUS_NOT_SUPPORTED.
- **Fix:** Distinguish error types: if `errors.Is(err, types.ErrNotSupported)` return STATUS_NOT_SUPPORTED; otherwise return `common.MapToSMB(err)` or STATUS_INTERNAL_ERROR.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. query_info.go:405-406: any error from buildFileInfoFromStore, buildFilesystemInfo, or BuildSecurityDescriptor maps unconditionally to StatusNotSupported. buildFilesystemInfo at lines 1098-1101 and 1139-1142 propagates real GetFilesystemStatistics errors; these reach line 406 and become StatusNotSupported instead of StatusInternalError. Only types.ErrNotSupported at line 1189 should produce StatusNotSupported.

### [MED] ConfirmClientID CB_NULL goroutine may set CBPathUp on stale record · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:614`
- **What:** Goroutine launched at line 614 re-acquires sm.mu.Lock (line 617) and looks up sm.clientsByID[clientID] to write rec.CBPathUp. For Case-5 re-SETCLIENTID (same clientID), the old ClientRecord pointer stays in clientsByID until the new unconfirmed record is confirmed; the goroutine finds the old pointer and sets CBPathUp on the old record, not the newly confirmed one.
- **Why it matters:** The new confirmed client record ends up with CBPathUp=false permanently (CB_NULL result never lands on it). Delegations remain disabled for the re-confirmed client even when the callback path is healthy.
- **Fix:** Capture the ClientRecord pointer before goroutine launch: recordPtr := record. Inside the goroutine, after re-acquiring sm.mu, compare rec == recordPtr; if different, return early. This is the same guard pattern used in lease timer callbacks.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. Case-5 path (reuseConfirmedClient): comment at lines 435-436 explicitly says clientsByID[confirmed.ClientID] is NOT overwritten. After ConfirmClientID promotes the unconfirmed record, clientsByID[clientID] still points to the OLD confirmed record. Goroutine at line 618 looks up sm.clientsByID[clientID] → gets old record → sets CBPathUp on old record. New confirmed record (in clientsByName via line 592) never gets CBPathUp=true. Delegations permanently disabled for re-confirmed client.

### [MED] sendRecallV41 goroutine blocks on time.After(30s) with no cancellation path — leaks on session destroy · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/delegation.go:541`
- **What:** sendRecallV41 is invoked from goroutines spawned by CheckDelegationConflict and NFSBreakHandler. The select at line 527 has two cases: resultCh receive and time.After(30s). There is no case for BackchannelSender.stopCh or a server context. When BackchannelSender.Stop() is called during Shutdown, if the stop fires during a retry-delay sleep (lines 229–239 in sendCallbackWithRetry) before the request is processed, the sender exits via stopCh without writing to resultCh. The sendRecallV41 goroutine then blocks for the full 30s before the timeout case fires.
- **Why it matters:** On session destroy or server shutdown, one goroutine per in-flight recall stays alive for up to 30s. Under a delegation-heavy workload with a forced restart, this leaks O(maxDelegations) goroutines for 30s, delaying clean shutdown and potentially exhausting goroutine resources.
- **Fix:** Add a server-lifetime context to sendRecall and pass it through to sendRecallV41. Replace the time.After select case with context cancellation: case <-ctx.Done(). Alternatively, share BackchannelSender.stopCh as a channel parameter so the waiting goroutine exits immediately when the sender stops.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: sendRecallV41 select at lines 527-545 has only resultCh and time.After(30s) cases. BackchannelSender.sendCallbackWithRetry exits via stopCh at line 234 without writing to resultCh. Goroutine blocks full 30s before timeout fires. No context or stopCh case in sendRecallV41's select.

### [MED] ContextStore.Stop panics on double-call — no sync.Once guard on channel close · `bugs` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/context.go:269`
- **What:** Stop() calls close(cs.stopCh) unconditionally. Closing an already-closed channel panics in Go. No guard prevents double invocation.
- **Why it matters:** If GSSProcessor.Stop is called twice during server shutdown (e.g., graceful and forced paths both invoke it, or a test re-uses a processor), the server panics. This crashes the entire NFS server process.
- **Fix:** Add stopOnce sync.Once to ContextStore. Replace Stop body with: cs.stopOnce.Do(func() { close(cs.stopCh); cs.cleanupTicker.Stop() }).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: ContextStore.Stop() at line 268 calls close(cs.stopCh) unconditionally with no sync.Once or closed-check guard. Double-call panics with 'close of closed channel'.

### [MED] ContextStore.Store capacity enforcement is non-atomic — maxContexts limit races under concurrent INIT · `bugs` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/context.go:208`
- **What:** Store calls Count() (O(n) sync.Map range), then conditionally evictOldest(), then contexts.Store(). These three steps are not atomic. Under concurrent INIT load N goroutines can all observe count < maxContexts, skip eviction, and all store, growing the store to maxContexts + N - 1.
- **Why it matters:** The maxContexts limit is a resource cap preventing unbounded memory use from unauthenticated INIT floods. Violating it under concurrency allows an attacker to exhaust server memory by sending parallel INIT requests, defeating the intended DoS protection.
- **Fix:** Track count with atomic.Int64. Atomically increment before contexts.Store; if new count exceeds maxContexts, call evictOldest and decrement post-eviction. Or hold a mutex over the check-evict-store triple.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: Store() at lines 207-215 calls Count() (sync.Map range, O(n)), then evictOldest(), then contexts.Store() with no mutex across the three steps. N concurrent INIT goroutines can all observe count < maxContexts and all store, exceeding the cap by N-1.

### [MED] Wrong RPC accept_stat for unknown program: RPCProcUnavail (3) instead of RPCProgUnavail (1) · `bugs` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206`
- **What:** Default case of the program switch uses `rpc.RPCProcUnavail` (3 = PROC_UNAVAIL) when the requested program number is unknown.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 5531 §9 requires PROG_UNAVAIL (accept_stat=1) when the server does not recognise the program number. PROC_UNAVAIL (3) means 'program known, procedure not implemented'. An RFC-compliant client (e.g. Linux nfsd retransmit logic, mount automount) may retry or fall back differently on PROG_UNAVAIL vs PROC_UNAVAIL — wrong status can cause hangs or mis-diagnosis.
- **Fix:** Change `rpc.RPCProcUnavail` to `rpc.RPCProgUnavail` at line 206: `errorReply, err := rpc.MakeErrorReply(call.XID, rpc.RPCProgUnavail)`
- **Verified:** Confirmed: dispatch.go line 206 uses rpc.RPCProcUnavail (3) for unknown program number in default case. RFC 5531 requires RPCProgUnavail (1). Wrong accept_stat returned to clients for unrecognised programs.

### [MED] Syncer.Close DrainAllUploads races stopCh: periodic uploader goroutine may hold uploading gate · `bugs` · area: block-engine-core
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/syncer.go:938`
- **What:** `Syncer.Close` sets `m.closed=true`, closes `stopCh`, then calls `DrainAllUploads`. `SyncNow` (inside DrainAllUploads) busy-waits on `uploading.CompareAndSwap` for up to 30 s (defaultShutdownTimeout). If the periodic uploader goroutine is in the middle of `syncLocalBlocks` (holding `uploading=true`) when `stopCh` is closed, the goroutine will NOT exit until `syncLocalBlocks` returns — it only checks `stopCh` in the outer `for { select }` loop, not inside the inner `func() { defer uploading.Store(false); syncLocalBlocks(ctx) }()` closure. `SyncNow`'s CAS-wait loop therefore spins for up to the full timeout before it can acquire the gate and run the final drain.
- **Why it matters:** Under a slow remote (S3 timeout up to 30 s per chunk), a mirror pass can easily take longer than the 30 s shutdown timeout. `DrainAllUploads` returns `ctx.Err()` (DeadlineExceeded) with un-mirrored data, and the parent `Store.Close` proceeds to tear down the remote store while the periodic uploader is still active and may call `m.remoteStore.Put` after the remote store is closed.
- **Fix:** Close `stopCh` AFTER the drain completes, not before. Move `close(m.stopCh)` to after `_ = m.DrainAllUploads(ctx)`. Alternatively, pass the `uploading`-gated context into the periodic goroutine so it can be cancelled during the inner mirror pass. At minimum, pass a separate shutdown context (not `context.Background()`) to `DrainAllUploads` so it can be cancelled when the remote store is truly gone.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: Syncer.Close (lines 938-965) closes stopCh then calls DrainAllUploads (30s ctx). Periodic uploader only checks stopCh in outer loop, not inside syncLocalBlocks goroutine. If syncLocalBlocks is running when stopCh closes, DrainAllUploads spins up to 30s on uploading CAS before acquiring gate. Potential for data-loss on slow/hung remote exceeding timeout.

### [MED] reapSupersededFileBlocks skips reap entirely when newBlocks is empty — stale FileBlock rows accumulate · `bugs` · area: block-engine-core
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/engine.go:414`
- **What:** `reapSupersededFileBlocks` returns immediately when `len(newBlocks) == 0` (third guard on line 414). This is called from `ObjectIDPersister` for both the conflict-retry path (line 300) and the normal path (line 304). A rollup pass that produces zero blocks (e.g., a file truncated to 0 between rollup and persist) skips all reap logic, leaving every prior-generation FileBlock row alive in the per-payload manifest.
- **Why it matters:** If the file is subsequently re-written, `ListFileBlocks` returns stale rows from the zero-block rollup pass alongside the new rows. `readLocalByHash` may hit an old-generation row whose CAS chunk has been GC'd (RefCount 0 from the prior reap that didn't run), returning `ErrChunkNotFound` and zero-filling bytes that should have valid content. The accumulation also inflates `snapshotPendingBlockRefs` output so the speculative-dedup trigger evaluates against stale blocks.
- **Fix:** When `newBlocks` is empty but `priorOffsets` is non-empty, reap ALL prior offsets (the entire file was re-chunked to nothing, e.g. after a truncate-to-zero followed by a rollup). Change the guard to: `if bs.coordinator == nil || len(priorOffsets) == 0 { return nil }` and handle the `newBlocks==0` case as 'region covers everything' (reap all priorOffsets unconditionally).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: reapSupersededFileBlocks at line 414 returns early when len(newBlocks)==0, skipping all prior-generation reap. Zero-block rollup (truncate-to-0 race) leaves stale FileBlock rows alive. Subsequent re-writes may encounter GC'd CAS chunks via stale rows.

### [MED] SyncQueue.Stop() panics on double-call — close of closed channel · `bugs` · area: block-engine-gc-syncer
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/sync_queue.go:125`
- **What:** Stop() checks `if !q.started` to guard early exit, but `started` is set to true on first Start() and never reset. A second call to Stop() passes the guard (started=true, !started=false) and calls close(q.stopCh) on an already-closed channel, panicking.
- **Why it matters:** Go panics on close of a closed channel. While the current single caller (Syncer.Close, which is idempotent) only calls Stop once, the API has no contract preventing double-Stop. Any refactor, test, or shutdown race that calls Stop twice will produce a hard panic rather than a no-op. The fix-pattern already used by HealthMonitor.Stop() (sync.Once) is standard Go idiom.
- **Fix:** Add a sync.Once field to SyncQueue and replace the `close(q.stopCh)` line with: q.stopOnce.Do(func() { close(q.stopCh) }). Remove or keep the `!q.started` guard as a fast-path.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: SyncQueue.Stop() at lines 116-125 checks !q.started but started is set true once and never reset. Second call passes the guard and reaches close(q.stopCh) on an already-closed channel, panicking. No sync.Once guard present.

### [MED] Close() double-timeout — graceful shutdown can block up to 60s instead of 30s · `bugs` · area: block-engine-gc-syncer
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/syncer.go:956`
- **What:** Close() creates a context with defaultShutdownTimeout (30s) and passes it to DrainAllUploads (line 958). After DrainAllUploads returns (which may have consumed the full 30s), it then calls queue.Stop(defaultShutdownTimeout) (line 962) with a fresh full 30s timeout. Total worst-case shutdown duration is 60s.
- **Why it matters:** The intent is a single 30s graceful-shutdown window. With two sequential 30s timeouts, a server with a stuck remote store will stall for 60s at process shutdown, delaying pod restarts, rolling updates, and operator-triggered restarts. During the second 30s window the queue workers are already draining against a cancelled workerCtx (stopCh was closed), but slow or hung S3 connections can still pin them.
- **Fix:** Capture the start time before DrainAllUploads, compute remaining = defaultShutdownTimeout - elapsed, pass max(remaining, 0) to queue.Stop. Alternatively, derive the queue.Stop timeout from the same context: pass ctx.Done() or use the remaining deadline via context.WithDeadline.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: Syncer.Close() at lines 956-962 creates a 30s context for DrainAllUploads, then calls queue.Stop(defaultShutdownTimeout) with a fresh 30s timeout sequentially. Worst-case shutdown is 60s. Intent was a single 30s window.

### [MED] RegisterStoreForShare publishes store before lock manager is ready · `bugs` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/service.go:180`
- **What:** At line 180, s.stores[shareName] = store is written under s.mu and the lock is released at line 186. Between lines 186 and 245 (where s.mu is reacquired to publish the lock manager), the store is visible in s.stores but no lock manager exists yet for the share. Any concurrent call to lockManagerForHandle during this window returns ErrStaleHandle even though the store is live.
- **Why it matters:** A protocol handler racing with RegisterStoreForShare can successfully resolve the store via storeForHandle (line 532) but fail on lockManagerForHandle (line 561) with a stale-handle error, causing spurious NFS ESTALE or SMB STATUS_FILE_CLOSED for lock operations on a share that was just mounted. The two-phase publish (store first, lock manager later) creates an observable inconsistency window.
- **Fix:** Build and recover the lock manager before publishing the store, then publish both atomically under a single s.mu acquisition. Alternatively, return ErrNotReady (not ErrStaleHandle) from lockManagerForHandle when the store exists but no LM exists yet, so callers can retry rather than surfacing ESTALE.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: RegisterStoreForShare publishes s.stores[shareName]=store at line 180 under s.mu, releases at line 186. Lock manager not published until line 245-246 (second s.mu acquisition). Window exists where storeForHandle succeeds but lockManagerForHandle returns ErrStaleHandle, causing spurious ESTALE/STATUS_FILE_CLOSED for lock ops on a freshly mounted share.

### [MED] badger backup Restore resets usedBytes to zero after restore but does not reinitialize it · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/badger/backup.go:163`
- **What:** Badger Restore streams KV entries into the store via WriteBatch but never reinitializes the in-memory usedBytes atomic counter. After restore the counter stays at whatever value it had before (typically 0 for a fresh store, but could be non-zero if the destination was Reset then Restored).
- **Why it matters:** GetUsedBytes and FSSTAT report 0 (or stale) after a Badger restore until the server restarts and initUsedBytesCounter runs from NewBadgerMetadataStore. Any quota/monitoring path reading usedBytes during the session after Restore sees wrong data.
- **Fix:** After the final wb.Flush() and CRC check in Restore, call s.initUsedBytesCounter() to recompute the counter from the newly-restored file rows. Or inline the scan: iterate f: prefix, sum sizes of FileTypeRegular entries, call s.usedBytes.Store(total).
- **Verified:** badger/backup.go:163 Restore() streams KV via WriteBatch but never calls initUsedBytesCounter() or resets s.usedBytes atomic. Counter stays at pre-restore value (typically 0 for fresh store). GetUsedBytes/FSSTAT report stale 0 until next server restart.

### [MED] memory/transaction.go ListChildren cursor restart when cursor name deleted between pages · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/memory/transaction.go:407`
- **What:** Cursor resolution (lines 407-414) searches sortedNames for the cursor string. If the cursor entry was deleted between two paginated ListChildren calls, the loop finds no match, startIdx stays 0, and the next page returns entries from the beginning of the directory — duplicating entries already returned to the client.
- **Why it matters:** NFS READDIR clients with large directories (multiple pages) may see duplicate directory entries if any file in the directory is deleted between paginated calls. The conformance suite may not catch this because tests rarely interleave deletion with multi-page READDIR.
- **Fix:** Use a binary search on sortedNames with the cursor as lower bound (return entries where name > cursor, not name == cursor + 1). Replace the exact-match loop with: startIdx = sort.SearchStrings(sortedNames, cursor); if startIdx < len(sortedNames) && sortedNames[startIdx] == cursor { startIdx++ }. This correctly advances past the cursor even when it no longer exists.
- **Verified:** memory/transaction.go:407-413 — cursor not found in sortedNames leaves startIdx=0, so next ListChildren page re-emits entries from directory start. Happens if cursor entry deleted between paginated READDIR calls. Duplicate entries returned as-if-complete to NFS/SMB client.

### [MED] ListChildren (pool and tx paths) silently swallows rows.Err() — network errors produce truncated listings · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/files.go:363`
- **What:** After the for rows.Next() loop in ListChildren (files.go:246 pool path, transaction.go:563 tx path), neither implementation calls rows.Err(). A network error or server-side abort mid-stream will cause rows.Next() to return false early; the function then returns whatever partial entries were accumulated plus an empty cursor, with no error. Callers (NFS READDIR, SMB QueryDirectory) believe the listing is complete.
- **Why it matters:** NFS clients rely on the cursor/EOF signal to know they have seen all directory entries. A truncated listing returned as complete causes clients to miss files — POSIX readdir conformance failure. Under long directory scans with Postgres checkpoints or network hiccups this is realistic.
- **Fix:** After the rows loop, check `if err := rows.Err(); err != nil { return nil, "", mapPgError(err, "ListChildren", "") }` in both files.go and transaction.go ListChildren implementations. Same fix needed in ListShares (shares.go:237, transaction.go:998).
- **Verified:** postgres/files.go:246 (pool path) and transaction.go:563 (tx path) ListChildren loops end without calling rows.Err(). Mid-stream network error or server abort causes rows.Next() to return false early; partial listing returned with empty cursor as if complete. NFS/SMB clients see missing files.

### [MED] ListShares (pool and tx paths) missing rows.Err() check · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/shares.go:237`
- **What:** ListShares in shares.go (pool path) and transaction.go:1006 (tx path) iterate rows.Next() without checking rows.Err() afterward. A mid-stream error returns a partial share list as if complete.
- **Why it matters:** Runtime.ListShares feeds the control-plane share enumeration; a partial list causes the operator reconciler to think shares are absent and potentially trigger spurious delete/recreate cycles.
- **Fix:** Add `if err := rows.Err(); err != nil { return nil, err }` after each rows.Next() loop.
- **Verified:** postgres/shares.go:230 (pool path) and transaction.go:998 (tx path) ListShares loops never call rows.Err(). Partial share list silently returned as complete on mid-stream error. Operator reconciler may treat absent shares as deleted and trigger spurious delete/recreate.

### [MED] encodeUTF16LE truncates non-BMP codepoints instead of encoding surrogate pairs · `bugs` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/srvsvc.go:301`
- **What:** binary.LittleEndian.PutUint16(result[i*2:], uint16(r)) silently truncates any rune > 0xFFFF. Characters such as emoji or CJK extension-B produce a wrong UTF-16 code unit and corrupt the wire string.
- **Why it matters:** Windows clients receive a malformed UTF-16 share name or domain name string. The NDR unicode string length fields will also be wrong (pre-computed from len(runes)*2 not surrogate-pair-aware byte count), potentially causing a client-side parse fault.
- **Fix:** Use golang.org/x/text/encoding/unicode or manual surrogate-pair encoding: for r > 0xFFFF, encode as two uint16 surrogate pair values (0xD800 + high10, 0xDC00 + low10) and resize result accordingly.
- **Verified:** srvsvc.go:297-304 encodeUTF16LE uses uint16(r) which silently truncates runes > 0xFFFF (emoji, CJK ext-B, etc.) instead of encoding surrogate pairs. Result length pre-computed as len(runes)*2 also wrong for non-BMP chars. Corrupted UTF-16 wire strings to Windows clients.

### [MED] parseSIDsFromRequest misparses NULL SID pointer entries in NDR conformant array · `bugs` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/lsarpc.go:369`
- **What:** After skipping the SID-pointer array, the loop unconditionally reads 4 bytes as NDR SubAuthorityCount and then sidSize more bytes as SID binary for every entry in numSids. NDR pointer arrays include NULL pointers (4-byte zero referent) for absent entries; those entries have no following SID data. If any SID pointer slot is NULL, all subsequent SIDs are parsed at the wrong offset.
- **Why it matters:** A Windows client that sends a LsarLookupSids2 request with a sparse SID array (some NULL pointers) will receive misresolved or empty name mappings for all SIDs after the first NULL. The pointer array is already skipped in bulk (ptrArrayEnd calculation), so the NULL/non-NULL distinction is lost and subsequent SID data alignment is wrong.
- **Fix:** Before jumping to SID data, scan each pointer slot: if pointer is 0 (NULL), skip that slot's SID data (no SubAuthorityCount+SID follows for a NULL pointer referent). Track non-NULL count separately and only loop over those when reading the deferred SID bodies.
- **Verified:** lsarpc.go:369-387 parseSIDsFromRequest iterates numSids unconditionally reading SubAuthorityCount+SID data. NDR pointer arrays can contain NULL 4-byte referents for absent entries with no following SID blob. Null entries not checked; all subsequent SIDs parsed at wrong offset, misresolving names for all SIDs past the first NULL.

### [MED] BACKCHANNEL_CTL handler unconditionally dereferences v41ctx without nil guard — inconsistent with all other v4.1 handlers requiring session context · `bugs` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/v41/handlers/backchannel_ctl.go:39`
- **What:** HandleBackchannelCtl dereferences v41ctx.SessionID at line 39 without first checking v41ctx != nil. FREE_STATEID (free_stateid.go:40) and RECLAIM_COMPLETE (reclaim_complete.go:39) both guard with if v41ctx == nil { return NFS4ERR_OP_NOT_IN_SESSION } before use. BACKCHANNEL_CTL is not a session-exempt op so the current dispatcher always passes non-nil, but the absence of the guard makes this a latent nil-panic if dispatch logic changes or an op is misdirected.
- **Why it matters:** Inconsistency with every other handler that needs v41ctx: all others defensively check. If BACKCHANNEL_CTL is ever invoked via a path that does not guarantee a SEQUENCE has run (e.g., future ops table reorganization, direct call in tests), line 39 will panic with a nil pointer dereference.
- **Fix:** Add the same guard at the top of the function body, after the Decode check: if v41ctx == nil { return &types.CompoundResult{Status: types.NFS4ERR_OP_NOT_IN_SESSION, OpCode: types.OP_BACKCHANNEL_CTL, Data: EncodeStatusOnly(types.NFS4ERR_OP_NOT_IN_SESSION)} }
- **Verified:** backchannel_ctl.go:39 dereferences v41ctx.SessionID with no nil guard. FREE_STATEID (free_stateid.go:40) and RECLAIM_COMPLETE (reclaim_complete.go:39) both guard `if v41ctx == nil { return NFS4ERR_OP_NOT_IN_SESSION }` before touching v41ctx. BACKCHANNEL_CTL skips that guard entirely.

### [MED] GetCachedAuthContext: ShareReadOnly cached indefinitely — share mode change not reflected · `bugs` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/doc.go:95`
- **What:** `ShareReadOnly` is stored in the `authCache` sync.Map keyed by (share, flavor, uid, gid, gids). There is no TTL or invalidation. If a share is changed from read-write to read-only at runtime (via API), the cached `ShareReadOnly=false` entries remain and the write-permission gate in `authCtx.ShareReadOnly` is never re-evaluated for existing connections.
- **Why it matters:** The cache never expires and there is no hook from the share-config mutator to clear entries. A user whose session was established before the share went read-only continues to have write access until the process restarts. This is a security invariant violation.
- **Fix:** Either (a) do not cache `ShareReadOnly` — re-derive it on every request by calling `auth.ResolveSharePermission` while still caching the identity-mapped Identity (the expensive part), or (b) add a short TTL (e.g. 30s) to the cache by storing a timestamp alongside the entry and re-checking when stale.
- **Verified:** doc.go:95-99 stores ShareReadOnly in authCache sync.Map with no TTL or invalidation. Share mutator has no hook to clear entries. A client whose authCache entry was populated before a share goes read-only retains write-permission until process restart.

### [MED] UMNTALL removes ALL clients' mount records, not just the calling client's · `bugs` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/mount/handlers/umountall.go:51`
- **What:** UmntAll() calls h.Registry.RemoveAllMounts() which invokes Tracker.RemoveAll(), deleting every mount entry across all clients. RFC 1813 Appendix I §5.4 says UMNTALL removes all mount entries for the calling client only. The clientIP is extracted at line 48 but never passed to the removal call.
- **Why it matters:** Any client calling UMNTALL will silently unmount all other clients' recorded sessions. The DUMP response will then show zero active mounts even though other clients are still using the server. While NFS mount-table tracking is advisory, this causes incorrect showmount output and can interfere with per-client logic that keys on mount state.
- **Fix:** Replace h.Registry.RemoveAllMounts() with h.Registry.RemoveMount(clientIP) in a loop, or add a RemoveMountsByClient(clientIP) method to the runtime interface that filters by client address. The Tracker already has RemoveAllByProtocol; a RemoveAllByClient(clientAddr string) following the same pattern would be clean.
- **Verified:** umountall.go:51 calls h.Registry.RemoveAllMounts() with no clientIP argument — removes every client's mounts. clientIP is extracted at line 46 but only used for logging. RFC 1813 §I.5.4 scopes UMNTALL to the calling client only.

### [MED] NSM admitPeerState int32 monotonicity gate rejects legitimate reboots when peer state wraps · `bugs` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nsm/handlers/handler.go:213`
- **What:** admitPeerState stores and compares int32 NSM state numbers with a strict greater-than check. NSM state numbers are unsigned in practice and can wrap: after 2^31 - 1 increments, the int32 representation goes negative. A reboot that produces a new state of e.g. 1 (after many reboots) will compare as 1 <= large_stored_value and be dropped silently, meaning crash recovery (lock release + reclaim) is never triggered for that host.
- **Why it matters:** NSM spec (RFC 1813 §B.2.2) states state is int32 on the wire but semantically an ever-increasing counter. Linux rpc.statd uses uint32 internally and wraps around. After enough reboots the gate becomes permanently closed for the host until the server also restarts. Stale locks from a wrapped-state host persist indefinitely.
- **Fix:** Use sequence-number comparison: treat the state numbers as uint32 and compare using the half-open window trick (RFC 1982 serial number arithmetic): admit if (uint32(incoming) - uint32(stored)) & 0x80000000 == 0 && incoming != stored. Alternatively store as uint32 in peerState map.
- **Verified:** handler.go:213 stores and compares int32 NSM state with strict `incoming <= stored`. After int32 wraps negative, any subsequent small positive state (e.g. 1 after reboot) compares <= large stored value and is silently dropped, blocking crash-recovery lock release.

### [MED] getDurableStore: bare type assertion panics instead of skipping · `bugs` · area: metadata-storetest-conformance
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/storetest/durable_handles.go:101`
- **What:** Bare `store.(DurableHandleStoreProvider)` with no ok-idiom
- **Why it matters:** Panics if any caller invokes getDurableStore directly against a store that doesn't implement DurableHandleStoreProvider. RunDurableHandleStoreTests guards via ok-check at line 28, but getDurableStore is a package-level helper callable from any test. A panic aborts the whole test binary rather than skipping the subtest.
- **Fix:** Use two-value form: `provider, ok := store.(DurableHandleStoreProvider); if !ok { t.Skip("store does not implement DurableHandleStoreProvider"); return nil }; return provider.DurableHandleStore()`
- **Verified:** durable_handles.go:101 uses bare `store.(DurableHandleStoreProvider)` without ok-idiom. RunDurableHandleStoreTests guards at line 28 but getDurableStore is exported at package level; any test calling it directly against a non-implementing store panics instead of skipping, aborting the whole test binary.

### [MED] pruneEmptyDirs skips pages 2+ of bin subdirectories · `bugs` · area: controlplane-snapshot-gc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/trash/service.go:439`
- **What:** pruneEmptyDirs calls svc.ReadDirectory(ctx, dirHandle, 0, 0) once and iterates only that single page. No loop on page.HasMore / page.NextCookie. Compare walkBin (line 144–184) which correctly loops.
- **Why it matters:** After Empty purges all recycled roots, pruneEmptyDirs sweeps the now-empty intermediary path-component dirs (e.g. 'a/b/' left behind by 'a/b/c.txt'). If the bin root holds >1 ReadDirectory page of child dirs, pages 2+ are silently skipped. Those dirs remain non-empty from the store's view, causing OnDisable's subsequent RemoveDirectory on the #recycle root to fail with ErrNotEmpty — the bin cannot be fully disabled. Even without OnDisable, the stale dirs accumulate and are never reclaimed.
- **Fix:** Mirror the walkBin loop pattern: wrap the ReadDirectory call and the for-range in a for-loop that breaks when !page.HasMore and advances cookie = page.NextCookie each iteration. Since each pass removes entries that may shift subsequent pages, always restart from cookie=0 after any RemoveDirectory succeeds (same restart-from-zero pattern used in purgeChildren line 531).
- **Verified:** trash/service.go:439 pruneEmptyDirs calls ReadDirectory once with no HasMore/NextCookie loop. walkBin at line 144 correctly loops. Bins with >1 page of child dirs leave pages 2+ unswept, preventing full bin disable and accumulating stale dirs.

### [MED] UpdateSnapshotState TOCTOU: RowsAffected=0 disambiguated by a separate COUNT that races with concurrent deletes · `bugs` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/snapshots.go:122`
- **What:** When the conditional UPDATE matches 0 rows, UpdateSnapshotState fires a second SELECT COUNT to decide between ErrSnapshotNotFound and ErrSnapshotStateConflict. Between the UPDATE and the COUNT another goroutine (e.g. DeleteSnapshot called by a concurrent rollback) can delete the row. The COUNT then returns 0, returning ErrSnapshotNotFound to the caller even though the correct answer was ErrSnapshotStateConflict. MarkSnapshotReady has the same pattern at line 222.
- **Why it matters:** The runtime CreateSnapshot retry path and the REST 409 mapping both branch on errors.Is(err, ErrSnapshotStateConflict). A spurious ErrSnapshotNotFound causes the retry to re-create a snapshot row rather than surfacing a conflict, potentially producing duplicate snapshot metadata or a skipped retry.
- **Fix:** Encode the disambiguation in the single UPDATE by using a RETURNING clause (Postgres) or a separate query inside the same transaction. Alternatively, accept the ambiguity and return ErrSnapshotStateConflict for all 0-rows cases (the caller can re-fetch to distinguish), since that is the safer failure mode.
- **Verified:** snapshots.go:122-131 and :222-230 both use UPDATE then COUNT to distinguish ErrSnapshotNotFound from ErrSnapshotStateConflict. Concurrent DeleteSnapshot between the two queries returns ErrSnapshotNotFound when ErrSnapshotStateConflict was correct, causing the retry path to re-create a snapshot row.

### [MED] DeleteNetgroup / GetSharesByNetgroup: UUID substring LIKE search produces false positives · `bugs` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/netgroups.go:58`
- **What:** Both DeleteNetgroup (line 58) and GetSharesByNetgroup (line 137) search for netgroup references using: WHERE config LIKE '%<netgroupID>%'. The netgroup UUID can appear as a substring in an unrelated JSON field value (e.g. a share name, another UUID that happens to share a prefix, or a stored path). This causes ErrNetgroupInUse to fire for netgroups that are not actually in use, making them permanently undeletable.
- **Why it matters:** JSON substring matching without structural awareness is unreliable. The netgroup_id field is nested inside the config blob; the check must match the exact JSON key-value pair, not a bare substring.
- **Fix:** Use a JSON path query: for SQLite, json_extract(config, '$.netgroup_id') = ? ; for PostgreSQL, config::jsonb->>'netgroup_id' = ?. This is structurally precise and eliminates false positives.
- **Verified:** netgroups.go:59 and :137 both use `config LIKE '%'+netgroup.ID+'%'`. A UUID can appear as a substring in unrelated JSON fields, triggering false ErrNetgroupInUse and making legitimately unused netgroups permanently undeletable.

### [MED] CreateUser and UpdateUser silently ignore SharePerms and Groups request fields · `bugs` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/users.go:112`
- **What:** CreateUserRequest.SharePerms (line 41) is accepted in the JSON body but never passed to CreateUserWithGroups or any other call — silently dropped. UpdateUserRequest.Groups (line 50) and SharePerms (line 52) are declared fields that are never read inside the Update handler (lines 205-229). Callers who specify these fields get a 201/200 with no error but the operation is a no-op.
- **Why it matters:** Dead request fields create a contract lie: the API schema advertises functionality that is not implemented. Clients that rely on setting share permissions at user creation time will observe silent data loss.
- **Fix:** For Create: apply req.SharePerms after CreateUserWithGroups returns, calling SetUserSharePermission for each entry. For Update: apply req.Groups via a store call (e.g. UpdateUserGroups) and req.SharePerms via SetUserSharePermission. If intentionally deferred, remove the fields from the request structs and document the omission.
- **Verified:** users.go Create handler (line 112) passes req.Groups to CreateUserWithGroups but req.SharePerms is never used. Update handler (lines 205-232) reads Email/DisplayName/Role/Enabled/UID but never reads req.Groups or req.SharePerms — both fields silently dropped with 200/201.

### [MED] BlockStoreStatsHandler.Stats and Evict leak raw internal error strings in response body · `bugs` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/blockstore.go:43`
- **What:** Stats handler calls NotFound(w, err.Error()) at line 43 and Evict handler calls BadRequest(w, err.Error()) at line 75. Both inline the raw error message — which can contain filesystem paths, share-name internals, or store-layer details — into the HTTP response body visible to API clients.
- **Why it matters:** All other error paths in adjacent handlers (block_gc.go, blockstore_audit.go) explicitly strip err.Error() from responses and log at Debug. These two handlers are inconsistent: an unauthenticated attacker cannot reach them (admin-gated), but any admin-level API consumer or operator tool will see unexpectedly detailed internal error strings, which is an information-disclosure inconsistency and violates the established sanitization pattern.
- **Fix:** Replace NotFound(w, err.Error()) with logger.Debug(..., err) + NotFound(w, "share not found") or an appropriate static message. Replace BadRequest(w, err.Error()) with logger.Debug(..., err) + BadRequest(w, "eviction failed").
- **Verified:** Confirmed. blockstore.go:43 calls NotFound(w, err.Error()) and line 75 calls BadRequest(w, err.Error()), inlining raw error strings. Adjacent block_gc.go uses static messages ('GC failed', 'share not found: '+name) — never raw err.Error(). Pattern inconsistency confirmed from source.

### [MED] Settings.Get maps all store errors to 404, hiding DB failures · `bugs` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/settings.go:61`
- **What:** GetSetting error handling at line 61-63 maps every error — including connectivity failures, context cancellations, and internal store errors — to HTTP 404 Not Found. A transient DB outage returns 404 to the caller, indistinguishable from a genuinely missing key.
- **Why it matters:** Callers (operator tools, the operator controller) cannot distinguish 'key does not exist' from 'store is down'. This causes operators to incorrectly conclude settings are missing and may trigger destructive re-creation actions. All other resource handlers (users, shares, adapters) distinguish ErrNotFound from other errors with appropriate 500 fallback.
- **Fix:** Check errors.Is(err, models.ErrSettingNotFound) for 404; fall through to InternalServerError for anything else, matching the pattern used in every other GET handler.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. settings.go:60-63: all GetSetting errors unconditionally return 404 with static 'Setting not found'. Cannot distinguish genuinely missing key from transient DB failure/context cancel. Other handlers (block_gc.go, shares.go) use errors.Is checks and 500 fallback. Semantic ambiguity real; static message means no raw-error leak but the 404-for-all-errors bug stands.

### [MED] ResetPassword: non-atomic UpdatePassword + UpdateUser leaves MustChangePassword inconsistent on failure · `bugs` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/users.go:310`
- **What:** ResetPassword calls UpdatePassword (line 300) then UpdateUser (line 310) to set MustChangePassword. If UpdatePassword succeeds but UpdateUser fails, the password is reset but MustChangePassword stays at its prior value. For an admin user this means MustChangePassword stays true (or false if it was already false), which is incorrect.
- **Why it matters:** Same two-step non-atomic write pattern as ChangeOwnPassword. Admin-only path, so blast radius is smaller, but an admin resetting another admin's password via the API can leave the target account in an inconsistent state silently (the 500 response does not indicate which step failed).
- **Fix:** Combine both writes into a single atomic store operation or transaction. At minimum log which step failed to allow operator recovery.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. users.go:300-313: UpdatePassword then UpdateUser — two separate store calls, no transaction. If UpdatePassword succeeds and UpdateUser fails, MustChangePassword stays at prior value. Non-atomic two-step write confirmed from source.

### [MED] wireIdentityResolver registers duplicate OnIdentityMappingChange subscription on Kerberos provider re-injection · `bugs` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/smb/adapter.go:504`
- **What:** wireIdentityResolver unconditionally appends a new unsub to shareUnsubscribers and overwrites handler.IdentityResolver each time it is called when both KerberosProvider and runtime are non-nil. SetKerberosProvider calls it at line 485; if SetRuntime was already called first (both non-nil at that point), a first subscription is registered. A subsequent SetKerberosProvider call (provider replacement / settings reload) registers a SECOND subscription for a new resolver while the OLD resolver's unsub remains in shareUnsubscribers.
- **Why it matters:** Two OnIdentityMappingChange callbacks are active: the live one (new resolver) and the stale one (old resolver). Every identity-mapping change event fires InvalidateCache on the discarded resolver unnecessarily. More critically, on Stop() both unsubs are called, but if stop/restart cycles accumulate unmatched calls without Stop in between, the subscriber list in the runtime grows unboundedly.
- **Fix:** Track whether a subscription was already registered (e.g. a wireIdentityUnsub field on the Adapter). In wireIdentityResolver, call the old unsub before appending a new one: `if s.wireIdentityUnsub != nil { s.wireIdentityUnsub() }; s.wireIdentityUnsub = rt.OnIdentityMappingChange(...)`. Do not also append to shareUnsubscribers — manage it separately so Stop still unsubscribes.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. wireIdentityResolver (line 497-505) always appends a new unsub to shareUnsubscribers without checking for existing subscription. SetRuntime (line 263) and SetKerberosProvider (line 485) both call it. When both are non-nil at SetKerberosProvider call, second subscription appended while first still in slice, leaving duplicate callbacks and double unsub on Stop.

### [MED] BaseAdapter.Stop ctx-cancellation path skips forceCloseConnections unlike gracefulShutdown timeout path · `bugs` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/base.go:512`
- **What:** When Stop(ctx) is called and ctx is cancelled before all connections drain, the function returns ctx.Err() immediately (line 516) without calling forceCloseConnections(). The goroutine launched at line 501 (waiting on activeConns.Wait()) is abandoned. In contrast, gracefulShutdown() calls forceCloseConnections() on timeout. initiateShutdown() sets a 100ms read deadline, so connections drain quickly in practice, but if a connection is mid-write or blocked on writeMu the goroutine may outlive the Stop call.
- **Why it matters:** Callers that pass a context with a short deadline (e.g. the outer DittoServer shutdown orchestrator) expect Stop to clean up after returning. The goroutine leak is bounded (initiateShutdown's 100ms deadline bounds drain), but remaining connections are not force-closed, which is asymmetric with the nil-ctx/gracefulShutdown path and means the goroutine silently outlives Stop.
- **Fix:** In the ctx.Done() branch of Stop, call forceCloseConnections() before returning, mirroring gracefulShutdown(). The leaked goroutine should also be given a way to exit: either use the same done channel with a post-forceClose drain, or accept that the goroutine finishes after the forced close (bounded, safe).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. base.go Stop(): ctx.Done path (line 512-516) returns ctx.Err() immediately without calling forceCloseConnections(). gracefulShutdown() (line 437) does call forceCloseConnections() on timeout. Asymmetry confirmed. Background goroutine waiting on activeConns.Wait() is abandoned on ctx cancellation path.

### [MED] generateRandomSecret: modular bias on JWT secret bytes · `bugs` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/dittoserver_controller.go:712`
- **What:** `chars[int(randomBytes[i])%len(chars)]`: `len(chars)` is 62. Since 256 is not divisible by 62 (256 % 62 = 6), the first 6 characters in `chars` get marginally higher probability (~1.6% extra) than the rest. This affects the JWT signing secret auto-generated when no user-provided secret is configured.
- **Why it matters:** Modulo bias is a well-known weakness in CSPRNG sampling. For a JWT secret this is a security concern even if exploitation is impractical.
- **Fix:** Use rejection sampling: read enough bytes, reject any byte ≥ `(256/len(chars))*len(chars)`, take the rest modulo `len(chars)`. Or use `math/rand/v2.IntN` with a CSPRNG source, or use `base64.URLEncoding` like `generateRandomPassword` already does.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. dittoserver_controller.go:712: chars[int(randomBytes[i])%len(chars)] with len(chars)=62. 256%62=6, so first 6 characters get ~1.6% higher selection probability. Modulo bias on JWT secret generation confirmed.

### [MED] retryOnConflict: busy-wait sleep blocks reconcile goroutine · `bugs` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/dittoserver_controller.go:79`
- **What:** `time.Sleep(time.Duration(i+1) * retryBackoffBase)` inside `retryOnConflict` blocks the calling goroutine. This is called from `reconcileStatefulSet` and `createOrUpdateService` which are on the controller's reconcile path. With maxRetries=3 and base=100ms, worst-case blocks for 600ms holding the reconcile worker thread.
- **Why it matters:** controller-runtime reconcilers should not hold goroutines with blocking sleeps; the correct pattern is to return `ctrl.Result{RequeueAfter: ...}` so the worker is free for other work. Under load (many DittoServer CRs) this reduces controller throughput.
- **Fix:** Remove the `time.Sleep`; on conflict return an error that is caught by the caller and converted to a `ctrl.Result{RequeueAfter: retryBackoffBase}` requeue, or use context-aware `time.After` inside a select. Alternatively, keep it for the short CreateOrUpdate path but cap at 1 retry.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. dittoserver_controller.go:79: time.Sleep(time.Duration(i+1)*retryBackoffBase) inside retryOnConflict, maxRetries=3, retryBackoffBase=100ms, worst-case 600ms blocking sleep on reconcile goroutine. Called from reconcileStatefulSet and createOrUpdateService on reconcile hot path.

### [MED] setAuthCondition: status update on stale in-memory object after setRetryCount may conflict · `bugs` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/auth_reconciler.go:427`
- **What:** `setAuthCondition` does a fresh Get + `r.Status().Update(ctx, latest)`. Before it is called, `setRetryCount` (line 162 or 181) also does a fresh Get + `r.Update(ctx, latest)` — a metadata update that bumps `resourceVersion`. The `setAuthCondition` re-fetch is independent so it sees the post-setRetryCount resourceVersion, which is fine. However, `reconcileAuth` is called without holding any lock, and both `setRetryCount` and `setAuthCondition` touch the same CR object in rapid succession. If another reconcile fires concurrently (e.g., from a watch event), the second `r.Status().Update` in `setAuthCondition` will get a 409 conflict and silently return without updating the condition (the error is only logged, never propagated).
- **Why it matters:** Line 427: `if err := r.Status().Update(ctx, latest); err != nil { logger.Error(err, ...) }` — conflict errors are swallowed. The `Authenticated` condition may remain stale, causing `updateReadyCondition` to compute a wrong `Ready` value, blocking production workloads that gate on `Ready=True`.
- **Fix:** Wrap `setAuthCondition`'s status update in a retry loop (similar to `retryOnConflict`), re-fetching on 409 conflict. Or merge both the retry-count annotation update and condition update into a single re-fetch+update cycle.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_reconciler.go:427: r.Status().Update error only logged, never propagated. setRetryCount and setAuthCondition both do independent Get+Update on same CR in rapid succession without coordination; conflict errors on setAuthCondition silently swallowed, leaving Authenticated condition stale.

### [MED] CopyPayload: Ctime not updated on dst file after content change · `bugs` · area: internal-adapter-common
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/common/copy_payload.go:77`
- **What:** CopyPayload updates dstFile.Mtime but never sets dstFile.Ctime = time.Now(). After the txn commits, dst's ctime reflects its original creation time, not the copy operation.
- **Why it matters:** POSIX: ctime must advance on any metadata or content change. Clients (NFS, SMB) cache file identity on (mtime, ctime, size) triplet. A stale ctime means clients observing the file before and after the copy see identical ctimes and may serve stale cached data. metadata/io.go WriteFile explicitly sets Ctime (io.go:230, 315, 429); CopyPayload bypasses that path and writes directly via tx.PutFile.
- **Fix:** Add `dstFile.Ctime = dstFile.Mtime` (or `time.Now()`) immediately after setting dstFile.Mtime at line 77, before the tx.PutFile call.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. copy_payload.go:77: dstFile.Mtime set to time.Now() but dstFile.Ctime never updated. tx.PutFile commits with stale ctime. metadata/io.go WriteFile explicitly sets both Mtime and Ctime. Direct tx.PutFile bypass omits Ctime update.

### [MED] followLogs goroutine and signal-handler leak — signal.Stop never called · `bugs` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfs/commands/logs.go:175`
- **What:** `signal.Notify(sigCh, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM)` registers `sigCh` but `signal.Stop(sigCh)` is never called before the function returns. The goroutine at line 177 blocks on `<-sigCh` forever after `ctx` is cancelled via the watcher-error path (line 209) or the watcher-closed path — the goroutine has no exit path other than receiving a signal.
- **Why it matters:** On normal watcher-error return the goroutine leaks. The signal registration also leaks: subsequent calls to `dfs logs -f` (e.g. in scripts that restart the command) accumulate signal registrations. On Go's signal delivery model this is harmless for process lifetime but is a correctness/resource bug.
- **Fix:** Call `signal.Stop(sigCh)` before returning in all paths, and close `sigCh` or use a `context`-aware pattern. Simplest: replace the manual goroutine+sigCh with `signal.NotifyContext(context.Background(), syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM)` which handles cleanup automatically, then `defer cancel()`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. logs.go:174-180: signal.Notify registers sigCh; goroutine blocks on <-sigCh. On watcher-error return (line 209) or watcher-closed return, function exits but goroutine has no exit path besides receiving a signal — it leaks. signal.Stop(sigCh) never called anywhere in the function.

### [MED] followLogs silently drops partial log lines (no trailing newline) · `bugs` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfs/commands/logs.go:197`
- **What:** `reader.ReadString('\n')` returns `(partialData, io.EOF)` when a write event delivers a line fragment that has no trailing newline yet. The inner loop `break`s on any error including `io.EOF` without printing `line`. The partial content is discarded. On the next write event, the `bufio.Reader` position is past the partial data so it is never re-read.
- **Why it matters:** Log lines written in two flushes (common for structured JSON loggers that write fields then newline separately, or for large lines) are silently dropped in `dfs logs -f`. Operators tailing logs during an incident would miss entries.
- **Fix:** Print the partial line before breaking: `if line != "" { fmt.Print(line) }` before the `break`. This is the standard `tail -f` pattern. Alternatively buffer across iterations using a `strings.Builder`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. logs.go:196-202: inner loop calls ReadString('\n'); on io.EOF with partial data, err != nil so break fires before fmt.Print(line). Partial line silently dropped. bufio.Reader position advanced past partial data so it's never re-read on next write event.

### [MED] CleanupBucket silently leaves objects when bucket has >1000 items · `bugs` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/framework/containers.go:223`
- **What:** CleanupBucket calls ListObjectsV2 once (no continuation loop) and deletes only the first page of up to 1000 objects. It then calls DeleteBucket. If the bucket contains >1000 objects, DeleteBucket fails with BucketNotEmpty and the error is silently swallowed (_ = lh.Client.DeleteBucket(...)). The bucket and all remaining objects are leaked. ListS3PrefixWithSizes at line 174 correctly paginates; CleanupBucket does not.
- **Why it matters:** S3 ListObjectsV2 returns at most 1000 keys per call. Tests that create many small chunks (dedup, vmfleet, store-matrix) can easily exceed 1000 objects, causing silent bucket leaks that accumulate across CI runs and eventually cause Localstack resource exhaustion.
- **Fix:** Replace the single ListObjectsV2 call with the same pagination loop used in ListS3PrefixWithSizes, collecting all keys before deleting them. Alternatively call lh.ListS3PrefixWithSizes and delete in batches (S3 DeleteObjects accepts up to 1000 keys per call).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. CleanupBucket (line 223) does single ListObjectsV2 with no ContinuationToken loop, deletes only first <=1000 objects, then calls DeleteBucket with error silently swallowed via _, _. ListS3PrefixWithSizes at line 174 correctly paginates; CleanupBucket does not. Silent leak for >1000-object buckets.
