### [MED] IP ACL bypass: clientAddr includes port, MatchesIPPattern never matches · `security` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/auth_permissions.go:90`
- **What:** CheckShareAccess passes raw clientAddr (format "IP:port") directly to MatchesIPPattern at lines 90 and 109. MatchesIPPattern calls net.ParseCIDR(pattern) which succeeds for CIDR patterns, but then net.ParseIP("1.2.3.4:12345") returns nil (port not stripped), so CIDR contains() fails. The exact-match fallback compares "1.2.3.4:12345" == "1.2.3.4" which is always false. Result: DeniedClients list never fires (banned IPs pass through), AllowedClients list never matches (permitted IPs are rejected).
- **Why it matters:** MatchesIPPattern expects a bare IP address (auth_identity.go:333 doc says 'clientIP'). The function signature, comment, and test file all use 'clientIP'. But CheckShareAccess receives 'clientAddr' which callers pass as conn.RemoteAddr().String() — always 'IP:port'. Port is stripped for NFS mount (extractClientIP) and xdr.ExtractClientIP, but CheckShareAccess has no equivalent strip, so the raw ':port' suffix breaks both CIDR and exact matching silently.
- **Fix:** Strip port before calling MatchesIPPattern. In CheckShareAccess, add: host, _, err := net.SplitHostPort(clientAddr); if err == nil { clientAddr = host }. Apply the same strip before building AuthContext.ClientAddr. Alternatively add port-stripping inside MatchesIPPattern itself since its documented contract is an IP address.
- **Verified:** Bug confirmed in code. MatchesIPPattern at auth_identity.go:333 expects bare IP; CheckShareAccess at auth_permissions.go:90,109 passes raw clientAddr which would include port. net.ParseIP('IP:port') returns nil, CIDR check fails; exact match 'IP:port'=='IP' also fails. However CheckShareAccess has no callers in production code — AllowedClients/DeniedClients enforcement is dead code. The IP ACL feature simply never fires (neither deny nor allow). Severity downgraded: bug is real but not reachable in current production paths.

### [MED] NLM FREE_ALL accepts unauthenticated lock-drop from any remote host · `security` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/dispatch.go:100`
- **What:** NLMProcFreeAll entry has NeedsAuth:false with comment 'uses AUTH_NULL'. The handler (free_all.go:77-93) accepts any caller_name from any source IP and logs it; the adapter OnClientCrash callback then releases all locks for that caller_name. No source-address restriction (unlike portmap SET/UNSET which gates on IsLocalhost). Any remote attacker can send FREE_ALL with Name=<victim_hostname> and cause all NLM locks held by that host to be released.
- **Why it matters:** Missing auth/authz: rpc.statd is the only legitimate sender; without a localhost-or-monitored-peer gate any network-adjacent host can forge FREE_ALL name=<active_client> to drop advisory locks, enabling a competing client to seize byte ranges -> silent data corruption. This is the canonical NLM spoofing primitive documented in CVE-2011-2500 class.
- **Fix:** Add source-IP restriction equivalent to portmap's IsLocalhost check, or verify that the sender's IP matches an SM_MON registration for the claimed name (same pattern as NSM Notify H16 gate in nsm/handlers/notify.go). Simplest: in the FreeAll handler or dispatch wrapper, reject calls whose ctx.ClientAddr is not loopback — rpc.statd always runs on the same host.
- **Verified:** Confirmed NeedsAuth:false at dispatch.go:100 — any remote host can send FREE_ALL. Handler at free_all.go:77-93 decodes, logs, returns void — it does NOT call OnClientCrash and does NOT release any locks (comment at line 88-90 says 'actual lock release is triggered by the adapter's OnClientCrash' but that call is absent). Auth bypass is real; however claimed impact (lock drop enabling data corruption) is overstated since handler is currently a stub no-op. Downgrade to MED: real auth bypass, but locks not actually released.

### [MED] Postgres DSN keyword injection via unquoted config values · `security` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/gorm.go:86`
- **What:** DSN() builds a libpq keyword=value string via fmt.Sprintf with no quoting of Host, User, Password, Database, SSLMode, or SSLRootCert. A value containing a space injects additional DSN keywords. For example, a password of `secret sslmode=disable dbname=postgres` silently overrides downstream parameters already set by the caller — bypassing TLS enforcement or redirecting to a different database.
- **Why it matters:** libpq keyword=value parsing treats unquoted spaces as parameter separators. The Validate() function only checks non-empty; no character sanitization or quoting is performed. An operator-supplied or env-var-supplied password/host with embedded spaces (or single quotes) can alter the effective connection parameters after the server has already started, violating the SSL posture or reaching an unintended schema.
- **Fix:** Quote every value in the DSN and escape interior single-quotes and backslashes per libpq rules. Minimal fix: write a helper `func libpqQuote(s string) string` that wraps the value in single quotes and replaces `\` → `\\` and `'` → `\'`, then use it for all six fields:

```go
func libpqQuote(s string) string {
    s = strings.ReplaceAll(s, `\`, `\\`)
    s = strings.ReplaceAll(s, `'`, `\'`)
    return `'` + s + `'`
}

func (c *PostgresConfig) DSN() string {
    dsn := fmt.Sprintf("host=%s port=%d user=%s password=%s dbname=%s",
        libpqQuote(c.Host), c.Port, libpqQuote(c.User),
        libpqQuote(c.Password), libpqQuote(c.Database))
    if c.SSLMode != "" {
        dsn += " sslmode=" + libpqQuote(c.SSLMode)
    }
    if c.SSLRootCert != "" {
        dsn += " sslrootcert=" + libpqQuote(c.SSLRootCert)
    }
    return dsn
}
```
Alternatively, use the `pgx` URL form (`postgres://user:pass@host/db?sslmode=...`) with `url.QueryEscape` for each component, which has unambiguous encoding semantics.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. gorm.go:86-96: DSN built via fmt.Sprintf with Host, User, Password, Database, SSLMode, SSLRootCert unquoted. A password containing ' sslmode=disable' or ' dbname=other' injects extra libpq keyword=value pairs, silently overriding TLS posture or target database. Validate() at line 149 only checks non-empty; no character sanitization. Severity lowered: requires config-file/env-var access (operator trust), not REST input. Fix: use pgx/v5 url.URL builder or single-quote-escape each value.

### [MED] qcow2 SHA256 pin never set — downloaded binary accepted without integrity check · `security` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/framework/qcow2_fixture.go:34`
- **What:** qcow2BaseSHA256 is set to the placeholder string "<freeze-at-first-run>". DownloadQcow2Base explicitly skips the integrity check when this placeholder is present (lines 77-81, 125-128), logging the actual hash but never failing. Any file served from qcow2BaseURL — including a MITM-substituted or CDN-rotated image — will be accepted and stored, then used to synthesize test clones written into the DittoFS share under test.
- **Why it matters:** The intent documented in the constant comment is that the observed SHA256 would be frozen in a follow-up commit. That commit never happened; the placeholder remains live. During a test run the framework performs an unauthenticated HTTP download (no TLS pinning beyond the CDN certificate) and writes the result to the local filesystem without verifying content. A supply-chain substitution or network attacker could inject arbitrary bytes that execute when the qcow2 is processed.
- **Fix:** Freeze the known-good SHA256 of the Alpine 3.20.3 cloud image into qcow2BaseSHA256 (the value should have been logged on first run; re-run the test, capture the logged hash, and set qcow2BaseSHA256 = "<actual hex digest>"). After freezing, the mismatch branch at line 131-135 will reject any future rotation or MITM.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: qcow2BaseSHA256=="<freeze-at-first-run>" sentinel present at line 34. Lines 77-81 return early with only a log (no fail) when placeholder detected and cache exists; lines 125-128 log but don't Fatalf when fresh download happens. Integrity check is intentionally skipped in placeholder mode. The follow-up freeze commit never happened.

### [MED] uint32 wraparound in verifier-length skip lets malicious callback server bypass RPC acceptStat check · `security` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/callback_common.go:299`
- **What:** ValidateCBReply reads verfLen (uint32) from the wire and computes paddedLen = int64((verfLen + 3) &^ 3). If verfLen = 0xFFFFFFFD the uint32 addition overflows to 0x00000000, paddedLen = 0, and reader.Seek(0, SeekCurrent) is a no-op. The verifier body bytes remain in the reader and are then parsed as acceptStat.
- **Why it matters:** A malicious NFS client running a fake callback server (reachable via the SSRF path above, or directly for v4.1 back-bound connections) can craft a CB_NULL or CB_COMPOUND reply with verfLen=0xFFFFFFFD followed by four zero bytes. ValidateCBReply returns nil (success). For CB_RECALL this causes the server to start the full leaseDuration revocation timer instead of the 5-second timer, letting the client retain a delegation it should have been forced to return — delegation state desync across the cross-protocol lock.LockManager.
- **Fix:** Add a bound check before the seek: if verfLen > MaxFragmentSize { return fmt.Errorf("verf body too large: %d", verfLen) }. This is consistent with the existing MaxFragmentSize guard in ReadFragment and eliminates the overflow.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. callback_common.go:297-302: guard is `if verfLen > 0` so 0xFFFFFFFD passes. uint32 addition: 0xFFFFFFFD+3=0x00000000, paddedLen=int64(0). reader.Seek(0, SeekCurrent) is no-op. Verifier body bytes remain in reader and are parsed as acceptStat. Mechanism: crafted CB reply bypasses verifier skip, forces garbage acceptStat parse.

### [MED] all_squash bypass: Username/Domain preserved through MapAllToAnonymous, named-principal ACEs still match · `security` · area: metadata-service-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/auth_identity.go:261`
- **What:** MapAllToAnonymous branch (lines 261-267) copies identity.Username and identity.Domain into the squashed Identity while replacing UID/GID/SID with anonymous values. buildFileAccessEvalContext (auth_permissions.go:1034-1038) sets evalCtx.Who = squashedIdentity.Username + "@" + squashedIdentity.Domain. aceMatchesWhoWithOwnerRights (acl/evaluate.go:346) matches ACEs via ace.Who == evalCtx.Who. A file with a named ACE (e.g. ALLOW "root@localdomain" WRITE_DATA) will still grant that access to the squashed identity because Who is preserved despite all_squash.
- **Why it matters:** all_squash / MapAllToAnonymous is a security control to strip all client identity. Preserving Username+Domain leaks the original identity into the ACL evaluation path and lets named-principal ACEs grant elevated rights that the squash is supposed to remove. The SID path is correctly zeroed (mapping.AnonymousSID) but the username path is not.
- **Fix:** Zero Username and Domain in the MapAllToAnonymous branch: return &Identity{UID: mapping.AnonymousUID, GID: mapping.AnonymousGID, SID: mapping.AnonymousSID}. Do not copy Username/Domain from the original identity. Also clear GroupSIDs for the same reason (currently not copied but verify). The squashed identity must carry no information from the original.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_identity.go:261-267: MapAllToAnonymous copies identity.Username and identity.Domain into squashed Identity. buildFileAccessEvalContext (auth_permissions.go:1035-1038) sets evalCtx.Who = Username+"@"+Domain. Named-principal ACEs matching Who still grant elevated rights to all_squash clients. UID/GID/SID correctly zeroed but username path leaks through.

### [MED] leaseTimeSeconds and identityMapper globals written without synchronization — data race on every GETATTR · `security` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/attrs/encode.go:87`
- **What:** leaseTimeSeconds (plain var uint32, line 82) is written by SetLeaseTime (line 87) and read unsynchronized on every GETATTR encode at lines 326 and 554. identityMapper (plain var identity.IdentityMapper interface, line 122) is written by SetIdentityMapper (line 128) and read at line 710 with an unsynchronized nil-check. The adjacent fsMax* vars correctly use atomic.Uint64 (lines 99-101), but these two globals do not.
- **Why it matters:** Concurrent GETATTR handling (one goroutine per RPC) races with initialization-time SetLeaseTime / SetIdentityMapper calls. A torn read of leaseTimeSeconds produces a garbage lease time on the wire. A torn read of the identityMapper interface value (two machine words: type pointer + data pointer) can yield a non-nil interface whose type pointer is zero, causing a nil-pointer dereference in the Resolve call at line 713 and crashing the server. This is in scope as unsafe deserialization: corrupted wire output or server crash triggered by external GETATTR traffic during startup.
- **Fix:** Replace leaseTimeSeconds with atomic.Uint32: 'var leaseTimeSeconds atomic.Uint32' with Store/Load calls in SetLeaseTime/GetLeaseTime and the two encode sites. For identityMapper, use atomic.Pointer[identity.IdentityMapper] or protect with a sync.RWMutex. Pattern is already established in the same file for fsMaxFileSize/Read/Write (lines 99-101).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. encode.go:82-88: leaseTimeSeconds plain var uint32, SetLeaseTime writes without sync, read at lines 326 and 554 in concurrent GETATTR. identityMapper plain interface var at line 122, written at line 128, read at line 710 with unsynchronized nil-check. Adjacent fsMax* vars use atomic.Uint64 (lines 99-101) — inconsistency confirms oversight. Interface torn read can yield nil-type non-nil interface → crash.

### [MED] SIDMapper polynomial-hash fallback can collide with real user/group RIDs · `security` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/auth/sid/mapper.go:211`
- **What:** PrincipalToSID falls back to a polynomial hash (rid = rid*31 + uint32(c)) for principal strings that are not well-known, not a numeric UID, and not a sid: prefix. The resulting RID is used to construct a full domain SID identical in format to UserSID(uid) = uid*2+1000.
- **Why it matters:** A crafted principal string whose polynomial hash equals uid*2+1000 for some target uid will produce the same Windows SID as that uid's domain user SID. SMB/NFSv4 ACL evaluation compares SIDs for equality; a successful collision lets an attacker-supplied ACE principal match a real user's SID, granting or denying access intended for that user. The 32-bit hash space is small enough for collision search (birthday probability).
- **Fix:** Reserve the hash-based RID range separately from the uid/gid RID ranges. For example, use RIDs >= 0x80000000 for hash-based entries (users use uid*2+1000 which stays well below 2^31 for realistic UIDs). Alternatively, refuse to construct domain SIDs for unknown principals and return WellKnownEveryone or a sentinel null SID instead of a hash-derived domain SID.
- **Verified:** mapper.go:219 confirmed: hash fallback calls makeDomainSID(rid) directly with polynomial rid. UserSID uses uid*2+1000 formula and same makeDomainSID. No guard prevents hash(principalString)==uid*2+1000 for a target uid. 32-bit polynomial hash space is small; collision search feasible. Same domain SID produced for attacker-controlled principal and real UID.

### [MED] Missing url.PathEscape on username/group/store names — client-side path traversal to unintended REST endpoints · `security` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/apiclient/users.go:61`
- **What:** `resourcePath("/api/v1/users/%s", username)` uses plain `fmt.Sprintf` with no `url.PathEscape`. Same pattern in `UpdateUser` (line 71), `DeleteUser` (line 76), `ResetUserPassword` (line 82), `groups.go` `GetGroup`/`UpdateGroup`/`DeleteGroup`/`AddGroupMember`/`RemoveGroupMember`, `stores.go` `GetMetadataStore`/`UpdateMetadataStore`/`DeleteMetadataStore`/`GetBlockStore`/`UpdateBlockStore`/`DeleteBlockStore`, `netgroups.go`, and the `username`/`groupName` second segment in `shares.go:248/253/259/264`.
- **Why it matters:** A value like `../groups/admins` in `username` produces path `/api/v1/users/../groups/admins`; Go's `net/http` transport canonicalizes `..` segments before sending, resolving to `/api/v1/groups/admins`. This routes the request to a completely different endpoint. An operator command like `dfsctl user get '../groups/admins'` silently hits the group endpoint, potentially returning or deleting the wrong resource. With crafted names an attacker who can name users/stores could manipulate other API consumers.
- **Fix:** Replace `resourcePath("/api/v1/users/%s", username)` with `"/api/v1/users/" + url.PathEscape(username)` (or add escaping inside `resourcePath`). Apply consistently to all bare-interpolated path segments: `groups.go`, `stores.go`, `netgroups.go`, and the second `%s` in `shares.go:248/253/259/264`. Shares already escape the first segment via `url.PathEscape(normalizeShareNameForAPI(...))` — the same must apply to the `username`/`groupName` segments.
- **Verified:** helpers.go:82 confirmed: resourcePath = plain fmt.Sprintf with no url.PathEscape. users.go:61,71,76 all use this. Go net/http sends raw .. path segments without normalization. '../groups/admins' in username would produce /api/v1/users/../groups/admins and router may normalize it to /api/v1/groups/admins, hitting a different endpoint.

### [MED] CIFS mount option injection via comma in SMB username or password (Linux) · `security` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfsctl/commands/share/mount_unix.go:136`
- **What:** `opts := fmt.Sprintf("vers=2.1,port=%d,username=%s,password=%s", port, username, password)` embeds raw username and password directly into the comma-delimited `-o` option string passed to `mount -t cifs`. A comma in the password (e.g. `p@ss,sec=none`) is parsed by the kernel CIFS driver as a new option.
- **Why it matters:** CIFS `-o` options are comma-separated. An attacker who controls the password (e.g. via the `DITTOFS_PASSWORD` env var or `--password` flag) can append arbitrary mount options such as `sec=none` (bypass auth), `vers=1.0`, or `forceuid=0`. When `dfsctl share mount` is run with `sudo`, this becomes a local privilege escalation: injected options can override security settings for the kernel mount.
- **Fix:** Reject usernames and passwords that contain commas before building `opts`, or pass credentials via a credentials file (`credentials=/tmp/creds`) with 0600 permissions rather than inline in the `-o` string. Validate `username` and `password` contain no `,` or `=` characters and return an error if they do.
- **Verified:** mount_unix.go:136 confirmed: opts = fmt.Sprintf("vers=2.1,port=%d,username=%s,password=%s", port, username, password) with no escaping. Comma in password injects new CIFS mount options. When run with sudo, injected options like sec=none bypass auth.

### [MED] process-global os.Setenv(KRB5CCNAME) not cleaned up, leaks across parallel tests · `security` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/kerberos_test.go:263`
- **What:** testConcurrentUsers calls `os.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", aliceCC)` and then `os.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", bobCC)` without ever restoring the original value. These are process-global mutations; if the test runs in parallel with other tests that rely on KRB5CCNAME they will use Bob's credential cache. The same pattern appears at nfsv4_kerberos_test.go:355,364.
- **Why it matters:** os.Setenv is process-global and permanent for the duration of the process. t.Setenv (used correctly in framework/kerberos.go:98-100) registers a cleanup that restores the previous value on test exit. Using bare os.Setenv here means the variable is not restored if the test fails mid-way, races against parallel test goroutines that read KRB5CCNAME, or is subsequently read by KinitWithCC helpers that inherit the wrong cache path.
- **Fix:** Replace both `os.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", aliceCC)` and `os.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", bobCC)` with `t.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", aliceCC)` / `t.Setenv("KRB5CCNAME", bobCC)`. Apply the same fix to nfsv4_kerberos_test.go:355 and 364.
- **Verified:** kerberos_test.go:263,273 and nfsv4_kerberos_test.go:355,364 confirmed: bare os.Setenv used, never t.Setenv. No cleanup registered. framework/kerberos.go:100 correctly uses t.Setenv for same variable. Process-global leak if test fails mid-way or runs in parallel.

### [MED] Wrong RPC accept_stat for unknown program: RPCProcUnavail instead of RPCProgUnavail · `slop` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206`
- **What:** Unknown-program default branch calls `rpc.MakeErrorReply(call.XID, rpc.RPCProcUnavail)` (value 3 = PROC_UNAVAIL) instead of `rpc.RPCProgUnavail` (value 1 = PROG_UNAVAIL). RFC 5531 §9 mandates PROG_UNAVAIL when the server does not recognise the program number; PROC_UNAVAIL means the program is known but the procedure is not. Sending the wrong accept_stat will confuse NFS clients that check the exact code before retrying via portmap.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong constant: both `RPCProcUnavail` and `RPCProgUnavail` exist in the rpc package with adjacent values (3 vs 1). Parallel inner/outer dispatch.go files both handle the same default case — `internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:203` correctly uses `rpc.RPCProgUnavail`, but the outer `pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206` copy uses the wrong constant.
- **Fix:** Change line 206 from `rpc.RPCProcUnavail` to `rpc.RPCProgUnavail`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206 uses rpc.RPCProcUnavail (value 3, PROC_UNAVAIL) for unknown program default case. internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:203 correctly uses rpc.RPCProgUnavail. RFC 5531 §9 requires PROG_UNAVAIL for unknown program numbers. Two parallel dispatch files, one has wrong constant.

### [MED] OnRead prefetches already-read hashes instead of upcoming hashes · `slop` · area: block-engine-gc-syncer
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/cache.go:363`
- **What:** allHashes accumulates hashes passed to OnRead (blocks already read). toPrefetch = allHashes[len-want:] selects the most-recently-seen hashes — the same blocks just read, not the next blocks. Comment says 'schedule depth upcoming hashes' but logic is inverted. After 3 reads of h0/h1/h2 with depth=1, prefetch fires for h2 (last read), not h3 (next block).
- **Why it matters:** Prefetch never warms truly upcoming blocks. It re-fetches the trailing already-read window, which is either a cache hit (no-op) or redundant re-load of blocks the caller already has. Sequential read performance gain is zero. Prefetch goroutines waste cycles on guaranteed-stale requests.
- **Fix:** OnRead must receive the full ordered hash sequence for the file (or at least a lookahead window beyond the current read position). Separate the 'already-read window' used for sequential detection from a 'future hashes' lookahead slice populated from the file's block manifest. Alternatively, engine.ReadAt should pass the upcoming BlockRef hashes alongside the just-satisfied ones so the tracker can schedule genuinely future blocks.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: cache.go:374 start=len(tr.allHashes)-want then toPrefetch=tr.allHashes[start:] selects last `want` hashes from already-read window. tr.allHashes contains only hashes passed to OnRead (already-read blocks). Prefetch fires for the trailing already-seen blocks, not upcoming ones. Sequential read prefetch provides zero benefit.

### [MED] UmntAll removes ALL clients' mounts instead of just the requesting client's · `slop` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/mount/handlers/umountall.go:51`
- **What:** UmntAll calls h.Registry.RemoveAllMounts() which delegates to mountTracker.RemoveAll() and flushes the entire global mount table — all clients, all shares.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 1813 Appendix I UMNTALL removes mounts for the calling client only. RemoveAll() at runtime.go:616 contains no client filter. Every other client's active mount record is silently wiped when any single client sends UMNTALL, corrupting DUMP output and potentially interfering with mount lifecycle tracking.
- **Fix:** Add a RemoveMountsByClient(clientAddr string) method to the mountRuntime interface and mountTracker, then call it here with extractClientIP(ctx.ClientAddr). RemoveAllMounts() should only be used for server shutdown, not for UMNTALL.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. umountall.go:51 calls `h.Registry.RemoveAllMounts()` → runtime.RemoveAllMounts() → Tracker.RemoveAll() which wipes entire mount table with no client filter (`mt.mounts = make(map[string]*MountInfo)`). RFC 1813 UMNTALL must remove only the calling client's mounts. Any client sending UMNTALL destroys all other clients' mount records. Severity MED not HIGH: mount table is advisory/tracking only; NFS access itself is not gated on it.

### [MED] FreeAll stub — decodes crash client name then discards it; no lock release wired · `slop` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/free_all.go:77`
- **What:** FreeAll decodes req.Name (the crashing client's hostname) and immediately returns without releasing any locks or invoking any crash-cleanup path. The Handler struct (handler.go:44) has fields nlmService and blockingQueue only — no crash callback reference. The comment at line 88 claims 'actual lock release is triggered by the adapter's OnClientCrash callback' but there is no such wiring: OnClientCrashFunc lives on nsm.Notifier (notifier.go:61), a separate type with no link to NLM Handler.
- **Why it matters:** When rpc.statd detects a client crash and sends NLM_FREE_ALL, the server must release all locks held by that client. This handler is a log-only stub: crash-recovery via FREE_ALL is entirely non-functional. Stale NLM locks persist indefinitely after a client crash, blocking any future lock attempt on those files by other clients.
- **Fix:** Add a CrashCleanupFunc field to Handler (or extend NLMLockService with ReleaseClientLocks(ctx, callerName)). In FreeAll, after decoding req.Name, call h.nlmService.ReleaseClientLocks(ctx.Context, req.Name) and h.blockingQueue.RemoveClientWaiters(req.Name) (the queue method already exists at queue.go:174).
- **Verified:** Confirmed stub. free_all.go:FreeAll() logs and returns — no lock release. Comment claims `adapter OnClientCrash` handles it but that path is wired to the NSM notifier (nsm/notifier.go:OnClientCrash via nlm.go:473) for SM_NOTIFY, not NLM_FREE_ALL. The NLM FREE_ALL RPC itself never triggers lock cleanup. However NSM SM_NOTIFY path IS wired and functional, so crash recovery is partially available via rpc.statd's SM_NOTIFY. Severity MED: lock cleanup exists via alternate path, but FREE_ALL specifically is a no-op.

### [MED] adapter.Adapter interface SetRuntime signature mismatch — interface unusable · `slop` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/adapter.go:60`
- **What:** Adapter interface declares SetRuntime(rt *runtime.Runtime) but every concrete implementation — BaseAdapter (base.go:179), NFSAdapter (nfs/adapter.go:376), smb.Adapter (smb/adapter.go:160) — declares SetRuntime(rt any). The signatures are incompatible in Go: a method with parameter type any does not satisfy an interface method with parameter type *runtime.Runtime. No compile-time assertion (var _ adapter.Adapter = ...) exists anywhere, so the mismatch is invisible. Any code that stores a concrete adapter in an adapter.Adapter variable and then calls SetRuntime would fail to compile or would require a type assertion that bypasses the interface.
- **Why it matters:** Broken interface contract. The service layer routes around this via its own RuntimeSetter interface (adapters/service.go:36-38) that takes any, meaning the intended interface method is completely dead. Callers who type-assert to adapter.Adapter (as suggested in service.go comments at line 25-26) and call SetRuntime would get a compile error, which indicates the interface definition was copied from the pre-refactor signature without updating it to match the any-based design needed to break the import cycle.
- **Fix:** Change adapter.Adapter.SetRuntime to SetRuntime(rt any) to match all concrete implementations, or remove it from the public interface entirely since the service layer dispatches via RuntimeSetter. Add compile-time assertions: var _ adapter.Adapter = (*nfs.NFSAdapter)(nil) and var _ adapter.Adapter = (*smb.Adapter)(nil) in their respective packages.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. adapter.Adapter interface (pkg/adapter/adapter.go:60) declares `SetRuntime(rt *runtime.Runtime)` but all concrete impls (base.go:179, nfs/adapter.go:376, smb/adapter.go:160) declare `SetRuntime(rt any)`. Method signatures incompatible in Go — concrete types do NOT satisfy the adapter.Adapter interface's SetRuntime method. No compile-time assertion anywhere. Service layer routes around via adapters.RuntimeSetter (takes `any`) making the adapter.Adapter.SetRuntime method entirely dead. Severity MED not HIGH: no callers actually use adapter.Adapter.SetRuntime (service uses RuntimeSetter), so no runtime crash — just a broken/dead interface contract.

### [MED] provisionOperatorAccount ignores PasswordSecretRef.Key — hardcodes "password" key · `slop` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/auth_reconciler.go:215`
- **What:** When user sets spec.identity.admin.passwordSecretRef, both provisionOperatorAccount (line 203-215) and cleanupOperatorServiceAccount (line 366-383) capture ref.Name but discard ref.Key. adminPassword is always read as adminSecret.Data["password"] regardless of what key the user specified in PasswordSecretRef.Key. When user's Secret stores the password under any key other than "password", the read returns empty string and admin login silently fails with wrong credentials.
- **Why it matters:** Fabricated/no-op use of a struct field: ref is assigned at line 203 (provisionOperatorAccount) and line 366 (cleanupOperatorServiceAccount) but only ref.Name is used; ref.Key — the whole point of SecretKeySelector — is never read. Same dead-pattern at cleanupOperatorServiceAccount line 383. The auto-generated credentials Secret happens to use key "password" so the default path works, masking the bug on user-provided paths.
- **Fix:** Use ref.Key when reading the user-provided secret: adminPassword := string(adminSecret.Data[ref.Key]). Also fix the same pattern at cleanupOperatorServiceAccount line 383. Guard against empty Key with a fallback to "password" only for the auto-generated secret path.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. auth_reconciler.go:203-215: `ref := ds.Spec.Identity.Admin.PasswordSecretRef` captures ref.Name but adminPassword is always `adminSecret.Data["password"]` — ref.Key is never consulted. User-provided Secret with password under any key other than `"password"` silently reads empty string → login fails. Same pattern in cleanupOperatorServiceAccount:366-383. Severity MED: affects only users who specify non-default key in PasswordSecretRef.Key; default path (key=password) works.

### [MED] NT hash prefix logged in plaintext to debug log on auth failure · `slop` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/session_setup.go:1134`
- **What:** `logger.Debug(... "ntHashPrefix", fmt.Sprintf("%x", ntHash[:4]) ...)` emits 4 bytes of the server-side NT hash in hex to the debug log on every NTLMv2 validation failure.
- **Why it matters:** NT hash is equivalent to a password. Even 4 bytes of it in logs gives an attacker significant oracle information when combined with brute-force. Debug logs are often captured at higher levels in production (log aggregators, crash reports). This is an AI-slop addition — no legitimate diagnostic purpose requires exposing any fraction of a credential hash.
- **Fix:** Remove the `ntHashPrefix` field entirely from the `logger.Debug` call. The username, domain variants tried, and error are sufficient for diagnosis.
- **Verified:** session_setup.go:1086 confirmed: ntHash comes from user.GetNTHash() — stored server-side NT hash. Line 1134 logs ntHash[:4] in hex at Debug level on every auth failure. NT hash is password-equivalent; even 4 bytes provide oracle information for brute-force attacks. No legitimate diagnostic purpose for exposing credential hash bytes.

### [MED] SET_INFO FileBasicInformation clears modeDOSSparse when recomputing mode · `slop` · area: smb-io-query-ioctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/handlers/set_info.go:333`
- **What:** When fileAttrs != 0, SET_INFO FileBasicInformation calls SMBModeFromAttrs then preserves modeDOSCompressed from the current metadata (line 333: `mode |= curFile.Mode & modeDOSCompressed`). modeDOSSparse (0x200000) is not preserved. Any SET_INFO FileBasicInformation with a non-zero FileAttributes field after FSCTL_SET_SPARSE will silently clear the sparse bit.
- **Why it matters:** FSCTL_SET_SPARSE persists the sparse attribute in modeDOSSparse so subsequent QUERY_INFO reflects FILE_ATTRIBUTE_SPARSE_FILE (ioctl_sparse.go handleSetSparse). A follow-up SET_INFO BasicInfo (e.g. setting ARCHIVE or READONLY) resets the mode via SMBModeFromAttrs which has no knowledge of the FSCTL-managed sparse bit, just as FILE_ATTRIBUTE_COMPRESSED is FSCTL-managed and was already protected. The smbtorture sparse_file_flag test chain exercises both FSCTL_SET_SPARSE and subsequent attribute queries; a client mixing attribute sets with sparse operations will observe the flag disappear.
- **Fix:** On line 333, preserve modeDOSSparse alongside modeDOSCompressed: change `mode |= curFile.Mode & modeDOSCompressed` to `mode |= curFile.Mode & (modeDOSCompressed | modeDOSSparse)`. Add a comment mirroring the existing modeDOSCompressed rationale: 'modeDOSSparse is FSCTL-managed (FSCTL_SET_SPARSE); preserve it so SET_INFO does not accidentally clear sparse state.'
- **Verified:** set_info.go:329-334 confirmed: when fileAttrs!=0, mode = SMBModeFromAttrs(fileAttrs) then only modeDOSCompressed is OR'd back from curFile.Mode. modeDOSSparse (0x200000) defined in converters.go:66 and used in ioctl_sparse.go is not preserved. Any SET_INFO FileBasicInformation with non-zero attrs after FSCTL_SET_SPARSE silently clears the sparse bit.

### [MED] acquireLock LOCK4denied Owner.OwnerData contains raw format string instead of decoded bytes · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-state-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/manager.go:1999`
- **What:** In acquireLock, when a conflicting lock is found via IsUnifiedLockConflicting, the LOCK4denied response is built with Owner.ClientID=0 and Owner.OwnerData=[]byte(el.Owner.OwnerID) where el.Owner.OwnerID is the formatted string 'nfs4:{clientid}:{owner_hex}'. The comment says 'Parse OwnerID to extract clientID and ownerData' but does not actually parse. The TestLock function (line 2089) correctly calls parseConflictOwner for the same case.
- **Why it matters:** Clients receive a malformed lock_owner4 in LOCK4denied: the 'owner' field contains the ASCII format string bytes instead of the opaque owner identifier, and ClientID is always 0. RFC 7530 Section 16.10.4 requires the owner of the conflicting lock in LOCK4denied. Linux nfs client uses this to display lock owner info; malformed data is a protocol violation causing incorrect diagnostics. Plausible-but-wrong logic: the fix exists in parseConflictOwner but was not called here.
- **Fix:** Replace lines 1997–2000 with a call to parseConflictOwner: `parseConflictOwner(el.Owner.OwnerID, denied)`. This is exactly what TestLock does at line 2089 for the same Owner.OwnerID format.

RFC 7530 §16.10.4 violation — malformed lock_owner4 in LOCK4denied.

### [MED] READDIR cookieverf mismatch silently ignored instead of NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/readdir.go:140`
- **What:** When cookie != 0 and cookieVerf mismatches the current directory verifier, the code logs at Debug and continues serving entries with current cookies. NFSv4 RFC 7530 §16.24.4 requires the server to return NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE in this case (the directory changed between READDIR pages — cookies from the old listing are stale/invalid). The comment says 'matches NFSv3 behavior' but NFSv4 behavior is explicitly stronger than NFSv3 on this point.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong logic copied from NFSv3 semantics. Clients relying on NFSv4 cookie-verifier contract to detect mid-scan directory modifications will silently receive incorrect/duplicated/skipped entries instead of a clean error+retry signal. Linux nfs client with vers=4 can end up with phantom or missing entries in large directories.
- **Fix:** Replace the debug-and-continue block with: `return &types.CompoundResult{Status: types.NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE, OpCode: types.OP_READDIR, Data: encodeStatusOnly(types.NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE)}`. The client will restart the READDIR from cookie=0 with the updated verifier.
- **Verified:** readdir.go:140-146 confirmed: when cookie!=0 and incomingVerf!=0 and mismatch, code only logs at Debug and continues serving entries. No NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE returned. Comment explicitly says 'matches NFSv3 behavior' but RFC 7530 §16.24.4 requires NFS4ERR_BAD_COOKIE for NFSv4. Clients will silently get stale/incorrect entries instead of a clean retry signal.

### [MED] Fabricated test assertion masks CB_SEQUENCE seqid double-increment bug · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-delegation-callback
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/state/backchannel_test.go:389`
- **What:** `TestBackchannelSender_SequenceIDIncrement` asserts only `seqID2 > seqID1` (line 392), not `seqID2 == seqID1 + 1`. The actual buggy implementation (seqids 1, 3, 5…) satisfies `>` so the test passes green while the RFC violation goes undetected. The test name and comment imply it verifies increment-by-one semantics, but the assertion is deliberately weakened to only check monotonicity.
- **Why it matters:** AI-slop pattern: test asserts a looser property than the protocol requires, appears to be exercising the constraint, but provides no protection against the real bug. A correct test would fail immediately if the fix in the prior finding is absent.
- **Fix:** Change the final assertion block to: `if seqID2 != seqID1+1 { t.Errorf("seqID must increment by exactly 1: got seqID1=%d seqID2=%d", seqID1, seqID2) }` and remove the now-redundant `seqID1 == seqID2` check.
- **Verified:** backchannel.go:270,284 confirmed: seqID=bs.nextXID.Add(1) then xid=bs.nextXID.Add(1) — two increments per sendCallback call, so seqID increments by 2 each call (1,3,5...). Test at backchannel_test.go:389-393 only asserts seqID2!=seqID1 and seqID2>seqID1, both satisfied by skip-by-2 behavior. RFC requires increment-by-1; weaker assertion masks the bug.

### [MED] privacy.go comments claim KeyUsageAcceptorSeal=26 but constant is 22 · `slop` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr

### [MED] populateBlockCounts misclassifies all CAS-path pending blocks as Dirty · `slop` · area: block-engine-core
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/stats.go:136`
- **What:** Check `b.LocalPath != "" || b.BlockStoreKey != ""` inside `BlockStatePending` case always false for post-Phase-17 CAS blocks. ObjectIDPersister (engine.go:223-228) and ChunkEmitter (engine.go:344-349) create FileBlock rows with State=Pending, LocalPath="", BlockStoreKey="". So every live CAS-path block hits `BlocksDirty++` instead of `BlocksLocal++`. `BlocksLocal` stays 0 in normal operation; `BlocksDirty` is inflated to include all locally-present-but-not-yet-mirrored blocks.
- **Why it matters:** Post-Phase-17 CAS surface tracks local presence via the CAS chunk store (local.Has(hash)), not via FileBlock.LocalPath. The pre-Phase-17 lifecycle set LocalPath on pending blocks; the new lifecycle omits it. The stats code was not updated: comment even says 'Pending now covers both legacy Dirty (no LocalPath/no key) and Local (complete, awaiting sync)' but the discriminator still uses the old fields. Plausible-but-wrong logic after rewrite.
- **Fix:** Replace `b.LocalPath != "" || b.BlockStoreKey != ""` with `!b.Hash.IsZero()`: a CAS-pending block whose hash is populated is locally present in the CAS chunk store. Alternatively use `b.IsDirty()` for dirty (hash zero) vs local (hash non-zero, pending). Keep the `BlockStateSyncing` → BlocksLocal and `BlockStateRemote` → BlocksRemote branches unchanged.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: stats.go:136 checks b.LocalPath != "" || b.BlockStoreKey != "". engine.go:223-228 (ObjectIDPersister) and :344-350 (ChunkEmitter) both create FileBlock{State:BlockStatePending} with no LocalPath or BlockStoreKey, so all CAS-path pending blocks fall to BlocksDirty++ instead of BlocksLocal++.

### [MED] TestCache_SequentialDetection_CACHE03 assertion does not verify prefetched hash identity · `slop` · area: block-engine-gc-syncer
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/cache.go:214`
- **What:** Test comment (line 206) says 'should trigger prefetch of h3 (depth=1)' but assertion is only loader.waitForCalls(1, ...) — any loader invocation passes, including re-loading h2 (the wrong block). The test passes with the wrong prefetch behavior described in the companion finding above.
- **Why it matters:** Fabricated/insufficient assertion masks the logic bug: test gives a false green signal that prefetch is working correctly when it is prefetching the wrong hash. A reviewer sees a passing test named CACHE03 and concludes prefetch correctness is verified.
- **Fix:** After loader.waitForCalls(1), inspect loader.calls and assert it contains hashN(3) (the next-block hash), not hashN(0)/hashN(1)/hashN(2). Add a parallel negative assertion that the calls slice does NOT contain only already-seen hashes.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: TestCache_SequentialDetection_CACHE03 at cache_test.go:214 calls loader.waitForCalls(1, 500ms) — only checks call count >=1. recordingLoader.calls slice records actual hashes but test never inspects it. Wrong prefetch hash (e.g. re-loading h2 instead of h3) would still pass.

### [MED] Non-atomic floor in releaseLogBytes loses concurrent Add(frameSize) increments · `slop` · area: block-local-fs-appendlog
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/local/fs/appendwrite.go:214`
- **What:** releaseLogBytes does `Add(-n) < 0` then `Store(0)` as two separate atomic ops. Between them, a concurrent AppendWrite's `logBytesTotal.Add(int64(n))` (line 435) can fire — the subsequent `Store(0)` clobbers that increment, permanently losing frameSize bytes from the budget counter.
- **Why it matters:** Budget under-count means the pressure gate (`logBytesTotal.Load() > maxLogBytes`) stays false when it should be true, allowing new writes past the ceiling. Under sustained create/delete churn with many concurrent AppendWrites, repeated racing floors cause cumulative drift, defeating the backpressure mechanism and enabling unbounded log growth until ErrPressureTimeout or OOM. Classic TOCTOU on two separate atomic ops masquerading as a single operation.
- **Fix:** Replace the two-op pattern with a CAS loop:
```go
func (bc *FSStore) releaseLogBytes(n int64) {
    if n <= 0 {
        return
    }
    for {
        old := bc.logBytesTotal.Load()
        next := old - n
        if next < 0 {
            next = 0
        }
        if bc.logBytesTotal.CompareAndSwap(old, next) {
            break
        }
    }
    bc.signalPressure()
}
```
This ensures the floor and the decrement are atomic with respect to concurrent Add calls.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: releaseLogBytes at appendwrite.go:214-215 does Add(-n) then Store(0) as two separate atomic ops. Concurrent AppendWrite's logBytesTotal.Add(int64(n)) at line 435 can fire between them; the Store(0) then clobbers that increment, permanently losing frameSize bytes from the budget counter.

### [MED] reclaimLeaseImpl no-lockStore path creates UnifiedLock but never adds it to lm.unifiedLocks — orphaned stub · `slop` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/reclaim.go:126`
- **What:** When lockStore is nil (lines 115-144), if no existing lease is found in memory, a new reclaimedLock is constructed with an empty FileHandle and returned — but it is never appended to lm.unifiedLocks[handleKey]. The caller receives a non-nil *UnifiedLock suggesting success, but no subsequent call (GetLeaseState, findLeaseByKey, AcknowledgeLeaseBreak, etc.) can locate this lease.
- **Why it matters:** Fabricated stub passing as done: the function returns a lock object that is immediately unreachable by any other manager method. Any code path that reclaims a lease and then attempts to use it (e.g., NFS state manager calling GetLeaseState to verify reclaim state) silently sees 'not found'. The path is documented as 'for testing' but no test exercises the orphaning.
- **Fix:** After constructing reclaimedLock, append it to lm.unifiedLocks[handleKey] (using FileHandle if available, else skip the append and return an explicit error: 'cannot reclaim: no file handle and no lock store'). Alternatively gate the function to always require lockStore and remove the stub path.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: reclaim.go lines 127-144 construct reclaimedLock with empty FileHandle (field not set) and return it without appending to lm.unifiedLocks[handleKey]. In contrast the lockStore path appends at line 101. The returned lock is unreachable by findLeaseByKey, GetLeaseState, AcknowledgeLeaseBreak, etc.

### [MED] memoryTransaction.ListChildren omits EAs clone — EA aliasing with stored view · `slop` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/memory/transaction.go:436`
- **What:** `memoryTransaction.ListChildren` shallow-copies `attr` from `fileData.Attr`, clones `Blocks` and `ACL`, but never clones `EAs`. The store-level `ListChildren` in `files.go:346-347` clones all three. The tx variant diverged by copy-paste.
- **Why it matters:** A caller that mutates the returned `DirEntry.Attr.EAs` map (or an individual value slice) inside a `WithTransaction` closure modifies the stored map in place. Subsequent reads within the same transaction or after commit will see corrupted EA bytes. The Badger and Postgres backends round-trip through JSON and never alias, so this is a memory-only cross-backend divergence.
- **Fix:** Add `attr.EAs = cloneEAs(fileData.Attr.EAs)` after line 437 (after the ACL clone), mirroring `files.go:347` and `buildFileWithNlink` in `store.go:499`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: memoryTransaction.ListChildren at lines 434-438 shallow-copies attr, clones Blocks and ACL, but never calls cloneEAs. files.go:347 (store-level ListChildren) does call cloneEAs. Callers mutating returned EAs inside a transaction modify the stored map in-place.

### [MED] Badger GetFilesystemStatistics counts Size of ALL file types, not just regular files · `slop` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/badger/transaction.go:1143`
- **What:** `GetFilesystemStatistics` accumulates `file.Size` for every key under the `f:` prefix regardless of `file.Type`. `initUsedBytesCounter` (store.go:424) and all `pendingDelta` bookkeeping are guarded by `file.Type == metadata.FileTypeRegular`. The scan at line 1143 has no such guard.
- **Why it matters:** Directories, symlinks, and device nodes all appear under `f:` with a `Size` field (typically 0 or a small value), but any non-zero size on such entries inflates `UsedBytes` in FSSTAT responses. More critically, the `UsedBytes` returned by `GetFilesystemStatistics` is structurally inconsistent with `GetUsedBytes()`, causing FSSTAT to report a different value than the atomic counter — a plausible-but-wrong copy of the full-scan pattern without the regular-files filter.
- **Fix:** Add a type guard: `if file.Type == metadata.FileTypeRegular { usedSize += file.Size }` at line 1143, mirroring the guard in `initUsedBytesCounter` (store.go:427).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: badgerTransaction.GetFilesystemStatistics at line 1143 accumulates usedSize += file.Size for every entry under prefixFile with no file.Type check. initUsedBytesCounter in store.go:430 guards with file.Type == metadata.FileTypeRegular. Structural inconsistency between the two UsedBytes sources.

### [MED] PutFile silently swallows old-size scan error, miscounting usedBytes · `slop` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/transaction.go:297`
- **What:** The pre-update old-size query '_ = tx.tx.QueryRow(ctx, ...).Scan(&oldSizeVal)' discards ALL errors with a blank identifier. The intent is 'not found → oldSize = 0', but the same discard also swallows genuine DB errors (type mismatch, connection drop, serialization failure during a nested tx). On a real scan error oldSizeVal remains Invalid and oldSize stays 0, so pendingDelta accumulates int64(file.Size) - 0 = file.Size instead of the correct delta, permanently over-crediting the atomic usedBytes counter.
- **Why it matters:** The usedBytes counter is the authoritative source for statfs UsedBytes reported to NFS/SMB clients. Systematic over-counting drifts statfs until the store is restarted. Because the scan error is discarded, the bug is invisible — no log entry, no error return. This is the plausible-but-wrong error discard pattern.
- **Fix:** Distinguish ErrNoRows from real errors: 'if err := tx.tx.QueryRow(ctx, query, ...).Scan(&oldSizeVal); err != nil && !errors.Is(err, pgx.ErrNoRows) { return mapPgError(err, "PutFile", "read old size") }'. Keep oldSize = 0 only on ErrNoRows; propagate other errors.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: transaction.go:296 uses _ = tx.tx.QueryRow(...).Scan(&oldSizeVal) discarding all errors. On a genuine DB error oldSizeVal stays zero-valued (Invalid), oldSize stays 0, pendingDelta accumulates full file.Size instead of delta. Invisible — no log, no error return.

### [MED] GetFilesystemStatistics ignores share-scoped handle, aggregates all shares globally · `slop` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/transaction.go:1244`
- **What:** Both the transaction-level GetFilesystemStatistics (transaction.go:1244) and the pool-level counterpart (server.go:146) execute 'SELECT COUNT(*) FROM files' / 'COALESCE(SUM(size), 0) ... FROM files' with no WHERE clause. The handle parameter (which encodes the share) is decoded nowhere and never used. In a multi-share server every share reports aggregated totals for the entire filesystem.
- **Why it matters:** NFS FSSTAT and SMB QueryFSInfo are per-share operations; clients use the returned avail/total to enforce quotas and display disk usage. When two shares exist, each share sees double the real used-bytes and half the correct available space. The service-layer quota path (service_quota_test.go) overrides TotalBytes from the quota table, masking this for quota-capped shares, but UsedFiles and UsedBytes still aggregate cross-share. This is a fabricated implementation that silently returns wrong data.
- **Fix:** Decode the handle to extract share_name, then add 'WHERE share_name = $1' to both COUNT and SUM queries. The tx-path already has access to the pool through tx.store; the store-path already has s.usedBytes (which is global — that counter also needs per-share tracking for a complete fix, but scoping the SQL query is the minimum).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: transaction.go:1244 query is SELECT COALESCE(SUM(size),0), COUNT(*) FROM files with no WHERE clause. server.go:146 similarly SELECT COUNT(*) FROM files with no share filter. handle parameter decoded nowhere. Multi-share servers report cross-share aggregates to every client.

### [MED] LoadSharesFromStore: dead fallback passes UUID as name to GetMetadataStore · `slop` · area: controlplane-runtime-shares
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/init.go:162`
- **What:** When GetMetadataStoreByID fails, the fallback at line 162 calls s.GetMetadataStore(ctx, share.MetadataStoreID), passing the UUID value (share.MetadataStoreID, always a 36-char UUID) as the name parameter. GetMetadataStore searches by the human-readable name column, not by ID. The fallback can never succeed: metadata store names are labels like "default" or "badger-1", not UUIDs. The code path is dead but presents as a legacy-compatibility shim.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong AI-generated logic: the comment says "fall back to name lookup" but the argument passed is still the ID, not a name. If GetMetadataStoreByID ever fails (e.g. after a store config deletion mid-restart, or a DB schema mismatch), every share referencing that store is silently skipped at boot with only a Warn log — the operator sees no actionable error and the server starts with missing shares.
- **Fix:** Remove the dead fallback branch entirely, or if legacy rows genuinely stored a name in MetadataStoreID, pass the correct field: metaStoreCfg, err = s.GetMetadataStore(ctx, share.MetadataStoreName) where MetadataStoreName is the name field. Since models.Share has no separate name field for this, the correct fix is to drop the fallback and let the Warn + continue path handle the failure: if err != nil { logger.Warn(...); continue }
- **Verified:** Confirmed: init.go:162 calls s.GetMetadataStore(ctx, share.MetadataStoreID) where s is a store.Store. store/metadata.go:13 shows GetMetadataStore queries by 'name' column. UUID passed as name never matches a human-readable name like 'default'.

### [MED] encodeUTF16LE truncates supplementary Unicode code points (> U+FFFF) · `slop` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/srvsvc.go:301`
- **What:** encodeUTF16LE converts each rune to uint16 via truncation (uint16(r)). Runes > U+FFFF (e.g. emoji in share names/comments) require surrogate pairs in UTF-16LE but are silently truncated to the low 16 bits, producing invalid UTF-16 and corrupting the NDR wire encoding for any non-BMP character.
- **Why it matters:** Fabricated UTF-16 encoder missing surrogate pair logic — classic AI-slop. The golang.org/x/text/encoding/unicode package or a manual surrogate-pair expansion is needed. Also used in lsarpc.go writeNDRUnicodeString (via the shared encodeUTF16LE import) for domain/user name encoding.
- **Fix:** Replace with a correct surrogate-aware encoder: import golang.org/x/text/encoding/unicode and use unicode.UTF16(unicode.LittleEndian, unicode.IgnoreBOM).NewEncoder(), or manually: if r > 0xFFFF { r -= 0x10000; append uint16(0xD800 + r>>10), uint16(0xDC00 + r&0x3FF) } else { append uint16(r) }.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: srvsvc.go:301 does uint16(r) truncation on every rune. No surrogate pair expansion for codepoints > U+FFFF. Produces invalid UTF-16LE for any non-BMP character.

### [MED] buildShareEnumLevel1Response NDR conformant array MaxCount uses byte-count instead of wchar count · `slop` · area: smb-security-ea-rpc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/rpc/srvsvc.go:213`
- **What:** nameLen = len(share.Name) + 1 is the UTF-8 byte length + 1. Written as NDR MaxCount and ActualCount for a wchar_t conformant array. NDR §14.3.3.4 specifies conformant array bounds in element count (wchar_t = 2 bytes), not byte count. For pure ASCII names len(UTF-8)==len(UTF-16)/2 so values match by accident. For any multi-byte UTF-8 name (accented chars, CJK) len(share.Name) != wchar count → NDR frame is malformed.
- **Why it matters:** Plausible-but-wrong: the code looks correct for ASCII but violates the NDR spec for non-ASCII. The fix would use len([]rune(share.Name))+1 (or the UTF-16 output length / 2 + 1) as the element count.
- **Fix:** Compute nameWcharCount := len([]rune(share.Name)) + 1 (rune count + null terminator in wide chars). Use nameWcharCount for MaxCount/ActualCount fields. Same for commentLen. The actual UTF-16LE bytes appended remain the same.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: srvsvc.go:213 uses len(share.Name)+1 (UTF-8 byte length) as NDR MaxCount/ActualCount for wchar_t conformant array. Breaks for any multi-byte UTF-8 name where byte count differs from rune count.

### [MED] identityMapper interface var — data race between SetIdentityMapper and concurrent GETATTR resolveOwnerString · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-types-attrs-v41
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/attrs/encode.go:122`
- **What:** Plain `var identityMapper identity.IdentityMapper` written by SetIdentityMapper() (line 128) and read by resolveOwnerString() (line 710) from concurrent GETATTR handlers. No mutex or atomic protects the interface value, which is a two-word pointer+type pair; torn reads are possible.
- **Why it matters:** Go interface values are not atomically readable/writable; a concurrent store and load of a plain interface var is a data race detectable by -race and can produce a torn read in practice.
- **Fix:** Protect with a sync/atomic.Pointer[identity.IdentityMapper] or a sync.RWMutex. Simplest: `var identityMapperMu sync.RWMutex; var identityMapper identity.IdentityMapper`; RLock on read, Lock on write — or use `atomic.Pointer`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: encode.go:122 declares plain var identityMapper identity.IdentityMapper. SetIdentityMapper (line 128) and resolveOwnerString (line 710) access it without mutex or atomic. sync/atomic is imported only for fsMaxFileSize/fsMaxReadSize/fsMaxWriteSize — not identityMapper.

### [MED] extractCallbackAddr hardcodes DittoFS server port 12049 for NLM GRANTED callbacks · `slop` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/lock.go:259`
- **What:** extractCallbackAddr strips the client's ephemeral port and replaces it with 12049 (the DittoFS NFS server port). The constructed address is stored in Waiter.CallbackAddr and later dialed by callback.SendGrantedCallback when a blocked lock is granted.
- **Why it matters:** NLM clients listen for GRANTED callbacks on their own local NLM port, which is registered with portmapper and typically different from the server's port. Dialing the client IP:12049 will almost certainly be refused (nothing listening there on the client) causing every blocking lock grant to fail, the lock to be immediately released, and the client to never receive GRANTED — effectively making blocking NLM locks non-functional. The client callback address should come from the portmapper lookup on the client side or from the NLM transport layer, not from a hardcoded server-side constant.
- **Fix:** Remove extractCallbackAddr. Use ctx.ClientAddr (which contains the actual client source address) as the base for the callback but resolve the client's NLM callback port via a portmapper GETPORT call to the client (prog=100021, vers=4, prot=TCP), or expose the callback port from the lock's transport context. At minimum, document this as unimplemented and return NLM4DeniedNoLocks for blocking requests until the callback port is properly resolved.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: lock.go:259 returns net.JoinHostPort(host, "12049") — hardcoded DittoFS server port. NLM GRANTED callbacks must go to the client's registered NLM port, not the server's port.

### [MED] Unguarded type assertion on KMIP ResponsePayload panics on nil/unexpected type · `slop` · area: block-remote-s3-encryption-compression
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/encryption/keyprovider/kmip.go:145`
- **What:** Bare type assertion `item.ResponsePayload.(ttlv.TTLV)` with no comma-ok form. After `ttlv.Unmarshal` into a generic `kmip.ResponseMessage`, `ResponsePayload` is normally `ttlv.TTLV`, but if a server sends a `ResultStatusSuccess` response with a missing/empty payload the field is nil — the assertion panics instead of returning an error.
- **Why it matters:** A panic in key-unwrap path during daemon startup (or mid-operation if provider is re-init) crashes the process. This is exactly the class of bug introduced by AI-generated code that assumes the happy-path type is always present: the success guard on line 140 checks `ResultStatus`, not `ResponsePayload` presence.
- **Fix:** Use comma-ok: `raw, ok := item.ResponsePayload.(ttlv.TTLV); if !ok { return nil, fmt.Errorf("keyprovider: kmip Get payload is not TTLV (got %T)", item.ResponsePayload) }` then pass `raw` to `ttlv.Unmarshal`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: kmip.go:145 bare type assertion item.ResponsePayload.(ttlv.TTLV) with no nil check or comma-ok form. ResultStatus check at line 140 does not guarantee payload is non-nil. Panics if KMIP server returns success with empty payload.

### [MED] pruneEmptyDirs reads only first directory page — silently skips intermediary dirs beyond page boundary · `slop` · area: controlplane-snapshot-gc
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/runtime/trash/service.go:439`
- **What:** pruneEmptyDirs calls svc.ReadDirectory with cookie=0 once and iterates only page.Entries, with no HasMore/NextCookie loop. walkBin immediately above uses a correct pagination loop. If a #recycle directory holds more intermediary directories than fit on one page, the excess are never visited and never removed.
- **Why it matters:** After Empty() purges all recycled roots, leftover empty intermediary directories that spill past the first page are silently skipped. The #recycle tree accumulates orphaned empty dirs across repeated Empty calls. The pattern is copy-paste of walkBin's inner loop body without the surrounding for { ... if !page.HasMore { return nil }; cookie = page.NextCookie } scaffolding — AI-slop incomplete port.
- **Fix:** Wrap the existing body in a pagination loop matching walkBin: `var cookie uint64; for { page, err := svc.ReadDirectory(ctx, dirHandle, cookie, 0); ...; if !page.HasMore { return nil }; cookie = page.NextCookie }`
- **Verified:** Confirmed: pruneEmptyDirs at service.go:439 calls ReadDirectory once with cookie=0 and iterates page.Entries with no HasMore/NextCookie loop. walkBin above (line 143-184) has the correct pagination loop. If #recycle contains more dirs than one page, overflow is silently skipped.

### [MED] Stats handler leaks raw internal error string in HTTP response body · `slop` · area: controlplane-api-rest

- **What:** NotFound(w, err.Error()) passes raw runtime error string directly into the 404 response body

This one diverges: err.Error() from GetBlockStoreStats can contain filesystem paths, share-internal state, or runtime internals. Also wrong status code class — a missing/unknown share is not a 404 from the caller's perspective here; it is a misconfiguration. Copy-paste drift: the log line at line 42 was added but the response sanitization was omitted.
- **Fix:** Replace with a fixed safe message: `NotFound(w, "share not found")` (or `InternalServerError(w, "stats unavailable")` if the error is not strictly a missing-share sentinel). Never interpolate err.Error() into the response body.

### [MED] smb.Adapter.OnReconnect is a no-op stub never called — SMB lease reclaim on reconnect silently absent · `slop` · area: adapter-shells-auth-config
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/smb/adapter.go:575`
- **What:** OnReconnect(ctx, sessionID, clientID) is an exported method that only calls logger.Info and returns — no lease reclaim, no LockStore query. The comment explicitly states 'A full implementation would: 1. Query LockStore … 2. Prepare them for reclaim … 3. Notify client' but none of that code exists. More critically, grep across the entire codebase finds zero callers of this method in production code: it is exported but never invoked.
- **Why it matters:** Stub passing as done. SMB clients that reconnect after server restart silently lose their held leases rather than reclaiming them during the grace window. This is a functional gap in SMB durable/persistent state recovery. The method being unreachable (no callers) means the gap is compounded — even if fixed internally, nothing drives it.
- **Fix:** Either remove the method if no caller exists (dead code) or wire it into the session reconnect path (session.Manager or the durable handle scavenger) and implement the LockStore enumeration described in the comment. At minimum add a //nolint:unused or explicit TODO issue reference so the gap is tracked; do not leave a documented stub as a public method that pretends to be functional.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: adapter.go:575 OnReconnect only calls logger.Info and returns. grep across entire codebase finds zero production callers of .OnReconnect — method is exported but never invoked.

- **Fix:** Change `fmt.Printf("dittofs %s\n", Version)` to `fmt.Printf("dfs %s\n", Version)` or `fmt.Printf("%s %s\n", cmd.Root().Name(), Version)`.
