### [MED] nfsv4_locking_test cross-protocol lock tests accept both outcomes — no hard assertion on actual lock conflict · `slop` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/cross_protocol_lock_test.go:175`
- **What:** XPRO-01 through XPRO-03 and the byte-range tests (testOverlappingByteRangeLockConflict) use `if err != nil { t.Logf(...) } else { t.Logf(...) framework.UnlockFileRange(...) }` branching where BOTH the lock-succeeded and lock-blocked paths are treated as passing. Concretely, testOverlappingByteRangeLockConflict (line 599) says "SMB lock on [0:512] unexpectedly acquired (platform-specific lock namespaces)" and proceeds to just unlock and pass. The server never enforcing cross-protocol lock conflicts would pass this test silently.
- **Why it matters:** These are supposed to be correctness tests for cross-protocol lock enforcement (XPRO-03, byte-range overlap). If the server has a bug where SMB ignores NFS byte-range locks, the test logs a non-fatal message and continues. This is fabricated-passing-assertion slop: the test can never fail even on known-broken behavior.
- **Fix:** For overlapping-range conflict tests, add a hard assert: `assert.ErrorIs(t, err, framework.ErrLockWouldBlock, "overlapping cross-protocol lock must be blocked")`. Document platform-specific exceptions explicitly with `t.Skip` rather than silently branching.
- **Verified:** Confirmed lines 174-183 (XPRO-01), 599-605 (byte-range overlap). Both lock-conflict and lock-success paths only call t.Logf — no t.Errorf/t.Fatalf. Server never enforcing cross-protocol locks passes silently.


## LOW

### [LOW] SMB password prompt abort silently proceeds with empty password · `bugs` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfsctl/commands/share/mount.go:166`
- **What:** `resolveSMBPassword` calls `cmdutil.HandleAbort(err)` on password prompt error and returns `("", nil)`. `HandleAbort` returns `nil` for Ctrl-C aborts. Caller `mountSMB` checks only `err != nil`, so on abort it proceeds to call `mountSMBLinux`/`mountSMBDarwin` with an empty password string instead of stopping.
- **Why it matters:** User presses Ctrl-C at the password prompt expecting cancellation; instead the command continues and attempts an SMB mount with `password=''`, producing a confusing auth-failure mount error rather than a clean abort message.
- **Fix:** After `prompt.Password` returns, check if the returned password is empty AND err is nil (i.e. abort was swallowed): `if err != nil { return "", cmdutil.HandleAbort(err) }` is correct but `HandleAbort` masks the abort as nil. Fix by propagating abort directly: `if err != nil { if prompt.IsAborted(err) { fmt.Println("\nAborted."); return "", fmt.Errorf("aborted") }; return "", err }`. Or restructure to not use HandleAbort in functions that return (string, error).
- **Verified:** Confirmed. cmdutil.HandleAbort returns nil for prompt.IsAborted errors (util.go:295-300). resolveSMBPassword therefore returns ("", nil) on Ctrl-C. mountSMB in mount_unix.go:124-127 checks only err != nil, so proceeds to mountSMBLinux/mountSMBDarwin with empty password string.

### [LOW] Double process.Wait() race in WaitForExit + ForceKill · `bugs` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/helpers/server.go:234`
- **What:** WaitForExit (line 234) and ForceKill (line 261) each spawn a goroutine calling sp.process.Wait() on the same os.Process. Tests that call WaitForExit (or StopGracefully which wraps it) AND register t.Cleanup(sp.ForceKill) — e.g. server_test.go testGracefulShutdownSIGTERM lines 146+157 — have two goroutines racing on the same Wait(). The second Wait() returns ECHILD; on some OS configurations this can also leave a zombie or trigger undefined behaviour in the Go runtime's internal process tracking.
- **Why it matters:** os.Process.Wait() must be called at most once per process. Concurrent calls are a data race. Go's os package documents 'Wait waits for the Process to exit' with no concurrency guarantee. The race is reliably triggered whenever both StopGracefully and ForceKill are called for the same ServerProcess (ForceKill is deferred via t.Cleanup in all signal-shutdown tests).
- **Fix:** Add a sync.Once (or a 'waited' bool guarded by a mutex) inside ServerProcess so the first caller to Wait() wins and subsequent calls return immediately. Alternatively, after StopGracefully succeeds, nil out sp.process so ForceKill's early-return guard fires.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. WaitForExit (line 234) and ForceKill (line 261) each spawn a goroutine calling sp.process.Wait(). server_test.go testGracefulShutdownSIGTERM registers t.Cleanup(sp.ForceKill) at line 146 and then calls sp.WaitForExit (via StopGracefully) at line 157 — two concurrent Wait() calls on the same os.Process.

### [LOW] Shared singleton holds stale *testing.T after first test ends · `bugs` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/framework/containers.go:114`
- **What:** sharedLocalstackHelper and sharedPostgresHelper are package-level globals. NewLocalstackHelper/NewPostgresHelper store the first caller's *testing.T in the struct (field T). Every subsequent test reuses the singleton and therefore its T. After the first test finishes, any call to lh.T.Helper(), lh.T.Fatalf(), lh.T.Logf(), or lh.Cleanup() (line 247: lh.T.Helper()) operates on a completed test's T — this is explicitly forbidden by the testing package and causes panic 'panic: testing: t.Helper called after test finished'.
- **Why it matters:** The testing package panics if Helper/Fatal/Log are called after the test function returns. With -parallel or any test ordering where the initialising test completes before a helper method is called on the singleton, the panic fires. The Cleanup() method at line 247 calls lh.T.Helper() unconditionally, so CleanupSharedContainers() will panic if called from TestMain after the first test has finished.
- **Fix:** Remove the T field from both helpers. Pass *testing.T as a parameter to every method that needs it (createClient, Cleanup, CleanupBucket, ListS3PrefixWithSizes) rather than storing it in the struct. The singleton pattern is fine; the stored T is the problem.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. sharedLocalstackHelper/sharedPostgresHelper are package-level singletons storing the first caller's *testing.T. Subsequent tests reuse the singleton. Cleanup() at containers.go:247 calls lh.T.Helper() on the stale T. If called after first test finishes (e.g. from TestMain via CleanupSharedContainers path that terminates the container, or any test calling lh.Cleanup()), panics per testing package rules.

### [LOW] inlineFetchOrWait sparse-block (fb==nil) path doesn't signal inflight waiters correctly · `bugs` · area: block-engine-core
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/block/engine/fetch.go:306`
- **What:** When `resolveFileBlock` returns `fb==nil` (sparse block), `inlineFetchOrWait` returns `(nil, true, nil)` without setting `completed=true`. The deferred `completeInFlight(key, result, completionErr=nil)` fires and signals all waiting goroutines with `err=nil`. Piggybacked waiters receive `(nil, false, nil)` — `downloaded=false` — and set `needLocalReadAt=true` in `EnsureAvailableAndRead`, triggering an extra local-read attempt that will miss and zero-fill via the slow path.
- **Why it matters:** The direct caller correctly zero-fills because it sees `downloaded=true, data=nil` (line 247-249). But every waiter that piggybacked on this in-flight entry takes the `case <-existing.done` branch (line 276-281), reads `result.err=nil`, and returns `(nil, false, nil)`. `EnsureAvailableAndRead` then sets `needLocalReadAt=true` and returns `(false, nil)` instead of `(true, nil)`. The upper call chain in `ensureAndReadFromLocal` then calls `readLocalByHash` (miss) and zero-fills. The result is correct but requires an extra round-trip per piggybacked waiter on sparse blocks under concurrent read load.
- **Fix:** Set `completed = true` before the `return nil, true, nil` at line 307, then call `m.completeInFlight(key, result, nil)` explicitly (same pattern as the success path at lines 361-362). This signals waiters before returning, and they decode the nil-error / nil-data from `result` to mean 'sparse block, use zero-fill' — although they still see `(nil, false, nil)` on the current waiter-return path, the fix at minimum stops the deferred completeInFlight from racing the explicit one.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: fb==nil path at line 306-308 returns (nil, true, nil) but completed stays false, so deferred completeInFlight fires with err=nil. Waiters receive (nil, false, nil) from line 280, EnsureAvailableAndRead sets needLocalReadAt=true (line 242-244) instead of zero-filling directly. Extra local-read round-trip per waiter on sparse blocks; behavior correct but wasteful.

### [LOW] requestLeaseImplWithMode: mutex unlocked but lm.mu.Unlock() called anyway when grantState==None and no break dispatched (double-unlock via early loop break) · `bugs` · area: metadata-lock-manager
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/lock/leases.go:556`
- **What:** When the loop at line 492 hits the `break` at line 556 ("conflict already satisfied") or line 584 ("already-breaking, suppressed"), it exits without setting `breakDispatched=true` and without releasing `lm.mu`. Control falls to line 648 where `if breakDispatched` is false, so the re-lock is skipped (mutex is already held). `bestGrantableState` is called. If it returns `LeaseStateNone`, the code reaches line 656 `lm.mu.Unlock()` — which is correct (one unlock for the one lock). However, when there are multiple conflicting leases in the slice (e.g., two already-breaking leases with the same target), the `break` at line 584 exits after processing only the FIRST match. The second conflicting lease is never AND-merged into `BreakingToRequired`.
- **Why it matters:** If two distinct lease keys on the same handleKey are both already-breaking and both conflict with the new opener, only the first one has its `BreakingToRequired` tightened via the AND-merge. The second lease retains its prior `BreakingToRequired` which may be too permissive for the new opener's target. The new opener's `bestGrantableState` then incorrectly evaluates against the first lease's tightened target while ignoring the second lease's stale target.
- **Fix:** Replace `break` at line 556 and line 584 with `continue` so all conflicting leases in the slice are processed. The `break` was likely intended to exit after the first fresh-dispatch (line 640, which correctly uses `break` since `mu` was released), but was accidentally applied to the no-dispatch paths too.
- **Verified:** leases.go:575-584 — when loop hits already-breaking lease, AND-merges BreakingToRequired then breaks. Second conflicting already-breaking lease in same handleKey slice never has its BreakingToRequired tightened. Double-unlock claim in description is wrong (no double-unlock occurs). bestGrantableState sees all locks including the unmodified second one, so grantability is still computed conservatively. Real but mild: BreakingToRequired of second lease remains too permissive while first is correctly tightened.

### [LOW] badger transaction GetFilesystemStatistics counts all file types in usedSize instead of regular files only · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-memory-badger
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/badger/transaction.go:1141`
- **What:** GetFilesystemStatistics (lines 1118-1178) increments usedSize += file.Size for every f: entry without filtering on file.Type == metadata.FileTypeRegular. The atomic usedBytes counter (maintained in PutFile/DeleteFile) only counts regular files.
- **Why it matters:** FSSTAT AvailableBytes diverges from the atomic counter path: the iterator path includes directories/symlinks/devices while the atomic path does not. Directories have Size=0 today but the divergence is a latent correctness gap and symlinks may have non-zero Size in some backends. Also introduces O(n) scan per stats call inside a write transaction, which blocks other writers.
- **Fix:** Add if file.Type != metadata.FileTypeRegular { continue } before fileCount++ and usedSize += file.Size at line 1141. Better: use s.usedBytes.Load() from the atomic counter (same value without a scan) and compute fileCount-only from the iterator.
- **Verified:** badger/transaction.go:1129-1149 GetFilesystemStatistics iterates all f: prefix entries accumulating file.Size without filtering file.Type==FileTypeRegular. initUsedBytesCounter (store.go:430) and PutFile (transaction.go:180) filter to regular files only. Divergence confirmed. Practical impact limited today since dirs have Size=0, but latent correctness gap for symlinks/other types with non-zero Size.

### [LOW] poolRow connection leak when Scan is never called · `bugs` · area: metadata-store-postgres
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/store/postgres/pool_helpers.go:174`
- **What:** queryRow acquires a pgxpool.Conn and wraps it in poolRow. poolRow.Scan() is the ONLY place conn.Release() is called. Unlike pgxpool's native QueryRow (which releases on rows.Close() via pgx internals), this custom wrapper has no fallback release. If any caller receives the poolRow and returns without calling Scan — for example if a pre-Scan nil-check fires, or if a future refactor introduces an early return — the connection is permanently leaked until the pool times it out. Currently every call site does call Scan, but there is no structural guarantee (no finalizer, no defer).
- **Why it matters:** A single leaked connection under the 10-connection default pool blocks all subsequent pool acquisitions after 10 leaks, hanging the server.
- **Fix:** Add a sync.Once-guarded release in poolRow so the connection is released on the first of {Scan call, explicit Close call}. Expose a Close() method on poolRow and defer it at call sites: `row := s.queryRow(...); defer row.Close(); err := row.Scan(...)`. Or replace the custom wrapper with pgxpool's native QueryRow which handles this correctly.
- **Verified:** pool_helpers.go:174 poolRow.Scan() is the only release site for conn. No defer fallback. Any caller that returns before calling Scan (future refactor, nil-guard, etc.) permanently leaks the connection. Currently all call sites invoke Scan, so not a live leak, but structural guarantee absent.

### [LOW] migrate_to_cas walkDir infinite loop risk on deeply-nested or cyclic metadata · `bugs` · area: cli-cmd-dfs-dfsctl
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/cmd/dfs/commands/migrate_to_cas.go:295`
- **What:** `walkDir` recurses without tracking visited directory handles. If the metadata store contains a cycle (corrupt or hand-crafted data where a child directory's handle equals an ancestor), the function recurses indefinitely until stack overflow. The metadata store contract doesn't guarantee cycle-freedom for corrupted data.
- **Why it matters:** Migration is an offline recovery tool run against potentially-corrupted stores. A stack overflow kills the migration process leaving the journal in an unknown state. The data is user-owned legacy content that may have been written by a buggy version.
- **Fix:** Maintain a `map[string]struct{}` of visited handles (using handle bytes as key) and return an error on re-visit: `if _, seen := visited[string(dirHandle)]; seen { return fmt.Errorf("cycle detected at handle %x", dirHandle) }`.
- **Verified:** Confirmed structurally: walkDir at line 295 recurses without visited-set. Go stack overflow on cycle. However severity is LOW — badger is a real store backed by a filesystem; cycles require corrupt data and this is an offline migration tool. Context cancellation (line 298) helps for other stuck cases but not for cycles. Real bug, reduced severity.

### [LOW] Mount temp directory leaked when raw umount used without Cleanup() · `bugs` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/nfsv41_disconnect_test.go:56`
- **What:** The cleanup registered at line 56 runs only `exec.Command("umount", "-f", mount.Path).Run()` and discards its return value. It does not call `os.RemoveAll(mount.Path)` nor `mount.Cleanup()`. The TempDir created by MountNFSWithVersion (via os.MkdirTemp) is therefore never removed. On repeated test runs this leaves stale directories in /tmp.
- **Why it matters:** Mount.Cleanup() calls both Unmount() and os.RemoveAll(). By bypassing it with a raw umount the directory removal step is skipped. This causes /tmp accumulation across test runs and can confuse CleanupStaleMounts() which glob-matches these patterns.
- **Fix:** Replace the inline cleanup with `t.Cleanup(mount.Cleanup)` (same pattern used by every other test in the file). If force-unmount is specifically needed, override the unmount inside a Cleanup func that still calls os.RemoveAll(mount.Path) afterwards.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. nfsv41_disconnect_test.go:56: cleanup func calls only exec.Command("umount", "-f", mount.Path).Run() with error discarded. No os.RemoveAll(mount.Path), no mount.Cleanup(). TempDir from os.MkdirTemp is never removed. /tmp accumulation across test runs.

### [LOW] ReleaseSessionLeases primary-session re-election scans already-removed sessionMap entries · `bugs` · area: smb-lease-oplock-notify
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/lease/manager.go:517`
- **What:** Phase 1 (lines 465-480) collects keys to release under `RLock`. Phase 1.5 (lines 483-491) calls `ReleaseLease` for each key, which calls `removeLeaseMapping` — removing the session's keys from `lm.sessionMap` under `Lock`. Phase 2 (lines 504-531) then acquires `Lock` and scans `lm.leaseClientGUID` for surviving candidates, reading `lm.sessionMap[clk.KeyHex]` to get `candidateSID`. The guard `candidateSID == sessionID` (line 518) is now dead: the released session's keys were already removed from `sessionMap` by phase 1.5, so `ok` is always false for them. If a concurrent goroutine calls `RequestLease` for the same `clientID/leaseKey` with a new session between phases 1.5 and 2, that new session's `sessionMap` entry could appear as a candidate — potentially electing a session that belongs to a different reconnect of the same client as 'primary' ahead of an older surviving session.
- **Why it matters:** In steady-state this is harmless (the check correctly excludes absent entries via `!ok`). Under a tight race — concurrent durable reconnect of the same ClientGUID arriving between the unlock of phase 1.5 and the lock of phase 2 — the newly-registered session for the reconnect can be elected primary even though an older surviving session of the same GUID exists and should be preferred. Break notifications then route to the reconnect session instead of the oldest surviving session, violating the `client->connections` head semantics. Low probability in practice.
- **Fix:** Snapshot the set of released keys before phase 1.5 (already have it in `keysToRelease`), then in phase 2 explicitly skip any `clk.KeyHex` that appears in the released-key set rather than relying on the `sessionMap` absence check. Alternatively, hold `lm.mu.Lock()` across both phase 1.5 (ReleaseLease body) and phase 2, but that requires splitting ReleaseLease into a locked variant.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: phase 1.5 (line 484) calls ReleaseLease which removes session's keys from sessionMap. Phase 2 (line 517) reads sessionMap for those same keys — `ok` is always false for released session's entries. The guard `candidateSID == sessionID` at line 518 is dead for those. Race window exists between phase 1.5 unlock and phase 2 lock for reconnecting sessions.

### [LOW] serverBootTime initialized at package init, not at server start — write verifier may be stale · `bugs` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/verf.go:11`
- **What:** `serverBootTime = uint64(time.Now().Unix())` runs at package initialization. If the binary is imported (e.g. in tests or as a library) and later restarted without reloading the package, the verifier does not change. More practically: if the Go runtime loads the package seconds before the NFS listener actually opens, the verifier does not reflect the true server-start time.
- **Why it matters:** RFC 1813 §3.3.21 requires the write verifier to change on any server restart so clients can detect lost unstable writes. A stale verifier causes clients to believe their UNSTABLE writes survived a restart when they did not.
- **Fix:** Initialize `serverBootTime` when the Handler is constructed or when the NFS adapter starts listening, not at package init time. Expose a `SetBootTime(t uint64)` function or pass it as a Handler field set in the adapter's `Start()` method.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: `var serverBootTime = uint64(time.Now().Unix())` at package init (line 11). Fires at binary load, not at NFS listener start. If package is loaded seconds before listener opens, verifier is stale relative to actual server-start time.

### [LOW] lookupLockErrorRow: missing engine.ErrStoreClosed sentinel — lock ops on closed store return generic fault instead of stale-handle · `bugs` · area: internal-adapter-common
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/common/lock_errmap.go:91`
- **What:** lookupLockErrorRow does not have the engine.ErrStoreClosed early-exit that lookupErrorRow has (errmap.go:267-269). A LOCK/UNLOCK operation that hits a closed store (share removed mid-op) falls through to defaultCodes: NFS3ErrIO / NFS4ERR_SERVERFAULT / StatusInternalError instead of the stale-handle row (NFS3ErrStale / NFS4ERR_STALE / StatusFileClosed).
- **Why it matters:** Clients receiving SERVERFAULT on a lock op retry indefinitely with backoff. Clients receiving STALE immediately re-mount/reopen. The asymmetry between the general and lock-context translators causes protocol-level confusion for the edge case of share hot-removal during an active lock operation.
- **Fix:** Add the same sentinel check at the top of lookupLockErrorRow: `if goerrors.Is(err, engine.ErrStoreClosed) { return errorMap[merrs.ErrStaleHandle] }` before the goerrors.As call, mirroring lookupErrorRow lines 267-269.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: lookupLockErrorRow (lock_errmap.go:91) has no engine.ErrStoreClosed early-exit. lookupErrorRow (errmap.go:267) does. Lock ops on closed store fall through to defaultCodes (SERVERFAULT/NFS3ErrIO) instead of stale-handle row. Fix: add goerrors.Is(err, engine.ErrStoreClosed) guard at top of lookupLockErrorRow.

### [LOW] extractNewLogs silently returns empty string if log shrinks · `bugs` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/nfsv4_delegation_test.go:486`
- **What:** extractNewLogs compares len(logAfter) > len(logBefore) and returns empty string if the condition is false. If the log file is truncated between the two reads (e.g. log rotation, server restart that truncates the file), len(logAfter) < len(logBefore) and the function silently returns "". All callers then log 'no replay/session activity detected' as a non-failure warning, masking real test infrastructure failures.
- **Why it matters:** Several tests (TestNFSv41EOSReplayOnReconnect, TestNFSv41SessionEstablishment, delegation tests) use extractNewLogs to detect evidence of server behaviour. A silent empty return causes the test to pass with a warning rather than surfacing the truncation. The condition should at minimum log a warning when logAfter is shorter.
- **Fix:** Add an explicit check: if len(logAfter) < len(logBefore) { t.Logf("WARNING: log file shrank (%d -> %d bytes), possible truncation", ...) }. Return the full logAfter in that case so callers still see whatever content is there.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: extractNewLogs (line 487) returns "" silently when len(logAfter) <= len(logBefore). All callers treat empty return as non-fatal. Log rotation or server restart that truncates the file masks real test infrastructure failures.

### [LOW] Shell injection in KDC AddPrincipal via unquoted password in bash -c · `security` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/framework/kerberos.go:161`
- **What:** AddPrincipal builds a kadmin.local command via fmt.Sprintf with `password` interpolated unquoted into a shell string, then passes the whole string to `bash -c`. Any password containing shell metacharacters (`;`, `$()`, backticks, spaces, `"`) executes arbitrary commands inside the KDC container.
- **Why it matters:** The caller controls `password`; tests pass values like "alice123" today but the API is public and nothing prevents a caller passing `"; arbitrary-cmd #`. Because the exec target is `bash -c cmd` the shell parses the entire interpolated string, not just the kadmin argument.
- **Fix:** Use kadmin.local's stdin (-stdin-password / -pass) or pass the add-princ query as a discrete argv element instead of a single shell string: `container.Exec(ctx, []string{"kadmin.local", "-q", fmt.Sprintf("addprinc -pw %s %s@%s", password, principal, k.realm)})` still goes through bash but the outer quotes are now literal — better still, read the password via stdin: write the password to stdin and use `addprinc +needchange <principal>` or the `-stdin` flag so no shell interpolation is needed.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. kerberos.go:161: cmd := fmt.Sprintf("kadmin.local -q \"addprinc -pw %s %s@%s\"", password, principal, k.realm) — password and principal interpolated unquoted into bash -c string. Shell metacharacters in password (';', '$(...)', backticks) execute arbitrary commands in KDC container. Test/e2e code only, not production path. Fix: pass kadmin args as separate exec argv elements or properly shell-quote both fields.

### [LOW] GSS token mechanism OID not verified — foreign-mechanism tokens silently accepted · `security` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/framework.go:202`
- **What:** extractAPReq() parses the GSS-API initial context token but explicitly skips OID verification: '// Skip the OID bytes (we could verify it's the krb5 OID, but we trust the caller)'. Any 0x60-tagged token with any OID value is accepted; the raw bytes after the token ID are passed to kerbService.Authenticate().
- **Why it matters:** The GSS-API OID identifies the security mechanism (RFC 2743 Section 3.1). Skipping OID verification violates RFC 2743 and RFC 4121. A client presenting a non-krb5 OID (e.g., SPNEGO, NTLM, or a crafted unknown OID) can force the server to attempt Kerberos parsing on arbitrary bytes. While the Kerberos parser will likely reject them, this also opens the door to mechanism-confusion attacks if a second GSS mechanism is ever added, and it makes the security boundary ambiguous.
- **Fix:** After reading oidLen and the OID bytes, compare them against kerbauth.KerberosV5OIDBytes (the 9-byte DER encoding of 1.2.840.113554.1.2.2). Reject with an error if they do not match. Remove the comment about trusting the caller.
- **Verified:** Confirmed OID skip at gss/framework.go:202. However, token ID check at line 216-218 validates `tokenID == kerbauth.GSSTokenIDAPReq` (0x0100), which rejects non-krb5 tokens before Kerberos parsing. OID skip is RFC 2743 violation and mechanism-confusion risk if a second GSS mechanism is added, but current exploitability is constrained by the token ID gate. Severity downgraded to LOW.

### [LOW] Auth cache key collision: share name containing ':' + digits can alias another share+credential tuple · `security` · area: nfs-v3-handlers
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v3/handlers/doc.go:37`
- **What:** authCacheKey builds a string by writing ctx.Share directly then appending ':'-prefixed uint values. No separator distinguishes the end of the share name from the start of the AuthFlavor field. A share named "myshare:0" with AuthFlavor=4294967295, UID=nil, GID=nil produces the same key as share "myshare" with AuthFlavor=0, UID=nil, GID=nil. The cached AuthContext (including ShareReadOnly, Identity with effective UID/GID after squash) from one credential set is returned for a different one.
- **Why it matters:** If an operator has shares whose names contain ':' + digits, a client connecting as one (share, credential) pair can receive a cached AuthContext built for a different credential set — potentially one with ShareReadOnly=false instead of true, or with a non-squashed identity. Exploitability is constrained by attacker needing to control or predict share names.
- **Fix:** Use a length-prefixed or fixed-width encoding for the share name, e.g. fmt.Sprintf("%d:%s", len(ctx.Share), ctx.Share) as the opening segment, or separate fields with a byte that cannot appear in a share name (e.g. '\x00'). Alternatively use a struct as key and a sync.Map[authCacheKeyStruct, *metadata.AuthContext] with a properly typed struct key.
- **Verified:** Confirmed structurally. authCacheKey writes share name raw then appendUint writes ':<n>' for each subsequent field. Share name containing ':digits' can collide with different (share, credential) tuple. e.g. share 's:1:2' + AuthFlavor=3 + nil UID/GID produces same prefix as share 's' + AuthFlavor=1 + UID=2 + GID=3. Exploitability requires attacker-controlled or predictable share names with ':digit' patterns. Real but constrained; severity LOW.

### [LOW] Internal connection error details leaked in 400 response for metadata store Create · `security` · area: controlplane-api-rest
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/controlplane/api/handlers/metadata_stores.go:90`
- **What:** `BadRequest(w, "Failed to create metadata store: "+err.Error())` forwards the raw Go error string from `CreateMetadataStoreFromConfig` to the HTTP response. For postgres connections this includes the target host:port, TLS negotiation details, and driver-level messages. For badger it includes filesystem paths and OS error strings.
- **Why it matters:** Internal topology (private hostnames, IP addresses, port numbers, TLS cert subjects) is disclosed to the calling admin. In a multi-tenant operator deployment this leaks infrastructure details beyond what the calling user should see. Also covered by the SSRF finding above — they compound.
- **Fix:** Log `err` at Error level internally; return only a sanitized message to the caller: `BadRequest(w, "Failed to create metadata store: invalid configuration")`. Callers can inspect server logs for diagnostics.
- **Verified:** Confirmed. metadata_stores.go:90: BadRequest(w, "Failed to create metadata store: "+err.Error()) forwards raw Go error string to HTTP response. For postgres includes host:port, TLS details; for badger includes filesystem paths and OS errors. Admin-only endpoint limits exposure but still leaks internal topology. Severity LOW given admin-only access.

### [LOW] integrity.go package comment swaps InitiatorSign/AcceptorSign numeric values · `security` · area: nfs-rpc-gss-xdr
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/rpc/gss/integrity.go:12`
- **What:** Package-level comment states 'For client->server: KeyUsageInitiatorSign (23)' and 'For server->client: KeyUsageAcceptorSign (25)'. Per RFC 4121 Section 2 and the definitions in types.go, KeyUsageInitiatorSign=25 and KeyUsageAcceptorSign=23 — the parenthetical numeric values are swapped.
- **Why it matters:** Code uses the named constants so the crypto is correct. However the wrong inline numbers will mislead reviewers into thinking the constants are wrong and could cause a genuine swap if anyone replaces a constant reference with a literal. Audit tools and future contributors will be confused.
- **Fix:** Change comment to: 'For client->server: KeyUsageInitiatorSign (25)' and 'For server->client: KeyUsageAcceptorSign (23)'.
- **Verified:** Confirmed swap: types.go defines KeyUsageAcceptorSign=23 and KeyUsageInitiatorSign=25. integrity.go package comment (lines 12-13) states InitiatorSign=(23) and AcceptorSign=(25) — both parenthetical values inverted. Code uses named constants so crypto is correct, but comment misleads reviewers and any literal substitution would break the key usage direction.

### [LOW] pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go sends PROC_UNAVAIL instead of PROG_UNAVAIL for unknown program number · `security` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206`
- **What:** The default branch of the program switch in handleRPCCall (outer NFSConnection dispatch) sends rpc.RPCProcUnavail (accept_stat=3) for an unrecognised program number. RFC 5531 §9 requires PROG_UNAVAIL (accept_stat=1) for this case. The inner consolidated Dispatch function at internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:203 correctly uses RPCProgUnavail.
- **Why it matters:** Sends a protocol-non-conformant error code. Well-behaved NFS clients use the accept_stat to decide how to retry; PROC_UNAVAIL suggests the program exists but the procedure is missing, which may cause incorrect client retry behaviour or confuse debugging tools.
- **Fix:** Change line 206 from rpc.RPCProcUnavail to rpc.RPCProgUnavail to match RFC 5531 and be consistent with the inner dispatch at internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:203.
- **Verified:** pkg/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:206 confirmed: default branch sends RPCProcUnavail for unknown program. internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch.go:203 correctly sends RPCProgUnavail. RFC 5531 requires PROG_UNAVAIL(1) not PROC_UNAVAIL(3) for unrecognised program.

### [LOW] Modular bias in generateRandomSecret JWT key generation · `security` · area: k8s-operator
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/k8s/dittofs-operator/internal/controller/dittoserver_controller.go:712`
- **What:** `result[i] = chars[int(randomBytes[i])%len(chars)]` — randomBytes[i] is uint8 (0-255), len(chars)=62. 256 is not a multiple of 62 (256 mod 62 = 8), so chars[0]-chars[7] are selected with probability 5/256 instead of 4/256. Over 32 bytes the bias is small (~0.4%) but the generated string is used as a JWT HMAC-SHA256 signing secret, not just a password.
- **Why it matters:** Modular reduction of uniform bytes over a non-power-of-2 alphabet introduces non-uniform distribution. Standard fix is rejection sampling. auth_reconciler.go generateRandomPassword correctly uses base64 of raw bytes (no modulo), so the JWT path is inconsistent with the password path.
- **Fix:** Use the same pattern as generateRandomPassword: `base64.URLEncoding.EncodeToString(randomBytes)` for 32+ bytes, or implement rejection sampling: regenerate any byte where value >= 62*(256/62).
- **Verified:** dittoserver_controller.go:712 confirmed: chars len=62, randomBytes[i] is uint8 (0-255), 256%62=8 → first 8 chars slightly over-represented. auth_reconciler.go generateRandomPassword uses base64.URLEncoding (no modulo) — inconsistency confirmed.

### [LOW] SMBAuthenticator silently grants guest when user not found and NtChallengeResponse present · `slop` · area: smb-session-negotiate-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/auth/authenticator.go:202`
- **What:** `handleNTLMAuthenticate`: when `userStore.GetUser` returns not-found (err != nil || user == nil), the code returns `AuthResult{IsGuest: true}` even when the client presented a full NTLMv2 `NtChallengeResponse`. An unknown user silently becomes a guest rather than receiving `STATUS_LOGON_FAILURE`.
- **Why it matters:** The production `session_setup.go` path (line 1256-1260) correctly returns `StatusLogonFailure` for unknown users. This divergence means any code that wires `SMBAuthenticator` instead of the handler path would grant unauthenticated guest access to anyone who presents a valid (but unresolvable) username.
- **Fix:** Return an error (`ErrAuthenticationFailed` or equivalent) when `user == nil || !user.Enabled`, consistent with `session_setup.go:1256`. Only fall through to guest when the token itself is empty/anonymous (which is already handled above).
- **Verified:** Confirmed: authenticator.go:201-206 returns IsGuest:true for unknown/not-found users even when NtChallengeResponse is present. However NewSMBAuthenticator is never called outside test files — not wired to production SMB server path. Bug exists in dead/test-only code. Downgrading severity: not exploitable in current production binary.

### [LOW] TestCLI_List_TableMode: asserts truncated 8-char ID with fragile substring check that always passes regardless of actual truncation · `slop` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/snapshot/snapshot_cli_test.go:309`
- **What:** The seeded ID is "snap-cli-list-1" (16 chars). The test asserts `strings.Contains(res.stdout, "snap-cli")` (line 309) and that the full ID does NOT appear (line 312). But "snap-cli" is a prefix of "snap-cli-list-1"; if the table does NOT truncate (a bug), the full ID appears in stdout AND "snap-cli" still matches, so the first assert still passes. The second assert (`!strings.Contains(stdout, "snap-cli-list-1")`) would catch this, but only if the full ID appears verbatim. If the formatter pads/wraps columns or uses ellipsis, neither assertion fires correctly.
- **Why it matters:** The negative assertion (full ID must NOT appear) is the real gate for truncation correctness. Using a 16-char ID where the 8-char prefix is indistinguishable from the truncated form means the positive assertion adds no signal — it can never distinguish between truncated and non-truncated output. The test is weak: a regression where truncation is removed would still pass the positive check.
- **Fix:** Use an ID like "snap-table-list-very-long-id-001" where the 8-char form ("snap-tab") does not prefix-match the full ID in an obvious way, and assert both presence of "snap-tab" AND absence of "snap-table-list". Or assert exact column widths using a regex.
- **Verified:** Confirmed at lines 309/312. Seeded ID is "snap-cli-list-1" (15 chars). Positive assert checks "snap-cli" which is a prefix of full ID — zero signal. Negative assert at line 312 is the only real gate. If formatter wraps/pads with ellipsis the negative check also passes silently. Weakness is real.

### [LOW] qcow2_fixture: SHA256 pin is a placeholder sentinel — integrity check is permanently bypassed · `slop` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/framework/qcow2_fixture.go:34`
- **What:** qcow2BaseSHA256 = "<freeze-at-first-run>" (a placeholder). When this placeholder is active (as it is in the committed code), DownloadQcow2Base skips the integrity check on both cached and freshly downloaded files (lines 74, 126–129). Any downloaded file — including a corrupted or tampered one — is accepted. The "freeze-at-first-run" design was never completed; the constant was never replaced with a real digest.
- **Why it matters:** The qcow2 fixture is used by TestDEDUP03_VMFleet40Pct to generate the 40% dedup gate. Without a pinned SHA256, a CDN rotation, man-in-the-middle, or network error produces a silently wrong base image, causing the dedup test to pass or fail on bogus data. This is a fabricated safety check that never actually runs.
- **Fix:** Download the image once, compute its SHA256, and replace the placeholder with the real hex digest. Add a CI step that fails if the placeholder is still present.
- **Verified:** Confirmed: `qcow2BaseSHA256 = "<freeze-at-first-run>"` (line 34). Lines 74, 77-80 skip the fatal SHA check when placeholder is active — cached file accepted without integrity verify. Design was never completed.

### [LOW] HandleSMB1Negotiate: SecurityBufferOffset off-by-one (128 vs 129) · `slop` · area: smb-framing-dispatch-compound
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/smb/response.go:1273`
- **What:** SecurityBufferOffset written as 128 with comment '64 (header) + 64 (fixed body)'. Body is `respBody = make([]byte, 65)` (StructureSize=65 per MS-SMB2 §2.2.4), so offset should be 64+65=129 (0x81), not 128 (0x80). Wrong value copied from a plausible-but-incorrect mental model where NEGOTIATE response body is 64 bytes.
- **Why it matters:** Per MS-SMB2 §2.2.4, NEGOTIATE response SecurityBufferOffset must point to the first byte of the security buffer, which immediately follows the 65-byte fixed NEGOTIATE response body. SecurityBufferLength is 0 in this SMB1-upgrade path so no client dereferences the offset today — functionally harmless — but the value is provably wrong and will silently corrupt any future attempt to append a real security buffer to this response path.
- **Fix:** Change `binary.LittleEndian.PutUint16(respBody[56:58], 128)` to `binary.LittleEndian.PutUint16(respBody[56:58], 129)` and fix the comment to '64 (header) + 65 (fixed body) = 129'.
- **Verified:** response.go:1273 confirmed: respBody=make([]byte,65), SecurityBufferOffset written as 128 with comment '64 (header) + 64 (fixed body)'. Should be 64+65=129. Comment and value both wrong.

### [LOW] OPEN CLAIM_DELEGATE_CUR encodes beforeCtime as afterCtime in change_info4 (no post-op lookup) · `slop` · area: nfs-v4-handlers-ops
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/v4/handlers/open.go:681`
- **What:** handleOpenClaimDelegateCur calls encodeOpenResult with (beforeCtime, beforeCtime, nil) — both before and after ctimes are identical. Unlike CLAIM_NULL (line 389 which computes a real afterCtime) and CLAIM_PREVIOUS (which uses 0,0 with a comment), this path never fetches post-op parent attributes, so change_info4.after always equals change_info4.before even when the OPEN causes a state change.
- **Why it matters:** Copy-paste from CLAIM_PREVIOUS zeroed-change_info but without the comment justifying it. For CLAIM_DELEGATE_CUR the current FH is the file (not newly created), so atomic=true with before==after is technically defensible, but omitting the post-op lookup is an inconsistency that could mislead clients doing attribute caching or delegation tracking.
- **Fix:** Either fetch the post-op parent attributes like CLAIM_NULL does and pass the real afterCtime, or pass (0, 0) and add a comment like CLAIM_PREVIOUS explaining the reclaim path intentionally returns zero change_info.
- **Verified:** open.go:681 confirmed: handleOpenClaimDelegateCur calls encodeOpenResult with (beforeCtime, beforeCtime, nil) — no post-op parent lookup, afterCtime==beforeCtime always. CLAIM_NULL path at line 389 computes real afterCtime; CLAIM_PREVIOUS at 463 uses 0,0 with comment justifying it. This path has neither.

### [LOW] handleNFSNull uses NFS3ErrAccess as fallback error status — wrong for NULL procedure · `slop` · area: nfs-dispatch-connection-auth
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/dispatch_nfs.go:157`
- **What:** `handleNFSNull` passes `types.NFS3ErrAccess` (13) as the `errorStatus` argument to `handleRequest`. RFC 1813 §3.3.1: NULL takes no arguments and always returns NFS3_OK. The fallback status is unreachable in practice (`DecodeNullRequest` always succeeds, `handler.Null` always returns NFS3_OK), but the value is semantically wrong and is copy-paste drift from adjacent read/access handlers.
- **Why it matters:** Copy-paste drift: `handleNFSNull` and `handleNFSGetAttr`/`handleNFSLookup`/`handleNFSAccess` all use `NFS3ErrAccess` as their hardcoded fallback. For NULL, GETATTR, SETATTR the correct fallback is `NFS3ErrIO` (I/O failure) or `NFS3ErrServerfault`; `NFS3ErrAccess` implies a permission denial which cannot arise from a decode failure.
- **Fix:** Change `types.NFS3ErrAccess` to `types.NFS3ErrServerfault` (or `types.NFS3ErrIO`) for `handleNFSNull`, `handleNFSGetAttr`, `handleNFSSetAttr`, `handleNFSLookup`, and `handleNFSAccess`. For `handleNFSAccess` specifically `NFS3ErrAccess` is at least plausible but misleading as a decode-failure code.
- **Verified:** handleNFSNull at dispatch_nfs.go:157 passes types.NFS3ErrAccess as errorStatus to handleRequest. RFC 1813 NULL always returns NFS3_OK; NFS3ErrAccess (permission denial) is semantically wrong as a decode-failure fallback. Unreachable in practice but slop confirmed.

### [LOW] NLM NULL response encodes NLM4Res (cookie+status) but spec requires void · `slop` · area: nfs-nlm-nsm-portmap-mount
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/internal/adapter/nfs/nlm/handlers/null.go:29`
- **What:** EncodeNullResponse serializes an NLM4Res struct (4-byte opaque length + cookie bytes + 4-byte status = at least 8 bytes) for the NULL procedure response. Open Group NLM v4 spec says NULL returns void (zero response bytes).
- **Why it matters:** Strict NLM clients (e.g., Linux lockd parsing the reply) expect zero data bytes after the RPC accept header for procedure 0. Extra bytes in the reply body may cause the client's XDR parser to misalign on the next response or log a spurious decode error, though most implementations tolerate trailing bytes for NULL.
- **Fix:** Return []byte{} from EncodeNullResponse (same pattern as EncodeFreeAllResponse / UmountResponse.Encode). Remove the NLM4Res encoding from the NULL path in null.go and in the dispatch wrapper handleNLMNull in dispatch.go.
- **Verified:** EncodeNullResponse in nlm/handlers/null.go serializes an NLM4Res struct (cookie + status) for the NULL procedure. NLM NULL spec requires void (zero response bytes). Extra bytes may misalign XDR parser on strict clients.

A reader relying on the comment to audit correctness will reason about cap semantics that do not apply; the len-based formula is in fact correct for aliased subslices, making this a documentation-only defect that obscures review.

### [LOW] Vacuous nil-check on FileHandle in testDeleteShare · `slop` · area: metadata-storetest-conformance
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/metadata/storetest/store_surface.go:98`
- **What:** createTestShare always fatals via t.Fatalf on any internal error before returning; it never returns a nil FileHandle. The `if root2 := createTestShare(...); root2 == nil` guard and the t.Fatal message are dead code that can never execute.
- **Why it matters:** FileHandle is []byte. createTestShare calls t.Fatalf (runtime.Goexit) on CreateShare/CreateRootDirectory/EncodeFileHandle failure, so the goroutine exits before reaching return rootHandle. The nil-check therefore always evaluates to false, and the t.Fatal('re-CreateShare after DeleteShare returned nil root handle') body is unreachable. The REAL test (that createTestShare does not fatal) is valid, but the assertion text and the nil branch are misleading no-ops: any future reviewer might trust the nil check as meaningful.
- **Fix:** Replace the guard with a plain call that captures the return to satisfy Go's unused-variable rule, or add a comment: root2 := createTestShare(t, store, shareName); _ = root2 // createTestShare fatals internally on error; reaching here means success
- **Verified:** createTestShare (suite.go:154) calls t.Fatalf on every error path and never returns nil. The nil guard at store_surface.go:98 is dead code — the goroutine exits via runtime.Goexit before reaching return. The t.Fatal message is unreachable.

### [LOW] EnsureDefaultAdapters uses != instead of errors.Is for sentinel comparison · `slop` · area: controlplane-store-models
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/pkg/controlplane/store/adapters.go:73`
- **What:** `if err != models.ErrAdapterNotFound` compares error by pointer instead of using `errors.Is`.
- **Why it matters:** Project idiom rule mandates `errors.Is`/`errors.As` for sentinel errors. A wrapped `ErrAdapterNotFound` (e.g. `fmt.Errorf("...: %w", models.ErrAdapterNotFound)`) would bypass this guard and propagate as an unexpected error, causing `EnsureDefaultAdapters` to abort startup instead of continuing.
- **Fix:** Replace `if err != models.ErrAdapterNotFound` with `if !errors.Is(err, models.ErrAdapterNotFound)`.
- **Verified:** adapters.go:73 uses 'err != models.ErrAdapterNotFound' (pointer equality) instead of errors.Is. Sentinel is errors.New so currently returned unwrapped by convertNotFoundError, making this low-risk in practice. Still violates project idiom and would silently break if wrapping is ever added.

### [LOW] TestNFSv4DelegationRecall / TestNFSv41BackchannelDelegationRecall: log-scraping assertions never fail — delegation recall is never confirmed · `slop` · area: e2e-test-framework
- **Where:** `/tmp/dittofs-audit/test/e2e/nfsv4_delegation_test.go:189`
- **What:** Both tests check server logs for "Delegation granted" and "CB_RECALL sent" but treat absence as a non-failure (lines 195–200, 448–464). The critical assertion is data consistency (`assert.Equal`), which passes regardless of whether delegations were ever issued or recalled. The log-scraping delegation-detection path is entirely optional — the test passes whether or not the server ever grants a single delegation.
- **Why it matters:** These are supposed to validate the full delegation lifecycle (grant → recall → data flush). A server that never grants delegations passes all tests. The optional log-scraping is vestigial documentation-as-test, not a correctness gate.
- **Fix:** Either expose a /metrics or /debug endpoint counting delegations_granted and delegations_recalled and assert counts > 0, or accept the current limitation and rename the tests to reflect they only test data consistency, not delegation behavior.
- **Verified:** nfsv4_delegation_test.go lines 189-206 and 440-464 confirmed: log-scraping results for 'Delegation granted'/'CB_RECALL sent' only call t.Log, never t.Error/t.Errorf/t.Fatal. Data consistency assert (assert.Equal on file content) passes regardless of delegation lifecycle. Server can skip delegations entirely and both tests pass. Fix: add t.Errorf if grantFound is false after a client open that should trigger delegation, or skip test if feature is unimplemented.
